　　"Very poorly explained... That is incorrect, the kappa is more commonly found in Mongolia.... Professor Cardozo gave this eight out of ten? I wouldn't have given it three...."
　　When the bell rang at last, Peralta held them back.
　　"You will each write an essay, to be handed in to me, on the ways you recognize and kill werewolves. I want two rolls of parchment or, the subject, and I want them by Monday morning. It is time somebody took this class in hand. Lopez, stay behind, we need to arrange your detention."
　　Roberto and Carolina left the room with the rest of the class, who waited until they were well out of earshot, then burst into a furious tirade about Peralta.
　　"Peralta's never been like this with any of our other Defense Against the Dark Arts teachers, even if he did want the job," Roberto said to Carolina. "Why's he got it in for Cardozo? D'you think this is all because of the boggart?"
　　"I don't know," said Carolina pensively. "But I really hope Professor Cardozo gets better soon...."
　　Diego caught up with them five minutes later, in a towering rage.
　　"D'you know what that --" (he called Peralta something that made Carolina say "Diego!") "-- is making me do? I've got to scrub out the bedpans in the hospital wing. Without magic!" He was breathing deeply, his fists clenched. "Why couldn't Martinez have hidden in Peralta's office, eh? He could have finished him off for us!"
　　Roberto woke extremely early the next morning; so early that it was till dark. For a moment he thought the roaring of the wind had woken him. Then he felt a cold breeze on the back of his neck and sat bolt upright -- Peeves the Poltergeist had been floating next to him, blowing hard in his ear.
　　"What did you do that for?" said Roberto furiously. Peeves puffed out his cheeks, blew hard, and zoomed backward out of the room, cackling.
　　Roberto fumbled for his alarm clock and looked at it. It was half past four. Cursing Peeves, he rolled over and tried to get back to sleep, but it was very difficult, now that he was awake, to ignore the sounds of the thunder rumbling overhead, the pounding of the wind against the castle walls, and the distant creaking of the trees in the Forbidden Forest. In a few hours he would be out on the Quidditch field, battling through that gale. Finally, he gave up any thought of more sleep, got up, dressed, picked up his Nimbus Two Thousand, and walked quietly out of the dormitory.
　　As Roberto opened the door, something brushed against his leg. He bent down just in time to grab Crookshanks by the end of his bushy tail and drag him outside.
　　"You know, I reckon Diego was right about you," Roberto told Crookshanks suspiciously. "There are plenty of mice around this place -- go and chase them. Go on," he added, nudging Crookshanks down the spiral staircase with his foot. "Leave Scabbers alone."
　　The noise of the storm was even louder in the common roorn. Roberto knew better than to think the match would be canceled; Quidditch matches weren't called off for trifles like thunderstorms. Nevertheless, he was starting to feel very apprehensive. Wood had pointed out Nicolas Ortega to him in the corridor; Ortega was a fifth year and a lot bigger than Roberto. Seekers were usually light
　　and speedy, but Ortega's weight would be an advantage in this weather because he was less likely to be blown off course.
　　Roberto whiled away the hours until dawn in front of the fire, getting up every now and then to stop Crookshanks from sneaking up
　　the boys, staircase again. At long last Roberto thought it must be time for breakfast, so he headed through the portrait hole alone.
　　"Stand and fight, you mangy cur!" yelled Sir Cadogan.
　　"Oh, shut up," Roberto yawned.
　　He revived a bit over a large bowl of porridge, and by the time he'd started on toast, the rest of the team had turned up.
　　"It's going to be a tough one," said Wood, who wasn't eating anything.
　　"Stop worrying, Oliver," said Alicia soothingly, "we don't mind a bit of rain."
　　But it was considerably more than a bit of rain. Such was the popularity of Quidditch that the whole school turned out to watch the match as usual, but they ran down the lawns toward the Quidditch field, heads bowed against the ferocious wind, umbrellas being whipped out of their hands as they went. just before he entered the locker room, Roberto saw Sosa, Crabbe, and Goyle, laughing and pointing at him from under an enormous umbrella on their way to the stadium.
　　The team changed into their scarlet robes and waited for Wood's usual pre-match pep talk, but it didn't come. He tried to speak several times, made an odd gulping noise, then shook his head hopelessly and beckoned them to follow him.
　　The wind was so strong that they staggered sideways as they walked out onto the field. If the crowd was cheering, they couldn't hear it over the fresh rolls of thunder. Rain was splattering over Roberto's glasses. How on earth was he going to see the Snitch in this?
　　The Hufflepuffs were approaching from the opposite side of the field, wearing canary-yellow robes. The Captains walked up to eacb other and shook hands; Ortega smiled at Wood but Wood no, looked as though he had lockjaw and merely nodded. Roberto saw Madam Hooch's mouth form the words, "Mount Your brooms.,, He pulled his right foot out of the mud with a squelch and swung it over his Nimbus Two Thousand. Madam Hooch put her whistle to her lips and gave it a blast that sounded shrill and distant they were off
　　Roberto rose fast, but his Nimbus was swerving slightly with the wind. He held it as steady as he could and turned, squinting into the rain.
　　Within five minutes Roberto was soaked to his skin and frozen, hardly able to see his teammates, let alone the tiny Snitch. He flew backward and forward across the field past blurred red and yellow shapes, with no idea of what was happening in the rest of the game. He couldn't hear the commentary over the wind. The crowd was hidden beneath a sea of cloaks and battered umbrellas. Twice Roberto came very close to being unseated by a Bludger; his vision was so clouded by the rain on his glasses he hadn't seen them coming.
　　He lost track of time. It was getting harder and harder to hold his broom straight. The sky was getting darker, as though night had decided to come early. Twice Roberto nearly hit another player, without knowing whether it was a teammate or opponent; everyone was now so wet, and the rain so thick, he could hardly tell them apart....
　　With the first flash of lightning came the sound of Madam Hooch's whistle; Roberto could just see the outline of Wood through the thick rain, gesturing him to the ground. The whole team splashed down into the mud.
　　"I called for time-out!" Wood roared at his team. "Come on, under here --"
　　They huddled at the edge of the field under a large umbrella; Roberto took off his glasses and wiped them hurriedly on his robes.
　　"What's the score?"
　　"We're fifty points up," said Wood, "but unless we get the Snitch soon, we'll be playing into the night."
　　"I've got no chance with these on," Roberto said exasperatedly, waving his glasses.
　　At that very moment, Carolina appeared at his shoulder; she was holding her cloak over her head and was, inexplicably, beaming.
　　"I've had an idea, Roberto! Give me your glasses, quick!"
　　He handed them to her, and as the team watched in amazement, Carolina tapped them with her wand and said, "Impervius!"
　　"There!" she said, handing them back to Roberto. "They'll repel water!"
　　Wood looked as though he could have kissed her.
　　"Brilliant!" he called hoarsely after her as she disappeared into the crowd. "Okay, team, let's go for it!"
　　Carolina's spell had done the trick. Roberto was still numb with cold, still wetter than he'd ever been in his life, but he could see. Full of fresh determination, he urged his broom through the turbulent air, staring in every direction for the Snitch, avoiding a Bludger, ducking beneath Ortega, who was streaking in the opposite direction....
　　There was another clap of thunder, followed immediately by forked lightning. This was getting more and more dangerous. Roberto needed to get the Snitch quickly -
　　He turned, intending to head back toward the middle of the field, but at that moment, another flash of lightning illuminated the stands, and Roberto saw something that distracted him completely , the silhouette of an enormous shaggy black dog, clearly imprinted against the sky, motionless in the topmost, empty row of seats.
　　Roberto's numb hands slipped on the broom handle and his Nimbus dropped a few feet. Shaking his sodden bangs out of his eyes, he squinted back into the stands. The dog had vanished.
　　"Roberto!" came Wood's anguished yell from the Gryffindor goal posts. "Roberto, behind you!"
　　Roberto looked wildly around. Nicolas Ortega was pelting up the field, and a tiny speck of gold was shimmering in the rain-filled air between them -
　　With a jolt of panic, Roberto threw himself flat to the broornhandle and zoomed toward the Snitch.
　　"Come on!" he growled at his Nimbus as the rain whipped his face. 'Taster!"
　　But something odd was happening. An eerie silence was falling across the stadium. The wind, though as strong as ever, was forgetting to roar. It was as though someone had turned off the sound, as though Roberto had gone suddenly deaf -- what was going on?
　　And then a horribly familiar wave of cold swept over him, inside him, just as he became aware of something moving on the field below...
　　Before he'd had time to think, Roberto had taken his eyes off the Snitch and looked down.
　　At least a hundred dementors, their hidden faces pointing up at him, were standing beneath him. It was as though freezing water were rising in his chest, cutting at his insides. And then he heard it again.... Someone was screaming, screaming inside his head... a woman...
　　"Not Roberto, not Roberto, please not Roberto!"
　　"Stand aside, you silly girl... stand aside, now...."
　　"Not Roberto, please no, take me, kill me instead --"
　　Numbing, swirling white mist was filling Roberto's brain.... What was he doing? Why was he flying? He needed to help her... She was going to die.... She was going to be murdered....
　　He was falling, falling through the icy mist.
　　"Not Roberto! Please... have mercy... have mercy....
　　A shrill voice was laughing, the woman was screaming, and Roberto knew no more.
　　"Lucky the ground was so soft."
　　"I thought he was dead for sure."
　　"But he didn't even break his glasses."
　　Roberto could hear the voices whispering, but they made no sense whatsoever. He didn't have a clue where he was, or how he'd got there, or what he'd been doing before he got there. All he knew was that every inch of him was aching as though it had been beaten.
　　"That was the scariest thing I've ever seen in my life."
　　Scariest... the scariest thing... hooded black figures... cold ... screaming...
　　Roberto's eyes snapped open. He was lying in the hospital wing. The Gryffindor Quidditch team, spattered with mud from head to foot, was gathered around his bed. Diego and Carolina were also there, looking as though they'd just climbed out of a swimming pool.
　　"Roberto!" said Pablo, who looked extremely white underneath, the mud. "How're you feeling?"
　　It was as though Roberto's memory was on fast forward. The lightning -- the Grim -- the Snitch -- and the dementors...
　　"What happened?" he said, sitting up so suddenly they all gasped.
　　"You fell off," said Pablo. "Must've been -- what -- fifty feet?"
　　"We thought you'd died," said Alicia, who was shaking.
　　Carolina made a small, squeaky noise. Her eyes were extremely bloodshot.
　　"But the match," said Roberto. "What happened? Are we doing a replay?"
　　No one said anything. The horrible truth sank into Roberto like a stone.
　　"We didn't -- lose?"
　　"Ortega got the Snitch," said Luis. "Just after you fell. He didn't realize what had happened. When he looked back and saw you on the ground, he tried to call it off. Wanted a rematch. But they won fair and square... even Wood admits it."
　　"Where is Wood?" said Roberto, suddenly realizing he wasn't there.
　　"Still in the showers," said Pablo. "We think he's trying to drown himself."
　　Roberto put his face to his knees, his hands gripping his hair. Pablo grabbed his shoulder and shook it roughly.
　　"C'mon, Roberto, you've never missed the Snitch before."
　　"There had to be one time you didn't get it," said Luis.
　　"It's not over yet," said Pablo. "We lost by a hundred points"
　　"Right? So if Hufflepuff loses to Ravenclaw and we beat Ravenclaw and Slytherin --."
　　"Hufflepuff'll have to lose by at least two hundred points," said Luis.
　　"But if they beat Ravenclaw..."
　　"No Way, Ravenclaw is too good. But if Slytherin loses against Hufflepuff..."
　　"It all depends on the points -- a margin of a hundred either way."
　　Roberto lay there, not saying a word. They had lost... for the first time ever, he had lost a Quidditch match.
　　After ten minutes or so, Madam Pomfrey came over to tell the team to leave him in peace.
　　"We'll come and see you later," Pablo told him. "Don't beat yourself up, Roberto, you're still the best Seeker we've ever had."
　　The team trooped out, trailing mud behind them. Madam Pomfrey shut the door behind them, looking disapproving. Diego and Carolina moved nearer to Roberto's bed.
　　"Dominguez was really angry," Carolina said in a quaking voice. "I've never seen him like that before. He ran onto the field as You fell, waved his wand, and you sort of slowed down before you hit the ground. Then he whirled his wand at the dementors. Shot silver stuff at them. They left the stadium right away... He was furious they'd come onto the grounds. We heard him --"
　　"Then he magicked you onto a stretcher," said Diego. "And walked up to school with you floating on it. Everyone thought you were --"
　　His voice faded, but Roberto hardly noticed. He was thinking about what the dementors had done to him... about the screaming voice. He looked up and saw Diego and Carolina lookin, at him so anxiously that he quickly cast around for something matter-of-fact to say.
　　"Did someone get my Nimbus?"
　　Diego and Carolina looked quickly at each other.
　　"Er --"
　　"What?" said Roberto, looking from one to the other.
　　"Well... when you fell off, it got blown away," said Carolina hesitantly.
　　"And?"
　　"And it hit -- it hit -- oh, Roberto -- it hit the Whomping Willow."
　　Roberto's insides lurched. The Whomping Willow was a very violent tree that stood alone in the middle of the grounds.
　　"And?" he said, dreading the answer.
　　"Well, you know the Whomping Willow," said Diego. "It -- it doesn't like being hit."
　　"Professor Flitwick brought it back just before you came around, said Carolina in a very small voice.
　　Slowly, she reached down for a bag at her feet, turned it upside down, and tipped a dozen bits of splintered wood and twig onto the bed, the only remains of Roberto's faithful, finally beaten broomstick.
　　CHAPTER TEN
　　THE MARAUDER'S MAP
　　Madam Pomfrey insisted on keeping Roberto in the hospital wing for the rest of the weekend. He didn't argue or complain, but he wouldn't let her throw away the shattered remnants of his Nimbus Two Thousand. He knew he was being stupid, knew that the Nimbus was beyond repair, but Roberto couldn't help it; he felt as though he'd lost one of his best friends.
　　He had a stream of visitors, all intent on cheering him up. Villalba sent him a bunch of earwiggy flowers that looked like yellow cabbages, and Martina Lopez, blushing furiously, turned up with a get-well card she had made herself, which sang shrilly unless Roberto kept it shut under his bowl of fruit. The Gryffindor team visited again on Sunday morning, this time accompanied by Wood, who told Roberto (in a hollow, dead sort of voice) that he didn't blame
　　him in the slightest. Diego and Carolina left Roberto's bedside only at night- But nothing anyone said or did could make Roberto feel any better, because they knew only half of what was troubling him.
　　He hadn't told anyone about the Grim, not even Diego -and Carolina, because he knew Diego would panic and Carolina would scoff. The fact remained, however, that it had now appeared twice, and both appearances had been followed by near-fatal accidents; the first time, he had nearly been run over by the Knight Bus; the second, fallen fifty feet from his broomstick. Was the Grim going to haunt him until he actually died? Was he going to spend the rest of his life looking over his shoulder for the beast?
　　And then there were the dementors. Roberto felt sick and humiliated every time he thought of them. Everyone said the dementors were horrible, but no one else collapsed every time they went near one. No one else heard echoes in their head of their dying parents.
　　Because Roberto knew who that screaming voice belonged to now. He had heard her words, heard them over and over again during the night hours in the hospital wing while he lay awake, staring at the strips of moonlight on the ceiling. When the dementors approached him, he heard the last moments of his mother's life, her attempts to protect him, Roberto, from Lord Salvador, and Salvador's laughter before he murdered her.... Roberto dozed fitfully, sinking into dreams full of clammy, rotted hands and petrified pleading, jerking awake to dwell again on his mother's voice.
　　It was a relief to return to the noise and bustle of the main school on Monday, where he was forced to think about other things, eve', if he had to endure Javier Sosas taunting. Sosa was almost beside himself with glee at Gryffindor's defeat. He had finally taken off his bandages, and celebrated having the full use of both arms again by doing spirited imitations of Roberto falling off his broom. Sosa spent much of their next Potions class doing dementor imitations across the dungeon; Diego finally cracked and flung a large, slippery crocodile heart at Sosa, which hit him in the face and caused Peralta to take fifty points from Gryffindor.
　　"If Peralta's teaching Defense Against the Dark Arts again, I'm skiving off," said Diego as they headed toward Cardozo's classroom after lunch. "Check who's in there, Carolina."
　　Carolina peered around the classroom door.
　　"It's okay!"
　　Professor Cardozo was back at work. It certainly looked as though he had been ill. His old robes were hanging more loosely on him and there were dark shadows beneath his eyes; nevertheless, he smiled at the class as they took their seats, and they burst at once into an explosion of complaints about Peralta's behavior while Cardozo had been ill.
　　"It's not fair, he was only filling in, why should he give us homework?"
　　"We don't know anything about werewolves two rolls of parchment!"
　　"Did you tell Professor Peralta we haven't covered them yet?" Cardozo asked, frowning slightly.
　　The babble broke out again.
　　"Yes, but he said we were really behind he wouldn't listen --"
　　"-- two rolls of parchment!"
　　Professor Cardozo smiled at the look of indignation on every face.
　　"Don't worry. I'll speak to Professor Peralta. You don't have to do the essay."
　　"Oh no," said Carolina, looking very disappointed. "I've already finished it!"
　　They had a very enjoyable lesson. Professor Cardozo had brought along a glass box containing a hinkypunk, a little one-legged creature who looked as though he were made of wisps of smoke, rather frail and harmless looking.
　　"Lures travelers into bogs," said Professor Cardozo as they took notes. "You notice the lantern dangling from his hand? Hops ahead -people follow the light -- then --"
　　The hinkypunk made a horrible squelching noise against the glass.
　　When the bell rang, everyone gathered up their things and headed for the door, Roberto among them, but --
　　"Wait a moment, Roberto," Cardozo called. "I'd like a word."
　　Roberto doubled back and watched Professor Cardozo covering the hinkypunk's box with a cloth.
　　"I heard about the match," said Cardozo, turning back to his desk and starting to pile books into his briefcase, "and I'm sorry about your broomstick. Is there any chance of fixing it?"
　　"No," said Roberto. "The tree smashed it to bits."
　　Cardozo sighed.
　　"They planted the Whomping Willow the same year that I arrived at Hogwarts. People used to play a game, trying to get near enough to touch the trunk. In the end, a boy called Davey Gudgeon nearly lost an eye, and we were forbidden to go near it. No broomstick would have a chance."
　　"Did you hear about the dementors too?" said Roberto with difficulty.
　　Cardozo looked at him quickly.
　　"Yes, I did. I don't think any of us have seen Professor Dominguez that angry. They have been growing restless for some time -- furious at his refusal to let them inside the grounds.... I suppose they were the reason you fell?"
　　"Yes," said Roberto. He hesitated, and then the question he had to ask burst from him before he could stop himself." Why? Why do they affect me like that? Am I just --?"
　　"It has nothing to do with weakness," said Professor Cardozo sharply, as though he had read Roberto's mind. "The dementors affect you worse than the others because there are horrors in your past that the others don't have."
　　A ray of wintery sunlight fell across the classroom, illuminating Cardozo's gray hairs and the lines on his young face.
　　"Dementors are among the foulest creatures that walk this earth. They infest the darkest, filthiest places, they glory in decay and despair, they drain peace, hope, and happiness out of the air around them. Even Muggles feel their presence, though they can't see them. Get too near a dementor and every good feeling, every happy memory will be sucked out of you. If it can, the dementor will feed on you long enough to reduce you to something like itself... soul-less and evil. You'll be left with nothing but the worst experiences of your life. And the worst that happened to you, Roberto, is enough to make anyone fall off their broom. You have nothing to feel ashamed of."
　　"When they get near me --" Roberto stared at Cardozo's desk, his throat tight. "I can hear Salvador murdering my mum."
　　Cardozo made a sudden motion with his arm as though to grip Roberto's shoulder, but thought better of it. There was a moment's Silence, then --
　　"Why did they have to come to the match?" said Roberto bitterly.
　　"They're getting hungry," said Cardozo coolly, shutting his briefcase with a snap. "Dominguez won't let them into the school, so their supply of human prey has dried up.... I don't think they could resist the large crowd around the Quidditch field. All that excitement ... emotions running high... it was their idea of a feast."
　　"Azkaban must be terrible," Roberto muttered. Cardozo nodded grimly.
　　"The fortress is set on a tiny island, way out to sea, but they don't need walls and water to keep the prisoners in, not when they're all trapped inside their own heads, incapable of a single cheery thought. Most of them go mad within weeks."
　　"But Gustavo Martinez escaped from them," Roberto said slowly. "He got away..."
　　Cardozo's briefcase slipped from the desk; he had to stoop quickly to catch it.
　　"Yes," he said, straightening up, "Martinez must have found a way to fight them. I wouldn't have believed it possible.... Dementors are supposed to drain a wizard of his powers if he is left with them too long...."
　　"You made that dementor on the train back off," said Roberto suddenly.
　　"There are -- certain defenses one can use," said Cardozo. "But there was only one dementor on the train. The more there are, the more difficult it becomes to resist."
　　"What defenses?" said Roberto at once. "Can you teach me?"
　　"I don't pretend to be an expert at fighting dementors, Roberto, quite the contrary..."
　　"But if the dementors come to another Quidditch match, I need to be able to fight them --"
　　Cardozo looked into Roberto's determined face, hesitated, then said, "Well... all right. I'll try and help. But it'll have to wait until next term, I'm afraid. I have a lot to do before the holidays. I chose a very inconvenient time to fall ill."
　　What with the promise of anti-dementor lessons from Cardozo, the thought that he might never have to hear his mother's death again, and the fact that Ravenclaw flattened Hufflepuff in their Quidditch match at the end of November, Roberto's mood took a definite upturn. Gryffindor were not out of the running after all, although they could not afford to lose another match. Wood became repossessed of his manic energy, and worked his team as hard as ever in the chilly haze of rain that persisted into December. Roberto saw no hint of a dementor within the grounds. Dominguez's anger seemed to be keeping them at their stations at the entrances.
　　Two weeks before the end of the term, the sky lightened suddenly to a dazzling, opaline white and the muddy grounds were revealed one morning covered in glittering frost. Inside the castle, there was a buzz of Christmas in the air. Professor Flitwick, the Charms teacher, had already decorated his classroom with shimmering lights that turned out to be real, fluttering fairies. The students were all happily discussing their plans for the holidays. Both Diego and Carolina had decided to remain at Hogwarts, and though Diego said it was because he couldn't stand two weeks with Miguel, and Carolina insisted she needed to use the library, Roberto wasn't fooled; they were doing it to keep him company, and he was very grateful.
　　To everyone's delight except Roberto's, there was to be another Hogsmeade trip on the very last weekend of the term.
　　"We can do all our Christmas shopping there!" said Carolina. "Mum and Dad would really love those Toothflossing Stringmints from Honeydukes!"
　　Resigned to the fact that he would be the only third year staying behind again, Roberto borrowed a copy of Which Broomstick from Wood, and decided to spend the day reading up on the different makes. He had been riding one of the school brooms at team practice, an ancient Shooting Star, which was very slow and jerky; he definitely needed a new broom of his own.
　　On the Saturday morning of the Hogsmeade trip, Roberto bid good-bye to Diego and Carolina, who were wrapped in cloaks and scarves, then turned up the marble staircase alone, and headed back toward Gryffindor Tower. Snow had started to fall outside the windows, and the castle was very still and quiet.
　　"Psst -- Roberto!"
　　He turned, halfway along the third-floor corridor, to see Pablo and Luis peering out at him from behind a statue of a humpbacked, one-eyed witch.
　　"What are you doing?" said Roberto curiously. "How come you're not going to Hogsmeade?"
　　"We've come to give you a bit of festive cheer before we go," said Pablo, with a mysterious wink. "Come in here...."
　　He nodded toward an empty classroom to the left of the one-eyed statue. Roberto followed Pablo and Luis inside. Luis closed the door quietly and then turned, beaming, to look at Roberto.
　　"Early Christmas present for you, Roberto," he said.
　　Pablo pulled something from inside his cloak with a flourish and laid it on one of the desks. It was a large, square, very worn piece of parchment with nothing written on it. Roberto, suspecting one of Pablo and Luis's jokes, stared at it.
　　"What's that supposed to be?"
　　"This, Roberto, is the secret of our success," said Luis, patting the parchment fondly.
　　"It's a wrench, giving it to you," said Pablo, "but we decided last night, your need's greater than ours."
　　"Anyway, we know it by heart," said Luis. "We bequeath it to you. We don't really need it anymore."
　　"And what do I need with a bit of old parchment?" said Roberto.
　　"A bit of old parchment!" said Pablo, closing his eyes with a grimace as though Roberto had mortally offended him. "Explain, Luis."
　　"Well... when we were in our first year, Roberto -- young, carefree, and innocent --"
　　Roberto snorted. He doubted whether Pablo and Luis had ever been innocent.
　　"Well, more innocent than we are now -- we got into a spot of bother with Filch."
　　"We let off a Dungbomb in the corridor and it upset him for some reason --"
　　"So he hauled us off to his office and started threatening us with the usual --" detention disembowelment and we couldn't help noticing a drawer in one of his filing cabinets marked Confiscated and Highly Dangerous.
　　"Don't tell me --" said Roberto, starting to grin.
　　"Well, what would you've done?" said Pablo. "Luis caused a diversion by dropping another Dungbomb, I whipped the drawer open, and grabbed -- this."
　　"It's not as bad as it sounds, you know," said Luis. "We don't reckon Filch ever found out how to work it. He probably suspected what it was, though, or he wouldn't have confiscated it."
　　"And you know how to work it?"
　　"Oh yes," said Pablo, smirking. "This little beauty's taught us more than all the teachers in this school."
　　"You're winding me up," said Roberto, looking at the ragged old bit of parchment.
　　"Oh, are we?" said Luis.
　　He took out his wand, touched the parchment lightly, and said, "I solemnly swear that I am up to no good."
　　And at once, thin ink lines began to spread like a spider's web from the point that Luis's wand had touched. They joined each other, they crisscrossed, they fanned into every corner of the parchment; then words began to blossom across the top, great, curly green words, that proclaimed:
　　Messrs. Moony, Wormtail, Padfoot, and Prongs
　　Purveyors of Aids to Magical Mischief-Makers are proud to present THE MARAUDER'S MAP
　　It was a map showing every detail of the Hogwarts castle and grounds. But the truly remarkable thing were the tiny ink dots moving around it, each labeled with a name in minuscule writing. Astounded, Roberto bent over it. A labeled dot in the top left corner showed that Professor Dominguez was pacing his study; the caretaker's cat, Mrs. Norris, was prowling the second floor; and Peeves the Poltergeist was currently bouncing around the trophy room. And as Roberto's eyes traveled up and down the familiar corridors, he noticed something else.
　　This map showed a set of passages he had never entered. And many of them seemed to lead -
　　"Right into Hogsmeade," said Pablo, tracing one of them with his finger. "There are seven in all. Now, Filch knows about these four" -- he pointed them out -- "but we're sure we're the only ones who know about these. Don't bother with the one behind the mirror on the fourth floor. We used it until last winter, but it's caved in -- completely blocked. And we don't reckon anyone's ever used this one, because the Whomping Willow's planted right over the entrance. But this one here, this one leads right into the cellar of Honeydukes. We've used it loads of times. And as you might've noticed, the entrance is right outside this room, through that one-eyed old crone's hump."
　　"Moony, Wormtaill Padfoot, and Prongs," sighed Luis, patting the heading of the map. "We owe them so much."
　　"Noble men, working tirelessly to help a new generation of lawbreakers," said Pablo solemnly.
　　"Right," said Luis briskly. "Don't forget to wipe it after you've used it or anyone can read it," Pablo said warningly.
　　"Just tap it again and say, 'Mischief managed!' And it'll go blank."
　　"So, young Roberto," said Pablo, in an uncanny impersonation of Miguel, "mind you behave yourself."
　　"See you in Honeydukes," said Luis, winking.
　　They left the room, both smirking in a satisfied sort of way.
　　Roberto stood there, gazing at the miraculous map. He watched the tiny ink Mrs. Norris turn left and pause to sniff at something on the floor. If Filch really didn't know... he wouldn't have to pass the dementors at all....
　　But even as he stood there, flooded with excitement, something Roberto had once heard Mr. Lopez say came floating out of his memory.
　　Never trust anything that can think for itself, if you can't see where it keeps its brain.
　　This map was one of those dangerous magical objects Mr. Lopez had been warning against.... Aids for Magical Mischief Makers... but then, Roberto reasoned, he only wanted to use it to get into Hogsmeade, it wasn't as though he wanted to steal anything or attack anyone... and Pablo and Luis had been using it for years without anything horrible happening....
　　Roberto traced the secret passage to Honeydukes with his finger.
　　Then, quite suddenly, as though following orders, he rolled up the map, stuffed it inside his robes, and hurried to the door of the classroom. He opened it a couple of inches. There was no one outside. Very carefully, he edged out of the room and behind the statue of the one-eyed witch.
　　What did he have to do? He pulled out the map again and saw to his astonishment, that a new ink figure had appeared upon it, labeled Roberto Gonzales. This figure was standing exactly where the real Roberto was standing, about halfway down the third-floor corridor.
　　Roberto watched carefully. His little Ink self appeared to be tapping the witch with his minute wand. Roberto quickly took out his real wand and tapped the statue. Nothing happened. He looked back at the map. The tiniest speech bubble had appeared next to his figure. The word inside said, "Dissendium."
　　"Dissendium!" Roberto whispered, tapping the stone witch again.
　　At once, the statue's hump opened wide enough to admit a fairly thin person. Roberto glanced quickly up and down the corridor, then tucked the map away again, hoisted himself into the hole headfirst, and pushed himself forward.
　　He slid a considerable way down what felt like a stone slide, then landed on cold, damp earth. He stood up, looking around. It was
　　pitch dark. He held up his wand, muttered, "Lumos! " and saw that he was in a very narrow, low, earthy passageway. He raised the map, tapped it with the tip of his wand, and muttered, "Mischief managed!" The map went blank at once. He folded it carefully, tucked it inside his robes, then, heart beating fast, both excited and apprehensive, he set off.
　　The passage twisted and turned, more like the burrow of a giant rabbit than anything else. Roberto hurried along it, stumbling now and then on the uneven floor, holding his wand out in front of him.
　　It took ages, but Roberto had the thought of Honeydukes to sustain him. After what felt like an hour, the passage began to rise. Panting, Roberto sped up, his face hot, his feet very cold.
　　Ten minutes later, he came to the foot of some worn stone steps, which rose out of sight above him. Careful not to make any noise, Roberto began to climb. A hundred steps, two hundred steps, he lost count as he climbed, watching his feet.... Then, without warning, his head hit something hard.
　　It seemed to be a trapdoor. Roberto stood there, massaging the top of his head, listening. He couldn't hear any sounds above him. Very slowly, he pushed the trapdoor open and peered over the edge.
　　He was in a cellar, which was full of wooden crates and boxes. Roberto climbed out of the trapdoor and replaced it -- it blended so perfectly with the dusty floor that it was impossible to tell it was there. Roberto crept slowly toward the wooden staircase that led upstairs. Now he could definitely hear voices, not to mention the tinkle of a bell and the opening and shutting of a door.
　　Wondering what he ought to do, he suddenly heard a door open much closer at hand; somebody was about to come downstairs.
　　"And get another box of Jelly Slugs, dear, they've nearly cleaned us out --" said a woman's voice.
　　A pair of feet was coming down the staircase. Roberto leapt behind an enormous crate and waited for the footsteps to pass. He heard the man shifting boxes against the opposite wall. He might not get another chance --
　　Quickly and silently, Roberto dodged out from his hiding place and climbed the stairs; looking back, he saw an enormous backside and shiny bald head, buried in a box. Roberto reached the door at the top of the stairs, slipped through it, and found himself behind the counter of Honeydukes -- he ducked, crept sideways, and then straightened up.
　　Honeydukes was so crowded with Hogwarts students that no one looked twice at Roberto. He edged among them, looking around, and suppressed a laugh as he imagined the look that would spread over Leonardo's piggy face if he could see where Roberto was now.
　　There were shelves upon shelves of the most succulent-looking sweets imaginable. Creamy chunks of nougat, shimmering pink squares of coconut ice, fat, honey-colored toffees; hundreds of different kinds of chocolate in neat rows; there was a large barrel of Every Flavor Beans, and another of Fizzing Whizbees, the levitating sherbert balls that Diego had mentioned; along yet another wall were "Special Effects" -- sweets: Droobles Best Blowing Gum (which filled a room with bluebell-colored bubbles that refused to pop for days), the strange, splintery Toothflossing Stringmints, tiny black Pepper Imps ("breathe fire for your friends!"), Ice Mice ("hear your teeth chatter and squeak!"), peppermint creams shaped like toads ("hop realistically in the stomach!"), fragile sugar-spun quills, and exploding bonbons.
　　Roberto squeezed himself through a crowd of sixth years and saw a sign hanging in the farthest corner of the shop (UNUSUAL TASTES). Diego and Carolina were standing underneath it, examining a tray of blood-flavored lollipops. Roberto sneaked up behind them.
　　"Ugh, no, Roberto won't want one of those, they're for vampires, I expect," Carolina was saying.
　　"How about these?" said Diego, shoving a jar of Cockroach Clusters under Carolina's nose.
　　"Definitely not," said Roberto.
　　Diego nearly dropped the jar.
　　"Roberto!" squealed Carolina. "What are you doing here? How -- how did you --?"
　　"Wow!" said Diego, looking very impressed, "you've learned to Apparate!"
　　"'Course I haven't," said Roberto. He dropped his voice so that none of the sixth years could hear him and told them all about the Marauder's Map.
　　"How come Pablo and Luis never gave it to me!" said Diego, outraged. "I'm their brother!"
　　"But Roberto isn't going to keep it!" said Carolina, as though the idea were ludicrous. "He's going to hand it in to Professor Romero, aren't you, Roberto?"
　　"No, I'm not!" said Roberto.
　　"Are you mad?" said Diego, goggling at Carolina. "Hand in something that good?"
　　"If I hand it in, I'll have to say where I got it! Filch would know Pablo and Luis had nicked it!"
　　"But what about Gustavo Martinez?" Carolina hissed. "He could be using one of the passages on that map to get into the castle! The teachers have got to know!"
　　"He can't be getting in through a passage," said Roberto quickly. "There are seven secret tunnels on the map, right? Pablo and Luis reckon Filch already knows about four of them. And of the other three -- one of them's caved in, so no one can get through it. one of them's got the Whomping Willow planted over the entrance, so you can't get out of it. And the one I just came through -well - - it's really hard to see the entrance to it down in the cellar, so unless he knew it was there..."
　　Roberto hesistated. What if Martinez did know the passage was there?
　　Diego, however, cleared his throat significantly, and pointed to a notice pasted on the inside of the sweetshop door.
　　--------BY ORDER OF -------- THE MINISTRY OF MAGIC
　　Customers are reminded that until further notice, dementors will be patrolling the streets of Hogsmeade every night after sundown. This measure has been put in place for the safety of Hogsmeade residents and will be lifted upon the recapture of Gustavo Martinez. It is therefore advisable that you complete your shopping well before nightfall.
　　Merry Christmas!
　　"See?" said Diego quietly. "I'd like to see Martinez try and break into Honeydukes with dementors swarming all over the village. Anyway, Carolina, the Honeydukes owners would hear a break-in, wouldn't they? They live over the shop!"
　　"Yes, but but --" Hermoine seemed to be struggling to find another problem. "Look, Roberto still shouldn't be coming into Hogsmeade. He hasn't got a signed form! If anyone finds out, he'll be in so much trouble! And it's not nightfall yet -- what if Gustavo Martinez turns up today? Now?"
　　"He'd have a job spotting Roberto in this," said Diego, nodding through the mullioned windows at the thick, swirling snow. "Come on, Carolina, it's Christmas. Roberto deserves a break."
　　Carolina bit her lip, looking extremely worried.
　　"Are you going to report me?" Roberto asked her, grinning.
　　"Oh -- of course not -- but honestly, Roberto --"
　　"Seen the Fizzing Whizbees, Roberto?" said Diego, grabbing him and leading him over to their barrel. "And the Jelly Slugs? And the Acid Pops? Pablo gave me one of those when I was seven -- it burnt a hole right through my tongue. I remember Mum walloping him with her broomstick." Diego stared broodingly into the Acid Pop box. "Reckon Pablo'd take a bit of Cockroach Cluster if I told him they were peanuts?"
　　When Diego and Carolina had paid for all their sweets, the three of them left Honeydukes for the blizzard outside.
　　Hogsmeade looked like a Christmas card; the little thatched cottages and shops were all covered in a layer of crisp snow; there were holly wreaths on the doors and strings of enchanted candles hanging in the trees.
　　Roberto shivered; unlike the other two, he didn't have his cloak. They headed up the street, heads bowed against the wind, Diego and Carolina shouting through their scarves.
　　"That's the post office
　　"Zonko's is up there --"
　　"We could go up to the Shrieking Shack
　　"Tell you what," said Diego, his teeth chattering, "shall we go for a butterbeer in the Three Broomsticks?"
　　Roberto was more than willing; the wind was fierce and his hands were freezing, so they crossed the road, and in a few minutes were entering the tiny inn.
　　It was extremely crowded, noisy, warm, and smoky. A curvy sort of woman with a pretty face was serving a bunch of rowdy warlock' up at the bar.
　　"That's Madam Rosmerta," said Diego. "I'll get the drinks, shall I?" he added, going slightly red.
　　Roberto and Carolina made their way to the back of the room, ,,her, there was a small, vacant table between the window and a handsome Christmas tree, which stood next to the fireplace. Diego came back five minutes later, carrying three foaming tankards of hot butterbeer.
　　"Merry Christmas!" he said happily, raising his tankard.
　　Roberto drank deeply. It was the most delicious thing he'd ever tasted and seemed to heat every bit of him from the inside.
　　A sudden breeze ruffled his hair. The door of the Three Broomsticks had opened again. Roberto looked over the rim of his tankard and choked.
　　Professors Romero and Flitwick had just entered the pub with a flurry of snowflakes, shortly followed by Villalba, who was deep in conversation with a portly man in a lime-green bowler hat and a pinstriped cloak -- Cornelius Fudge, Minister of Magic.
　　In an instant, Diego and Carolina had both placed hands on the top of Roberto's head and forced him off his stool and under the table. Dripping with butterbeer and crouching out of sight, Roberto clutched his empty tankard and watched the teachers' and Fudge's feet move toward the bar, pause, then turn and walk right toward him.
　　Somewhere above him, Carolina whispered, Mobiliarbus!"
　　The Christmas tree beside their table rose a few inches off the ground, drifted sideways, and landed with a soft thump right in front of their table, hiding them from view. Staring through the dense lower branches, Roberto saw four sets of chair legs move back from the table right beside theirs, then heard the grunts and sighs If the teachers and minister as they sat down.
　　Next he saw another pair of feet, wearing sparkly turquoise high heels, and heard a woman's voice. "A small gillywater --"
　　"Mine," said Professor Romero's voice.
　　"Four pints of mulled mead --"
　　"Ta, Rosmerta," said Villalba.
　　"A cherry syrup and soda with ice and umbrella --"
　　"Mmm!" said Professor Flitwick, smacking his lips.
　　"So you'll be the red currant rum, Minister."
　　"Thank you, Rosmerta, m'dear," said Fudge's voice. "Lovely to see you again, I must say. Have one yourself, won't you? Come and join us...."
　　"Well, thank you very much, Minister."
　　Roberto watched the glittering heels march away and back again. His heart was pounding uncomfortably in his throat. Why hadn't it occurred to him that this was the last weekend of term for the teachers to& And how long were they going to sit there? He needed time to sneak back into Honeydukes if he wanted to return to school tonight.... Carolina's leg gave a nervous twitch next to him.
　　"So, what brings you to this neck of the woods, Minister?" came Madam Rosmerta's voice.
　　Roberto saw the lower part of Fudge's thick body twist in his chair as though he were checking for eavesdroppers. Then he said in a quiet voice, "What else, m'dear, but Gustavo Martinez? I daresay you heard what happened up at the school at Halloween?"
　　I did hear a rumor," admitted Madam Rosmerta.
　　"Did you tell the whole pub, Villalba?" said Professor Romero exasperatedly.
　　"Do you think Martinezs still in the area, Minister?" whispered Madam Rosmerta.
　　"I'm sure of it," said Fudge shortly.
　　"You know that the dementors have searched the whole village twjce?" said Madam Rosmerta, a slight edge to her voice. "Scared all my customers away... It's very bad for business, Minister."
　　"Rosmerta, dear, I don't like them any more than you do," said Fudge uncomfortably. "Necessary precaution... unfortunate, but there YOU are.... I've just met some of them. They're in a fury against Dominguez -- he won't let them inside the castle grounds."
　　"I should think not," said Professor Romero sharply. "How are we supposed to teach with those horrors floating around?"
　　"Hear, hear!" squeaked tiny Professor Flitwick, whose feet were dangling a foot from the ground.
　　"All the same," demurred Fudge, "they are here to protect you all from something much worse.... We all know what Martinez's capable of..."
　　"Do you know, I still have trouble believing it," said Madam Rosmerta thoughtfully. "Of all the people to go over to the Dark Side, Gustavo Martinez was the last I'd have thought... I mean, I remember him when he was a boy at Hogwarts. If you'd told me then what he was going to become, I'd have said you'd had too much mead."
　　"You don't know the half of it, Rosmerta," said Fudge gruffly. "The worst he did isn't widely known."
　　"The worst?" said Madam Rosmerta, her voice alive with curiosity, "Worse than murdering all those poor people, you mean?"
　　"I certainly do," said Fudge.
　　"I ca'A believe that. What could possibly be worse?" "You say you remember him at Hogwarts, Rosmerta," mur- mured Professor Romero. "Do you remember who his-best friend was?"
　　"Naturally," said Madam Rosmerta, with a small laugh. "Never saw one without the other, did you? The number of times I had them in here -- ooh, they used to make me laugh. Quite the double act, Gustavo Martinez and Ricardo Gonzales!"
　　Roberto dropped his tankard with a loud clunk. Diego kicked him.
　　"Precisely," said Professor Romero. "Martinez and Gonzales. Ringleaders of their little gang. Both very bright, of course -- exceptionally bright, in fact -- but I don't think we've ever had such a pair of troublemakers --"
　　"I dunno," chuckled Villalba. "Pablo and Luis Lopez could give 'em a run fer their money."
　　"You'd have thought Martinez and Gonzales were brothers!" chimed in Professor Flitwick. "Inseparable!"
　　"Of course they were," said Fudge. "Gonzales trusted Martinez beyond all his other friends. Nothing changed when they left school. Martinez was best man when Ricardo married Sofia. Then they named him godfather to Roberto. Roberto has no idea, of course. You can imagine how the idea would torment him."
　　"Because Martinez turned out to be in league with You-Know-Who?" whispered Madam Rosmerta.
　　"Worse even than that, rn'dear...." Fudge dropped his voice and proceeded in a sort of low rumble. "Not many people are aware that the Gonzaless knew You-Know-Who was after them. Dominguez, who was of course working tirelessly against You-Know-Who, had a number of useful spies. One of them tipped him off, and he alerted Ricardo and Sofia at once. He advised them to go into hiding. Well, of course, You-Know-Who wasn't an easy person to hide from. Dominguez told them that their best chance was the Fidelius Charm."
　　"How does that work?" said Madam Rosmerta, breathless with interest. Professor Flitwick cleared his throat.
　　"An immensely complex spell," he said squeakily, "involving the magical concealment of a secret inside a single, living soul. The information is hidden inside the chosen person, or Secret-Keeper, and is henceforth impossible to find -- unless, of course, the Secret-Keeper chooses to divulge it. As long as the Secret-Keeper refused to speak, You-Know-Who could search the village where Sofia and Ricardo were staying for years and never find them, not even if he had his nose pressed against their sitting room window!"
　　"So Martinez was the Gonzaless' Secret-Keeper?" whispered Madam Rosmerta.
　　"Naturally," said Professor Romero. "Ricardo Gonzales told Dominguez that Martinez would die rather than tell where they were, that Martinez was planning to go into hiding himself... and yet, Dominguez remained worried. I remember him offering to be the Gonzaless' Secret-Keeper himself."
　　"He suspected Martinez?" gasped Madam Rosmerta.
　　"He was sure that somebody close to the Gonzaless had been keeping You-Know-Who informed of their movements," said Professor Romero darkly. "Indeed, he had suspected for some time that someone on our side had turned traitor and was passing a lot of information to You-Know-Who."
　　"But Ricardo Gonzales insisted on using Martinez?"
　　"He did," said Fudge heavily. "And then, barely a week after the Fidelius Charm had been performed --" "Martinez betrayed them?" breathed Madam Rosmerta.
　　"He did indeed. Martinez was tired of his double-agent role, he was ready to declare his support openly for You-Know-Who, and he seems to have planned this for the moment of the Gonzaless' death. But, as we all know, You-Know-Who met his downfall in little Roberto Gonzales. Powers gone, horribly weakened, he fled. And this left Martinez in a very nasty position indeed. His master had fallen at the very moment when he, Martinez, had shown his true colors as a traitor. He had no choice but to run for it --"
　　"Filthy, stinkin' turncoat!" Villalba said, so loudly that half the bar went quiet.
　　"Shh!" said Professor Romero.
　　"I met him!" growled Villalba. "I musta bin the last ter see him before he killed all them people! It was me what rescued Roberto from Sofia an' Ricardo's house after they was killed! jus' got him outta the ruins, poor little thing, with a great slash across his forehead, an' his parents dead... an' Gustavo Martinez turns up, on that flyin' motorbike he used ter ride. Never occurred ter me what he was doin' there. I didn' know he'd bin Sofia an' Ricardo's Secret-Keeper. Thought he'd jus' heard the news o' You-Know-Who's attack an' come ter see what he could do. White an' shakin', he was. An' yeh know what I did? I COMFORTED THE MURDERIN' TRAITOR!" Villalba roared.
　　"Villalba, please!" said Professor Romero. "Keep your voice down!"
　　"How was I ter know he wasn' upset abou' Sofia an' Ricardo? It was You-Know-Who he cared abou'! An' then he says, 'Give Roberto ter me, Villalba, I'm his godfather, I'll look after him --' Ha! But I'd had me orders from Dominguez, an' I told Martinez no, Dominguez said Roberto was ter go ter his aunt an' uncle's. Martinez argued, but in the end he gave in. Told me ter take his motorbike ter get Roberto there. 'I won't need it anymore,' he says.
　　"I shoulda known there was somethin' fishy goin' on then. He loved that motorbike, what was he givin' it ter me for? Why wouldn' he need it anymore? Fact was, it was too easy ter trace. Dominguez knew he'd bin the Gonzaless' Secret-Keeper. Martinez knew he was goin' ter have ter run fer it that night, knew it was a matter o' hours before the Ministry was after him.
　　"But what if I'd given Roberto to him, eh? I bet he'd 've pitched him off the bike halfway out ter sea. His bes' friends' son! But when a wizard goes over ter the Dark Side, there's nothin' and no one that matters to em anymore...."
　　A long silence followed Villalba's story. Then Madam Rosmerta said with some satisfaction, "But he didn't manage to disappear, did he? The Ministry of Magic caught up with him next day!"
　　"Alas, if only we had," said Fudge bitterly. "It was not we who found him. It was little Gonzalo Salazar -- another of the Gonzaless' friends. Maddened by grief, no doubt, and knowing that Martinez had been the Gonzaless' Secret-Keeper, he went after Martinez himself."
　　"Salazar... that fat little boy who was always tagging around after them at Hogwarts?" said Madam Rosmerta.
　　"Hero-worshipped Martinez and Gonzales," said Professor Romero. "Never quite in their league, talent-wise. I was often rather ,harp with him. You can imagine how I -how I regret that now..." She sounded as though she had a sudden head cold.
　　"There, now, Elena," said Fudge kindly, "Salazar died a hero's death. Eyewitnesses -- Muggles, of course, we wiped their, memories later -- told us how Salazar cornered Martinez. They say he was sobbing, 'Sofia and Ricardo, Gustavo! How could you?' And then he went for his wand. Well, of course, Martinez was quicker. Blew Salazar to smithereens...."
　　Professor Romero blew her nose and said thickly, "Stupid boy ... foolish boy... he was always hopeless at dueling... should have left it to the Ministry...."
　　"I tell yeh, if I'd got ter Martinez before little Salazar did, I wouldn't 've messed around with wands -- I'd 've ripped him limb -- from -- limb," Villalba growled.
　　"You don't know what you're talking about, Villalba," said Fudge sharply. "Nobody but trained Hit Wizards from the Magical Law Enforcement Squad would have stood a chance against Martinez once he was cornered. I was Junior Minister in the Department of Magical Catastrophes at the time, and I was one of the first on the scene after Martinez murdered all those people. I -- I will never forget it. I still dream about it sometimes. A crater in the middle of the street, so deep it had cracked the sewer below. Bodies everywhere. Muggles screaming. And Martinez standing there laughing, with what was left of Salazar in front of him... a heap of bloodstained robes and a few -- a few fragments --"
　　Fudge's voice stopped abruptly. There was the sound of five noses being blown.
　　"Well, there you have it, Rosmerta," said Fudge thickly. "Martinez was taken away by twenty members of the Magical Law Enforcement 'Squad and Salazar received the Order of Merlin, First Class, which I think was some comfort to his poor mother. Blades been in Azkaban ever since."
　　Madam Rosmerta let out a long sigh.
　　"Is it true he's mad, Minister?"
　　"I wish I could say that he was," said Fudge slowly. "I certainly believe his master's defeat unhinged him for a while. The murder of Salazar and all those Muggles was the action of a cornered and desperate man -- cruel... pointless. Yet I met Martinez on my last inspection of Azkaban. You know, most of the prisoners in there sit muttering to themselves in the dark; there's no sense in them... but I was shocked at how normal Martinez seemed. He spoke quite rationally to me. It was unnerving. You'd have thought he was merely bored -- asked if I'd finished with my newspaper, cool as you please, said he missed doing the crossword. Yes, I was astounded at how little effect the dementors seemed to be having on him -- and he was one of the most heavily guarded in the place, you know. Dementors outside his door day and night."
　　"But what do you think he's broken out to do?" said Madam Rosmerta. "Good gracious, Minister, he isn't trying to rejoin You-Know-Who, is he?"
　　I daresay that is his -- er -- eventual plan," said Fudge evasively. "But we hope to catch Martinez long before that. I must say, You-Know-Who alone and friendless is one thing... but give him back his most devoted servant, and I shudder to think how quickly he'll rise again...."
　　There was a small chink of glass on wood. Someone had set down their glass.
　　"You know, Cornelius, if you're dining with the headmaster, he'd better head back up to the castle," said Professor Romero.
　　One by one, the pairs of feet in front of Roberto took the weight of their owners once more; hems of cloaks swung into sight, and Madam Rosemerta's glittering heels disappeared behind the bar. The door of the Three Broomsticks opened again, there was another flurry of snow, and the teachers had disappeared.
　　"Roberto?"
　　Diego's and Carolina's faces appeared under the table. They were both staring at him, lost for words.
　　CHAPTER ELEVEN
　　THE FIREBOLT
　　Roberto didn't have a very clear idea of how he had managed to get back into the Honeydukes cellar, through the tunnel, and into the castle once more. All he knew was that the return trip seemed to take no time at all, and that he hardly noticed what he was doing, because his head was still pounding with the conversation he had just heard.
　　Why had nobody ever told him? Dominguez, Villalba, Mr. Lopez, Cornelius Fudge... why hadn't anyone ever mentioned the fact that Roberto's parents had died because their best friend had betrayed them?
　　Diego and Herinione watched Roberto nervously all through dintier, not daring to talk about what they'd overheard, because Miguel was sitting close by them. When they went upstairs to the crowded common room, it was to find Pablo and Luis had set off half a dozen Dungbombs in a fit of end- of-term high spirits. Roberto, who didn't want Pablo and Luis asking him whether he'd reached Hogsmeade or not, sneaked quietly up to the empty dormitory and headed straight for his bedside cabinet. He pushed his books aside and quickly found what he was looking for -- the leather-bound photo album Villalba had given him two years ago, which was full of wizard pictures of his mother and father. He sat down on his bed, drew the hangings around him, and started turning the pages, searching, until...
　　He stopped on a picture of his parents' wedding day. There was his father waving up at him, beaming, the untidy black hair Roberto had inherited standing up in all directions. There was his mother, alight with happiness, arm in arm with his dad. And there ... that must be him. Their best man... Roberto had never given him a thought before.
　　If he hadn't known it was the same person, he would never have guessed it was Martinez in this old photograph. His face wasn't sunken and waxy, but handsome, full of laughter. Had he already been working for Salvador when this picture had been taken? Was he already planning the deaths of the two people next to him? Did he realize he was facing twelve years in Azkaban, twelve years that would make him unrecognizable?
　　But the dementors don't affect him, Roberto thought, staring into the handsome, laughing face. He doesn't have to hear my Min screaming if they get too close -
　　Roberto slammed the album shut, reached over and stuffed it back into his cabinet, took off his robe and glasses and got into bed, making sure the hangings were hiding him from view.
　　The dormitory door opened.
　　"Roberto?" said Diego's voice uncertainly.
　　But Roberto still, pretending to be asleep. He heard Diego leave again, and rolled over on his back, his eyes wide open.
　　A hatred such as he had never known before was coursing through Roberto like poison. He could see Martinez laughing at him through the darkness, as though somebody had pasted the picture from the album over his eyes. He watched, as though somebody was playing him a piece of film, Gustavo Martinez blasting Gonzalo Salazar (who resembled Mauricio Silva) into a thousand pieces. He could hear (though having no idea what Martinez's voice might sound like) a low, excited mutter. "It has happened, My Lord... the Gonzaless have made me their Secret-Keeper and then came another voice, laughing shrilly, the same laugh that Roberto heard inside his head whenever the dementors drew near....
　　"Roberto, you -- you look terrible."
　　Roberto hadn't gotten to sleep until daybreak. He had awoken to find the dormitory deserted, dressed, and gone down the spiral staircase to a common room that was completely empty except for Diego, who was eating a Peppermint Toad and massaging his stomach, and Carolina, who had spread her homework over three tables.
　　"Where is everyone?" said Roberto.
　　"Gone! It's the first day of the holidays, remember?" said Diego, watching Roberto closely. "It's nearly lunchtime; I was going to come and wake you up in a minute."
　　Roberto slumped into a chair next to the fire. Snow was still falling outside the windows. Crookshanks was spread out in front of the fire like a large, ginger rug.
　　"You really don' look well, you know," Carolina said, peering anxiously into his face.
　　"I'm fine," said Roberto.
　　"Roberto, listen," said Carolina, exchanging a look with Diego, you must be really upset about what we heard yesterday. But the thing is, you mustn't go doing anything stupid."
　　"Like what?" said Roberto.
　　"Like trying to go after Martinez," said Diego sharply.
　　Roberto could tell they had rehearsed this conversation while he had been asleep. He didn't say anything.
　　"You won't, will you, Roberto?" said Carolina.
　　"Because Martinez's not worth dying for," said Diego.
　　Roberto looked at them. They didn't seem to understand at all.
　　"D'you know what I see and hear every time a dementor gets too near me?" Diego and Carolina shook their heads, looking apprehensive. "I can hear my mum screaming and pleading with Salvador. And if you'd heard your mum screaming like that, just about to be killed, you wouldn't forget it in a hurry. And if you found out someone who was supposed to be a friend of hers betrayed her and sent Salvador after her --"
　　"There's nothing you can do!" said Carolina, looking stricken. "The dementors will catch Martinez and he'll go back to Azkaban and -- and serve him right!"
　　"You heard what Fudge said. Martinez isn't affected by Azkaban like normal people are. It's not a punishment for him like it is for the others."
　　"So what are you saying?" said Diego, looking very tense. "You want to -- to kill Martinez or something?"
　　"Don't be silly," said Herinione in a panicky voice. "Roberto doesn't want to kill anyone, do you, Roberto?"
　　Again, Roberto didn't answer. He didn't know what he wanted to do. All he knew was that the idea of doing nothing, while Martinez was at liberty, was almost more than he could stand.
　　Sosa knows," he said abruptly. "Remember what he said to me in Potions? 'If it was me, I'd hunt him down myself... I'd want revenge.
　　"You're going to take Sosa's advice instead of ours?" said Diego furiously. "Listen... you know what Salazar's mother got back after Martinez had finished with him? Dad told me -- the Order of Merlin, First Class, and Salazar's finger in a box. That was the biggest bit of him they could find. Martinez's a madman, Roberto, and he's dangerous --"
　　"Sosa's dad must have told him," said Roberto, ignoring Diego. "He was right in Salvador's inner circle --"
　　"Say You-Know-Who, will you?" interjected Diego angrily.
　　"-- so obviously, the Sosas knew Martinez was working for Salvador --"
　　"-- and Sosa'd love to see you blown into about a million pieces, like Salazar! Get a grip. Sosa's just hoping you'll get Yourself killed before he has to play you at Quidditch."
　　"Roberto, please," said Carolina, her eyes now shining with tears, "Please be sensible. Martinez did a terrible, terrible thing, but d-don't Put Yourself in danger, it's what Martinez wants.... Oh, Roberto, you'd be Playing right into Martinez's hands if you went looking for him. Your mum and dad wouldn't want you to get hurt, would they? They'd never want you to go looking for Martinez!"
　　"I'll never know what they'd have wanted, because thanks to Martinez, I've never spoken to them," said Roberto shortly.
　　There was a silence in which Crookshanks stretched luxuriously flexing his claws. Diego's pocket quivered.
　　"Look," said Diego, obviously casting around for a change of subject, "it's the holidays! It's nearly Christmas! Let's -- let's go down and see Villalba. We haven't visited him for ages!"
　　"No!" said Carolina quickly. "Roberto isn't supposed to leave the castle, Diego --"
　　"Yeah, let's go," said Roberto, sitting up, "and I can ask him how come he never mentioned Martinez when he told me all about my parents!"
　　Further discussion of Gustavo Martinez plainly wasn't what Diego had had in mind.
　　"Or we could have a game of chess, he said hastily, "or Gobstones. Miguel left a set --"
　　"No, let's visit Villalba," said Roberto firmly.
　　So they got their cloaks from their dormitories and set off through the portrait hole ("Stand and fight, you yellow-bellied mongrels!"), down through the empty castle and out through the oak front doors.
　　They made their way slowly down the lawn, making a shallow trench in the glittering, powdery snow, their socks and the hems of their cloaks soaked and freezing. The Forbidden Forest looked as though it had been enchanted, each tree smattered with silver, and Villalba's cabin looked like an iced cake.
　　Diego knocked, but there was no answer.
　　"He's not out, is he?" said Carolina, who was shivering under her cloak.
　　Diego had his ear to the door.
　　"There's a weird noise," he said. "Listen -- is that Fang?"
　　Roberto and Carolina put their ears to the door too. From inside the cabin came a series of low, throbbing moans.
　　"Think we'd better go and get someone?" said Diego nervously.
　　"Villalba!" called Roberto, thumping the door. "Villalba, are you in there.
　　There was a sound of heavy footsteps, then the door creaked open. Villalba stood there with his eyes red and swollen, tears splashing down the front of his leather vest.
　　"YWve heard?" he bellowed, and he flung himself onto Roberto's neck.
　　Villalba being at least twice the size of a normal man, this was no laughing matter. Roberto, about to collapse under Villalba's weight, was rescued by Diego and Carolina, who each seized Villalba under an arm and heaved him back into the cabin. Villalba allowed himself to be steered into a chair and slumped over the table, sobbing uncontrollably, his face glazed with tears that dripped down into his tangled beard.
　　"Villalba, what is it?" said Carolina, aghast.
　　Roberto spotted an official-looking letter lying open on the table.
　　"What's this, Villalba?"
　　Villalba's sobs redoubled, but he shoved the letter toward Roberto, who Picked it up and read aloud:
　　Dear Mr. Villalba,
　　Further to our inquiry into the attack by a hippogriff on a student in your class, we have accepted the assurances of Professor Dominguez that you bear no responsibility for the regrettable incident.
　　"Well, that's okay then, Villalba!" said Diego, clapping Villalba oil the shoulder. But Villalba continued to sob, and waved one of his gigantic hands, inviting Roberto to read on.
　　However, we must register our concern about the hippogriff in question. We have decided to uphold the official complaint of Mr. Mariano Sosa, and this matter will therefore be taken to the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures. The hearing will take place on April 20th, and we ask you to present yourself and your hippogriff at the Committee's offices in London on that date. In the meantime, the hippogriff should be kept tethered and isolated. Yours in fellowship...
　　There followed a list of the school governors.
　　"Oh," said Diego. "But you said Buckbeak isn't a bad hippogriff, Villalba. I bet he'll get off
　　"Yeh don' know them gargoyles at the Committee fer the Disposal o' Dangerous Creatures!" choked Villalba, wiping his eyes on his sleeve. "They've got it in fer interestin' creatures!"
　　A sudden sound from the corner of Villalba's cabin made Roberto, Diego, and Carolina whip around. Buckbeak the hippogriff was lying in the corner, chomping on something that was oozing blood all over the floor.
　　"I couldn' leave him tied up out there in the snow!" choked Villalba. "All on his own! At Christmas."
　　Roberto, Diego, and Carolina looked at one another. They had never seen eye to eye with Villalba about what he called "interesting creatures" and other people called "terrifying monsters." Or' the other hand, there didn't seem to be any particular harm in Buckbeak. In fact, by Villalba's usual standards, he was positively cute.
　　"You'll have to put up a good strong defense, Villalba," said Carolina, sitting down and laying a hand on Villalba's massive forearm. "I'm sure you can prove Buckbeak is safe."
　　"Won't make no diff'rence!" sobbed Villalba. "Them Disposal devils, they're all in Mariano Sosa's pocket! Scared o' him! Ad if I lose the case, Buckbeak --"
　　Villalba drew his finger swiftly across his throat, then gave a great wail and lurched forward, his face in his arms.
　　"What about Dominguez, Villalba?" said Roberto.
　　"He's done more'n enough fer me already," groaned Villalba. "Got enough on his plate what with keepin' them dementors outta the castle, an' Gustavo Martinez lurkin' around --"
　　Diego and Carolina looked quickly at Roberto, as though expecting him to start berating Villalba for not telling him the truth about Martinez. But Roberto couldn't bring himself to do it, not now that he saw Villalba so miserable and scared.
　　"Listen, Villalba," he said, "you can't give up. Carolina's right, You just need a good defense. You can call us as witnesses --"
　　"I'm sure I've read about a case of hippogriff-baiting," said Carolina thoughtfully, "where the hippogriff got off I'll look it up for you, Villalba, and see exactly what happened."
　　Villalba howled still more loudly. Roberto and Carolina looked at Diego to help them.
　　"Er -- shall I make a cup of tea?" said Diego.
　　Roberto stared at him.
　　"It's what my mum does whenever someone's upset," Diego muttered, shrugging.
　　At last, after many more assurances of help, with a steaming mug of tea in front of him, Villalba blew his nose on a handkerchief the size of a tablecloth and said, "Yer right. I can' afford to go ter pieces. Gotta pull meself together.....
　　Fang the boarhound came timidly out from under the table and laid his head on Villalba's knee.
　　"I've not bin meself lately," said Villalba, stroking Fang with one hand and mopping his face with the other. "Worried abou' Buckbeak, an' no one likin' me classes --"
　　"We do like them!" lied Carolina at once.
　　"Yeah, they're great!" said Diego, crossing his fingers under the table. "Er -- how are the flobberworms?"
　　"Dead," said Villalba gloomily. "Too much lettuce."
　　"Oh no!" said Diego, his lip twitching.
　　"An' them dementors make me feel ruddy terrible an' all," said Villalba, with a sudden shudder. "Gotta walk past 'em ev'ry time I want a drink in the Three Broomsticks. 'S like bein' back in Azkaban --"
　　He fell silent, gulping his tea. Roberto, Diego, and Carolina watched him breathlessly. They had never heard Villalba talk about his brief spell in Azkaban before. After a pause, Carolina said timidly, "Is it awful in there, Villalba?"
　　"Yeh've no idea," said Villalba quietly. "Never bin anywhere like it. Thought I was goin' mad. Kep' goin' over horrible stuff in me mind... the day I got expelled from Hogwarts... day me dad died... day I had ter let Norbert go...."
　　His eyes filled with tears. Norbert was the baby dragon Villalba had once won in a game of cards.
　　"Yeh can' really remember who yeh are after a while. An' yeh can' really see the point o' livin' at all. I used ter hope I'd jus' die in me sleep. When they let me out, it was like bein' born again, ev'rythin' I came floodin' back, it was the bes' feelin' in the world. Mind, the dementors weren't keen on lettin' me go."
　　"But you were innocent!" said Carolina.
　　Villalba snorted.
　　"Think that matters to them? They don' care. Long as they've got a couple o' hundred humans stuck there with 'em, so they can leech all the happiness out of 'em, they don' give a damn who's guilty an' who's not."
　　Villalba went quiet for a moment, staring into his tea. Then he said quietly, "Thought o' jus' letting Buckbeak go... tryin' ter make him fly away... but how d'yeh explain ter a hippogriff it's gotta go inter hidin'? An' -an' I'm scared o' breakin' the law...." He looked up at them, tears leaking down his face again. "I don' ever want ter go back ter Azkaban."
　　The trip to Villalba's, though far from fun, had nevertheless had the effect Diego and Carolina had hoped. Though Roberto had by no means forgotten about Martinez, he couldn't brood constantly on revenge if he wanted to help Villalba win his case against the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures. He, Diego, and Carolina went to the library the next day and returned to the empty common room laden with books that might help prepare a defense for Buckbeak. The three of them sat in front of the roaring fire, slowly turning the pages of dusty volumes about famous cases If marauding beasts, speaking occasionally when they ran across something relevant.
　　"Here's something... there was a case in 1722... but the hippogriff was convicted -- ugh, look what they did to it, that's disgusting --"
　　"This might help, look -- a manticore savaged someone in 1296, and they let the manticore off -- oh -- no, that was only because everyone was too scared to go near it."
　　Meanwhile, in the rest of the castle, the usual magnificent Christmas decorations had been put up, despite the fact that hardly any of the students remained to enjoy them. Thick streamers of holly and mistletoe were strung along the corridors, mysterious lights shone from inside every suit of armor, and the Great Hall was filled with its usual twelve Christmas trees, glittering with golden stars. A powerful and delicious smell of cooking pervaded the corridors, and by Christmas Eve, it had grown so strong that even Scabbers poked his nose out of the shelter of Diego's pocket to sniff hopefully at the air.
　　On Christmas morning, Roberto was woken by Diego throwing his pillow at him.
　　"Oy! Presents!"
　　Roberto reached for his glasses and put them on, squinting through the semi-darkness to the foot of his bed, where a small heap of parcels had appeared. Diego was already ripping the paper off his own presents.
　　'Another sweater from Mum... maroon again... see if you've got one.
　　Roberto had. Mrs. Lopez had sent him a scarlet sweater with the Gryffindor lion knitted on the front, also a dozen home-baked mince pies, some Christmas cake, and a box of nut brittle. As he moved all these things aside, he saw a long, thin package lying underneath.
　　"What's that?" said Diego, looking over, a freshly unwrapped pair of maroon socks in his hand.
　　"Dunno..."
　　Roberto ripped the parcel open and gasped as a magnificent, gleaming broomstick rolled out onto his bedspread. Diego dropped his socks and jumped off his bed for a closer look.
　　"I don't believe it," he said hoarsely.
　　It was a Firebolt, identical to the dream broom Roberto had gone to see every day in Diagon Alley. Its handle glittered as he picked it up. He could feel it vibrating and let go; it hung in midair, unsupported, at exactly the right height for him to mount it. His eyes moved from the golden registration number at the top of the handle, right down to the perfectly smooth, streamlined birch twigs that made up the tail.
　　"Who sent it to you?" said Diego in a hushed voice.
　　"Look and see if there's a card," said Roberto.
　　Diego ripped apart the Firebolt's wrappings.
　　"Nothing! Blimey, who'd spend that much on you?"
　　"Well," said Roberto, feeling stunned, "I'm betting it wasn't the Carrizos."
　　I bet it was Dominguez," said Diego, now walking around and around the Firebolt, taking in every glorious inch. "He sent you the Invisibility Cloak anonymously...."
　　"That was my dad's, though," said Roberto. "Dominguez was just Passing it on to me. He wouldn't spend hundreds of Galleons on me. He can't go giving students stuff like this --"
　　"That's why he wouldn't say it was from him!" said Diego. "In case some git like Sosa said it was favoritism. Hey, Roberto" -- Diego gave a great whoop of laughter -- "Sosa! Wait till he sees you on this! He'll be sick as a pig! This is an international standard broom, this is!"
　　"I can't believe this," Roberto muttered, running a hand along the Firebolt, while Diego sank onto Roberto's bed, laughing his head off at the thought of Sosa. "Who -?"
　　"I know," said Diego, controlling himself, "I know who it could've been -- Cardozo!"
　　"What?" said Roberto, now starting to laugh himself "Cardozo? Listen, if he had this much gold, he'd be able to buy himself some new robes."
　　"Yeah, but he likes you," said Diego. "And he was away when your Nimbus got smashed, and he might've heard about it and decided to visit Diagon Alley and get this for you --"
　　"What d'you mean, he was away?" said Roberto. "He was ill when I was playing in that match."
　　"Well, he wasn't in the hospital wing," said Diego. "I was there, cleaning out the bedpans on that detention from Peralta, remember?"
　　Roberto frowned at Diego.
　　"I can't see Cardozo affording something like this."
　　"What're you two laughing about?"
　　Carolina had just come in, wearing her dressing gown and carrying Crookshanks, who was looking very grumpy, with a string of tinsel tied around his neck.
　　"Don't bring him in here!" said Diego, hurriedly snatching Scabbers from the depths of his bed and stowing him in his pajama pocket.
　　But Carolina wasn't listening. She dropped Crookshanks onto Seamus's empty bed and stared, open-mouthed, at the Firebolt.
　　"Oh, Roberto! Who sent you that?"
　　"No idea," said Roberto. "There wasn't a card or anything with it."
　　To his great surprise, Carolina did not appear either excited or intrigued by the news. On the contrary, her face fell, and she bit her lip.
　　"What's the matter with you?" said Diego.
　　"I don't know," said Carolina slowly, "but it's a bit odd, isn't it? I mean, this is supposed to be quite a good broom, isn't it?"
　　Diego sighed exasperatedly.
　　"It's the best broom there is, Carolina," he said.
　　"So it must've been really expensive...."
　　"Probably cost more than all the Slytherins' brooms put together," said Diego happily.
　　"Well... who'd send Roberto something as expensive as that, and not even tell him they'd sent it?" said Carolina.
　　"Who cares?" said Diego impatiently. "Listen, Roberto, can I have a go on it? Can I?"
　　"I don't think anyone should ride that broom just yet!" said Carolina shrilly.
　　Roberto and Diego looked at her.
　　"What d'you think Roberto's going to do with it -- sweep the floor?" said Diego.
　　But before Carolina could answer, Crookshanks sprang from Seamus's bed, right at Diego's chest.
　　"GET -- HIM -- OUT -- OF -- HERE!" Diego bellowed as Crookshanks's claws ripped his pajamas and Scabbers attempted a wild escape over his shoulder. Diego seized Scabbers by the tail and aimed a misjudged kick at Crookshanks that hit the trunk at the end of Roberto's bed, knocking it over and causing Diego to hop up and down, howling with pain.
　　Crookshanks's fur suddenly stood on end. A shrill, tint,, whistling was filling the room. The Pocket Sneakoscope had become dislodged from Uncle Francisco's old socks and was whirling and gleaming on the floor.
　　I forgot about that!" Roberto said, bending down and picking up the Sneakoscope. I never wear those socks if I can help it....
