　　The Sneakoscope whirled and whistled in his palm. Crookshanks was hissing and spitting at it.
　　"You'd better take that cat out of here, Carolina," said Diego furiously, sitting on Roberto's bed nursing his toe. "Can't you shut that thing up?" he added to Roberto as Carolina strode out of the room, Crookshanks's yellow eyes still fixed maliciously on Diego.
　　Roberto stuffed the Sneakoscope back inside the socks and threw it back into his trunk. All that could be heard now were Diego's stifled moans of pain and rage. Scabbers was huddled in Diego's hands. It had been a while since Roberto had seen him out of Diego's pocket, and he was unpleasantly surprised to see that Scabbers, once so fat, was now very skinny; patches of fur seemed to have fallen out too
　　"He's not looking too good, is he?" Roberto said.
　　"It's stress!" said Diego. "He'd be fine if that big stupid furball left him alone!"
　　But Roberto, remembering what the woman at the Magical Menagerie had said about rats living only three years, couldn't help feeling that unless Scabbers had powers he had never revealed, he was reaching the end of his life. And despite Diego's frequent conplaints that Scabbers was both boring and useless, he was sure Diego would be very miserable if Scabbers died.
　　Christmas spirit was definitely thin on the ground in the Gryffindor common room that morning. Carolina had shut Crookshanks in her dormitory, but was furious with Diego for trying to kick him; Diego was still fuming about Crookshanks's fresh attempt to eat Scabbers. Roberto gave up trying to make them talk to each other and devoted himself to examining the Firebolt, which he had brought down to the common room with him. For some reason this seemed to annoy Carolina as well; she didn't say anything, but she kept looking darkly at the broom as though it too had been criticizing her cat.
　　At lunchtime they went down to the Great Hall, to find that the House tables had been moved against the walls again, and that a single table, set for twelve, stood in the middle of the room. Professors Dominguez, Romero, Peralta, Sprout, and Flitwick were there, along with Filch, the caretaker, who had taken off his usual brown coat and was wearing a very old and rather moldy- looking tailcoat. There were only three other students, two extremely nervous-looking first years and a sullen-faced Slytherin fifth year.
　　"Merry Christmas!" said Dominguez as Roberto, Diego, and Carolina approached the table. "As there are so few of us, it seemed foolish to use the House tables.... Sit down, sit down!"
　　Roberto, Diego, and Carolina sat down side by side at the end of the table.
　　"Crackers!" said Dominguez enthusiastically, offering the end of a large silver noisemaker to Peralta, who took it reluctantly and tugged. With a bang like a gunshot, the cracker flew apart to reveal a large, pointed witchs hat topped with a stuffed vulture.
　　Roberto, remembering the boggart, caught Diego's eye and they both grinned; Peralta's mouth thinned and he pushed the hat toward Dominguez, who swapped it for his wizard's hat at once.
　　"Dig in!" he advised the table, beaming around.
　　As Roberto was helping himself to roast potatoes, the doors of the Great Hall opened again. It was Professor Trelawney, gliding toward them as though on wheels. She had put on a green sequined dress in honor of the occasion, making her look more than ever like a glittering, oversized dragonfly.
　　"Sibyll, this is a pleasant surprise!" said Dominguez, standing up.
　　"I have been crystal gazing, Headmaster," said Professor Trelawney in her mistiest, most faraway voice, "and to my astonishment, I saw myself abandoning my solitary luncheon and coming to join you. Who am I to refuse the promptings of fate? I at once hastened from my tower, and I do beg you to forgive my lateness...."
　　"Certainly, certainly," said Dominguez, his eyes twinkling. "Let me draw you up a chair --"
　　And he did indeed draw a chair in midair with his wand, which revolved for a few seconds before falling with a thud between Professors Peralta and Romero. Professor Trelawney, however, did not sit down; her enormous eyes had been roving around the table, and she suddenly uttered a kind of soft scream.
　　I dare not, Headmaster! If I join the table, we shall be thirteen! Nothing could be more unlucky! Never forget that when thirteen dine together, the first to rise will be the first to die!"
　　"We'll risk it, Sibyll," said Professor Romero inpatiendy. "Do sit down, the turkey's getting stone cold."
　　Professor Trelawney hesitated, then lowered herself into the empty chair, eyes shut and mouth clenched tight, as though expecting a thunderbolt to hit the table. Professor Romero poked a large spoon into the nearest tureen.
　　"Tripe, Sibyll?"
　　Professor Trelawney ignored her. Eyes open again, she looked around once more and said, "But where is dear Professor Cardozo?"
　　"I'm afraid the poor fellow is ill again," said Dominguez, indicating that everybody should start serving themselves. "Most unfortunate that it should happen on Christmas Day."
　　"But surely you already knew that, Sibyll?" said Professor Romero, her eyebrows raised.
　　Professor Trelawney gave Professor Romero a very cold look.
　　"Certainly I knew, Elena, 11 she said quietly. "But one does not parade the fact that one is All- Knowing. I frequently act as though I am not possessed of the Inner Eye, so as not to make others nervous.
　　"That explains a great deal," said Professor Romero tartly.
　　Professor Trelawney's voice suddenly became a good deal less misty.
　　"If you must know, Elena, I have seen that poor Professor Cardozo will not be with us for very long. He seems aware, himself, that his time is short. He positively fled when I offered to crystal gaze for him --"
　　"Imagine that," said Professor Romero dryly.
　　I doubt," said Dominguez, in a cheerful but slightly raised voice, which put an end to Professor Romero and Professor Trelawney's conversation, "that Professor Cardozo is in any immediate danger. Carlos, you've made the potion for him again?"
　　"Yes, Headmaster," said Peralta. "W -- what?" said Roberto, scrambling to his feet. "Why?"
　　"It will need to be checked for jinxes," said Professor Romero. "Of course, I'm no expert, but I daresay Madam Hooch and Professor Flitwick will strip it down --"
　　"Strip it down?" repeated Diego, as though Professor Romero was mad.
　　"It shouldn't take more than a few weeks," said Professor Romero. "You will have it back if we are sure it is jinx-free."
　　"There's nothing wrong with it!" said Roberto, his voice shaking slightly. "Honestly, Professor --"
　　"You can't know that, Gonzales," said Professor Romero, quite kindly, "not until you've flown it, at any rate, and I'm afraid that is out of the question until we are certain that it has not been tampered with. I shall keep you informed."
　　Professor Romero turned on her heel and carried the Firebolt out of the portrait hole, which closed behind her. Roberto stood staring after her, the tin of High-Finish Polish still clutched in his hands. Diego, however, rounded on Carolina.
　　"What did you go running to Romero for?
　　Carolina threw her book aside. She was still pink in the face, but stood up and faced Diego defiantly.
　　"Because I thought -- and Professor Romero agrees with me -- that that broom was probably sent to Roberto by Gustavo Martinez!"
　　CHAPTER TWELVE
　　THE PATDIEGOUS
　　Roberto knew that Carolina had meant well, but that didn't stop him from being angry with her. He had been the owner of the best broom in the world for a few short hours, and now, because of her interference, he didn't know whether he would ever see it again. He was positive that there was nothing wrong with the Firebolt now, but what sort of state would it be in once it had been subjected to all sorts of anti-jinx tests?
　　Diego was furious with Carolina too. As far as he was concerned, the stripping-down of a brand- new Firebolt was nothing less than criminal damage. Carolina, who remained convinced that she had acted for the best, started avoiding the common room. Roberto and Diego supposed she had taken refuge in the library and didn't try to persuade her to come back. All in all, they were glad when the rest of the school returned shortly after New Year, and Gryffindor Tower became crowded and noisy again. Wood sought Roberto out on the night before term started.
　　"Had a good Christmas?" he said, and then, without waiting for an answer, he sat down, lowered his voice, and said, "I've been, doing some thinking over Christmas, Roberto. After last match, you know. If the dementors come to the next one... I mean... we can't afford you to -- well --"
　　Wood broke off, looking awkward.
　　"I'm working on it," said Roberto quickly. "Professor Cardozo said he'd train me to ward off the dementors. We should be starting this week. He said he'd have time after Christmas."
　　"Ah," said Wood, his expression clearing. "Well, in that case -- I really didn't want to lose you as Seeker, Roberto. And have you ordered a new broom yet?"
　　"No," said Roberto.
　　"What! You'd better get a move on, you know -- you can't ride that Shooting Star against Ravenclaw!"
　　"He got a Firebolt for Christmas," said Diego.
　　"A Firebolt? No! Seriously? A -- a real Firebolt?"
　　"Don't get excited, Oliver," said Roberto gloomily. "I haven't got it anymore. It was confiscated." And he explained all about how the Firebolt was now being checked for jinxes.
　　"Jinxed? How could it be jinxed?"
　　"Gustavo Martinez" Roberto said wearily. "He's supposed to be after me. So Romero reckons he might have sent it."
　　Waving aside the information that a famous murderer was after his Seeker, Wood said, "But Martinez couldn't have bought a Firebolt! He's on the run! The whole country's on the lookout for him! How could he just walk into Quality Quidditch Supplies and buy a broomstick?"
　　"I know," said Roberto, "but Romero still wants to strip it down --"
　　Wood went pale.
　　"I'll go and talk to her, Roberto," he promised. "I'll make her see reason.... A Firebolt... a real Firebolt, on our team... She wants Gryffindor to win as much as we do.... I'll make her see sense. A Firebolt..."
　　Classes started again the next day. The last thing anyone felt like doing was spending two hours on the grounds on a raw January morning, but Villalba had provided a bonfire full of salamanders for their enjoyment, and they spent an unusually good lesson collecting dry wood and leaves to keep the fire blazing while the flame-loving lizards scampered up and down the crumbling, white-hot logs. The first Divination lesson of the new term was much less fun; Professor Trelawney was now teaching them palmistry, and she lost no time in informing Roberto that he had the shortest life line she had ever seen.
　　It was Defense Against the Dark Arts that Roberto was keen to get to; after his conversation with Wood, he wanted to get started on his anti-dementor lessons as soon as possible.
　　"Ah yes," said Cardozo, when Roberto reminded him of his promise at the end of class. "Let me see... how about eight o'clock on Thursday evening? The History of Magic classroom should be large enough.... I'll have to think carefully about how we're going to do this.... We can't bring a real dementor into the castle to practice on...."
　　"Still looks ill, doesn't he?" said Diego as they walked down the corridor, heading to dinner. "What d'you reckon's the matter with him?"
　　There was a loud and impatient "tuh" from behind them. It was Carolina, who had been sitting at the feet of a suit of armor, repacking her bag, which was so full of books it wouldn't close.
　　"And what are you tutting at us for?" said Diego irritably.
　　"Nothing," said Carolina in a lofty voice, heaving her bag back over her shoulder.
　　"Yes, you were," said Diego. "I said I wonder what's wrong with Cardozo, and you --"
　　"Well, isn't it obvious?" said Carolina, with a look of maddening superiority.
　　"If you don't want to tell us, don't," snapped Diego.
　　"Fine," said Carolina haughtily, and she marched off.
　　"She doesn't know," said Diego, staring resentfully after Carolina. "She's just trying to get us to talk to her again."
　　At eight o'clock on Thursday evening, Roberto left Gryffindor Tower for the History of Magic classroom. It was dark and empty when he arrived, but he lit the lamps with his wand and had waited only five minutes when Professor Cardozo turned up, carrying a large packing case, which he heaved onto Professor Binn's desk.
　　"What's that?" said Roberto.
　　"Another boggart," said Cardozo, stripping off his cloak. "I've been combing the castle ever since Tuesday, and very luckily, I found this one lurking inside Mr. Filch's filing cabinet. It's the nearest we'll get to a real dementor. The boggart will turn into a dementor when he sees you, so we'll be able to practice on him. I can store him in my office when we're not using him; there's a cupboard under my desk he'll like."
　　"Okay," said Roberto, trying to sound as though he wasn't apprehensive at all and merely glad that Cardozo had found such a good substitute for a real dementor.
　　"So..." Professor Cardozo had taken out his own wand, and indicated that Roberto should do the same. "The spell I am going to try and teach you is highly advanced magic, Roberto -- well beyond ordinary Wizarding Level. It is called the Patronus Charm."
　　"How does it work?" said Roberto nervously.
　　"Well, when it works correctly, It conjures up a Patronus," said Cardozo, "which is a kind of anti- dementor -- a guardian that acts as a shield between you and the dementor."
　　Roberto had a sudden vision of himself crouching behind a Villalbasized figure holding a large club. Professor Cardozo continued, "The Patronus is a kind of positive force, a projection of the very things that the dementor feeds upon -- hope, happiness, the desire to survive -- but it cannot feel despair, as real humans can, so the dementors can't hurt it. But I must warn you, Roberto, that the charm might be too advanced for you. Many qualified wizards have difficulty with it."
　　"What does a Patronus look like?" said Roberto curiously.
　　"Each one is unique to the wizard who conjures it."
　　"And how do you conjure it?"
　　"With an incantation, which will work only if you are concentrating, with all your might, on a single, very happy memory."
　　Roberto cast his mind about for a happy memory. Certainly, nothing that had happened to him at the Carrizos' was going to do. Finally, he settled on the moment when he had first ridden a broomstick.
　　"Right," he said, trying to recall as exactly as possible the wonderful, soaring sensation of his stomach.
　　"The incantation is this --" Cardozo cleared his throat. "Expecto patronum!"
　　"Expecto patronum, " Roberto repeated under his breath, "expecto patronum."
　　"Concentrating hard on your happy memory?"
　　"Oh -- yeah --" said Roberto, quickly forcing his thoughts back to that first broom ride. "Expecto patrono -- no, patronum -- sorry -- expecto patronum, expecto patronum"
　　Something whooshed suddenly out of the end of his wand; it looked like a wisp of silvery gas.
　　"Did you see that?" said Roberto excitedly. "Something happened!"
　　"Very good," said Cardozo, smiling. "Right, then -- ready to try it on a dementor?"
　　"Yes," Roberto said, gripping his wand very tightly, and moving into the middle of the deserted classroom. He tried to keep his mind on flying, but something else kept intruding.... Any second now, he might hear his mother again... but he shouldn't think that, or he would hear her again, and he didn't want to... or did he?
　　Cardozo grasped the lid of the packing case and pulled.
　　A dementor rose slowly from the box, its hooded face turned toward Roberto, one glistening, scabbed hand gripping its cloak. The lamps around the classroom flickered and went out. The dementor stepped from the box and started to sweep silently toward Roberto, drawing a deep, rattling breath. A wave of piercing cold broke over him --
　　"Expecto patronum!" Roberto yelled. "Expecto patronum! Expecto --"
　　But the classroom and the dementor were dissolving.... Roberto was failing again through thick white fog, and his mother's voice was louder than ever, echoing inside his head -- "Not Roberto! Not Roberto! please -- I'll do anything!"
　　"Stand aside. Stand aside, girl!"
　　"Roberto!"
　　Roberto jerked back to life. He was lying flat on his back on the floor. The classroom lamps were alight again. He didn't have to ask what had happened.
　　"Sorry," he muttered, sitting up and feeling cold sweat trickling down behind his glasses.
　　"Are you all right?" said Cardozo.
　　"Yes..." Roberto pulled himself up on one of the desks and leaned against it.
　　"Here --" Cardozo handed him a Paulacolate Frog. "Eat this before we try again. I didn't expect you to do it your first time; in fact, I would have been astounded if you had."
　　"It's getting worse," Roberto muttered, biting off the Frog's head. "I could hear her louder that time -- and him -- Salvador
　　Cardozo looked paler than usual. ,
　　"Roberto, if you don't want to continue, I will more than understand --"
　　"I do!" said Roberto fiercely, stuffing the rest of the Paulacolate Frog into his mouth. "I've got to! What if the dementors turn up at our match against Ravenclaw? I can't afford to fall off again. If we lose this game we've lost the Quidditch Cup!"
　　"All right then... " said Cardozo. "You might want to select 'other memory, a happy memory, I mean, to concentrate on.... That one doesn't seem to have been strong enough...."
　　Roberto thought hard and decided his feelings when Gryffindor had won the House Championship last year had definitely qualified as very happy. He gripped his wand tightly again and took up his position in the middle of the classroom.
　　"Ready?" said Cardozo, gripping the box lid.
　　"Ready," said Roberto; trying hard to fill his head with happy thoughts about Gryffindor winning, and not dark thoughts about what was going to happen when the box opened.
　　"Go!" said Cardozo, pulling off the lid. The room went icily cold and dark once more. The dementor glided forward, drawing its breath; one rotting hand was extending toward Roberto -
　　"Expecto patronum!" Roberto yelled. "Expecto patronum! Expecto Pat --"
　　White fog obscured his senses... big, blurred shapes were moving around him... then came a new voice, a man's voice, shouting, panicking --
　　"Sofia, take Roberto and go! It's him! Go! Run! I'll hold him off --"
　　The sounds of someone stumbling ftom a room -- a door bursting open -- a cackle of high- pitched laughter --
　　"Roberto! Roberto... wake up...."
　　Cardozo was tapping Roberto hard on the face. This time it was a minute before Roberto understood why he was lying on a dusty classroom floor.
　　"I heard my dad," Roberto mumbled. "That's the first time I've ever heard him -- he tried to take on Salvador himself, to give my mum time to run for it...."
　　Roberto suddenly realized that there were tears on his face mingling with the sweat. He bent his face as low as possible, wiping them off on his robes, pretending to do up his shoelace, so that Cardozo wouldn't see.
　　"You heard Ricardo?" said Cardozo in a strange voice.
　　"Yeah..." Face dry, Roberto looked up. "Why -- you didn't know my dad, did you?"
　　"I -- I did, as a matter of fact," said Cardozo. "We were friends at Hogwarts. Listen, Roberto -- perhaps we should leave it here for tonight. This charm is ridiculously advanced.... I shouln't have suggested putting you through this...."
　　"No!" said Roberto. He got up again. "I'll have one more go! I'm not thinking of happy enough things, that's what it is.... Hang on...."
　　He racked his brains. A really, really happy memory... one that he could turn into a good, strong Patronus...
　　The moment when he'd first found out he was a wizard, and would be leaving the Carrizos for Hogwarts! If that wasn't a happy memory, he didn't know what was.... Concentrating very hard on how he had felt when he'd realized he'd be leaving Privet Drive, Roberto got to his feet and faced the packing case once more.
　　"Ready?" said Cardozo, who looked as though he were doing this against his better judgment. "Concentrating hard? All right -- go!"
　　He pulled off the lid of the case for the third time, and the dementor rose out of it; the room fell cold and dark
　　'EXPECTO PATDIEGOUM!" Roberto bellowed. "EXPECTO PATDIEGOUM! EXPECTO PATDIEGOUM! "
　　The screaming inside Roberto's head had started again -- except this time, it sounded as though it were coming from a badly tuned radio -- softer and louder and softer again -- and he could still see the dementor -- it had halted -- and then a huge, silver shadow came bursting out of the end of Roberto's wand, to hover between him and the dementor, and though Roberto's legs felt like water, he was still on his feet -- though for how much longer, he wasn't sure --
　　"Riddikulus!" roared Cardozo, springing forward.
　　There was a loud crack, and Roberto's cloudy Patronus vanished along with the dementor; he sank into a chair, feeling as exhausted as if he'd just run a mile, and felt his legs shaking. Out of the corner of his eye, he saw Professor Cardozo forcing the boggart back into the packing case with his wand; it had turned into a silvery orb again.
　　"Excellent!" Cardozo said, striding over to where Roberto sat. "Excellent, Roberto! That was definitely a start!"
　　"Can we have another go? Just one more go?"
　　"Not now," said Cardozo firmly. "You've had enough for one night. Here --"
　　He handed Roberto a large bar of Honeydukes' best chocolate.
　　"Eat the lot, or Madam Pomfrey will be after my blood. Same time next week?"
　　"Okay," said Roberto. He took a bite of the chocolate and watched Cardozo extinguishing the lamps that had rekindled with the disappearance of the dementor. A thought had just occurred to him.
　　"Professor Cardozo?" he said. "If you knew my dad, you must've known Gustavo Martinez as well."
　　Cardozo turned very quickly.
　　"What gives you that idea?" he said sharply.
　　"Nothing -- I mean, I just knew they were friends at Hogwarts too...."
　　Cardozo's face relaxed.
　　"Yes, I knew him," he said shortly. "Or I thought I did. You'd better be off, Roberto, it's getting late."
　　Roberto left the classroom, walking along the corridor and around a corner, then took a detour behind a suit of armor and sank down on its plinth to finish his chocolate, wishing he hadn't mentioned Martinez, as Cardozo was obviously not keen on the subject. Then Roberto's thoughts wandered back to his mother and father...
　　He felt drained and strangely empty, even though he was so full of chocolate. Terrible though it was to hear his parents' last moments replayed inside his head, these were the only times Roberto had heard their voices since he was a very small child. But he'd never be able to produce a proper Patronus if he half wanted to hear his parents again....
　　"They're dead," he told himself sternly. "They're dead and listening to echoes of them won't bring them back. You'd better get a grip on yourself if you want that Quidditch Cup."
　　He stood up, crammed the last bit of chocolate into his mouth, and headed back to Gryffindor Tower.
　　Ravenclaw played Slytherin a week after the start of term. Slytherin won, though narrowly. According to Wood, this was good news for Gryffindor, who would take second place if they beat Ravenclaw too. He therefore increased the number of team practices to five a leek. This meant that with Cardozo's anti-dementor classes, which in themselves were more draining than six Quidditch practices, Roberto had just one night a week to do all his homework. Even so, he was showing the strain nearly as much as Carolina, whose immense workload finally seemed to be getting to her. Every night, without fail, Carolina was to be seen in a corner of the common room, several tables spread with books, Arithmancy charts, rune dictionaries, diagrams of Muggles lifting heavy objects, and file upon file of extensive notes; she barely spoke to anybody and snapped when she was interrupted.
　　"How's she doing it?" Diego muttered to Roberto one evening as Roberto sat finishing a nasty essay on Undetectable Poisons for Peralta. Roberto looked up. Carolina was barely visible behind a tottering pile of books.
　　"Doing what?"
　　"Getting to all her classes!" Diego said. "I heard her talking to Professor Vector, that Arithmancy witch, this morning. They were going on about yesterday's lesson, but Carolina can't 've been there, because she was with us in Care of Magical Creatures! And Ernie McMillan told me she's never missed a Muggle Studies class, but half of them are at the same time as Divination, and she's never missed one of them either!"
　　Roberto didn't have time to fathom the mystery of Carolina's impossible schedule at the moment; he really needed to get on with Peralta's essay. Two seconds later, however, he was interrupted again, this time by Wood.
　　"Bad news, Roberto. I've just been to see Professor Romero about the Firebolt. She -- er -- got a bit shirty with me. Told m' I'd got my priorities wrong. Seemed to think I cared more about winning the Cup than I do about you staying alive. Just because I told her I didn't care if it threw you off, as long as you caught the Snitch first." Wood shook his head in disbelief. "Honestly, the way she was yelling at me... you'd think I'd said something terrible... then I asked her how much longer she was going to keep it. He screwed up his face and imitated Professor Romero's severe voice. 'As long as necessary, Wood'... I reckon it's time you ordered a new broom, Roberto. There's an order form at the back of Which Broomstick... you could get a Nimbus Two Thousand and One, like Sosa's got."
　　"I'm not buying anything Sosa thinks is good," said Roberto flatly.
　　January faded imperceptibly into February, with no change in the bitterly cold weather. The match against Ravenclaw was drawing nearer and nearer, but Roberto still hadn't ordered a new broom. He was now asking Professor Romero for news of the Firebolt after every Transfiguration lesson, Diego standing hopefully at his shoulder, Carolina rushing past with her face averted.
　　"No, Gonzales, you can't have it back yet," Professor Romero told him the twelfth time this happened, before he'd even opened his mouth. "We've checked for most of the usual curses, but Professor Flitwick believes the broom might be carrying a Hurling Hex. I shall tell you once we've finished checking it. Now, please stop badgering me."
　　To make matters even worse, Roberto's anti-dementor lessons were not going nearly as well as he had hoped. Several sessions on, he was able to produce an indistinct, silvery shadow every time the boggart-dementor approached him, but his Patronus was too feeble to drive the dementor away. All it did was hover, like a semitransparent cloud, draining Roberto of energy as he fought to keep it there. Roberto felt angry with himself, guilty about his secret desire to hear his parents' voices again.
　　"You're expecting too much of yourself," said Professor Cardozo, sternly in their fourth week of practice. "For a thirteen-year-old wizard, even an indistinct Patronus is a huge achievement. You aren't passing out anymore, are you?"
　　I thought a Patronus would -- charge the dementors down or something," said Roberto dispiritedly. "Make them disappear --"
　　"The true Patronus does do that," said Cardozo. "But you've achieved a great deal in a very short space of time. If the dementors put in an appearance at your next Quidditch match, You will be able to keep them at bay long enough to get back to the ground."
　　"You said it's harder if there are loads of them," said Roberto.
　　"I have complete confidence in you," said Cardozo, smiling. "Here -- you've earned a drink - something from the Three Broomsticks. You won't have tried it before --"
　　He pulled two bottles out of his briefcase.
　　"Butterbeer!" said Roberto, without thinking. "Yeah, I like that stuff!"
　　Cardozo raised an eyebrow.
　　"Oh -Diego and Carolina brought me some back from Hogsmeade," Roberto lied quickly.
　　I see," said Cardozo, though he still looked slightly suspicious. "Well -- let's drink to a Gryffindor victory against Ravenclaw! Not that I'm supposed to take sides, as a teacher... " he added hastily
　　They drank the butterbeer in silence, until Roberto voiced something he'd been wondering for a while.
　　"What's under a dementor's hood?"
　　Professor Cardozo lowered his bottle thoughtfully.
　　"Hmmm... well, the only people who really know are in no condition to tell us. You see, the dementor lowers its hood only to use its last and worst weapon."
　　"What's that?"
　　"They call it the Dementor's Kiss," said Cardozo, with a slightly twisted smile. "It's what dementors do to those they wish to destroy utterly. I suppose there must be some kind of mouth under there, because they clamp their jaws upon the mouth of the victim and -- and suck out his soul."
　　Roberto accidentally spat out a bit of butterbeer.
　　"What -- they kill --?"
　　"Oh no," said Cardozo. "Much worse than that. You can exist without your soul, you know, as long as your brain and heart are still working. But you'll have no sense of self anymore, no memory, no. .. anything. There's no chance at all of recovery. You'll just exist. As an empty shell. And your soul is gone forever... lost."
　　Cardozo drank a little more butterbeer, then said, "It's the fate that awaits Gustavo Martinez. It was in the Daily Prophet this morning. The Ministry have given the dementors permission to perform it if they find him."
　　Roberto sat stunned for a moment at the idea of someone having their soul sucked out through their mouth. But then he thought of Martinez.
　　"He deserves it," he said suddenly.
　　"You think so?" said Cardozo lightly. "Do you really think anyone deserves that?"
　　"Yes," said Roberto defiantly. "For... for some things..."
　　He would have liked to have told Cardozo about the conversation he'd overheard about Martinez in the Three Broomsticks, about Martinez betraying his mother and father, but it would have involved revealing that he'd gone to Hogsmeade without permission, and he knew Cardozo wouldn't be very impressed by that. So he finished his butterbeer, thanked Cardozo, and left the History of Magic classroom.
　　Roberto half wished that he hadn't asked what was under a dementor's hood, the answer had been so horrible, and he was so lost in unpleasant thoughts of what it would feel like to have your soul sucked out of you that he walked headlong into Professor Romero halfway up the stairs.
　　"Do watch where you're going, Gonzales!"
　　"Sorry, Professor --"
　　"I've just been looking for you in the Gryffindor common room, Well, here it is, we've done everything we could think of, and there doesn't seem to be anything wrong with it at all. You've got a very good friend somewhere, Gonzales...."
　　Roberto's jaw dropped. She was holding out his Firebolt, and it looked as magnificent as ever.
　　"I can have it back?" Roberto said weakly. "Seriously?"
　　"Seriously," said Professor Romero, and she was actually smiling. "I daresay you'll need to get the feel of it before Saturday's match, won't you? And Gonzales -- do try and win, won't you? Or we'll be out of the running for the eighth year. in a row, as Professor Peralta was kind enough to remind me only last night...."
　　Speechless, Roberto carried the Firebolt back upstairs toward Gryffindor Tower. As he turned a corner, he saw Diego dashing toward him, grinning from ear to ear.
　　"She gave it to You? Excellent! Listen, can I still have a go on it? Oscarorrow?"
　　"Yeah... anything," said Roberto, his heart lighter than it had been in a month. "You know what -- we should make up with Carolina.... She was only trying to help...."
　　"Yeah, all right," said Diego. "She's in the common room how working, for a change --"
　　They turned into the corridor to Gryffindor Tower and saw Mauricio Silva, pleading with Sir Cadogan, who seemed to be refusing him entrance.
　　"I wrote them down!" Mauricio was saying tearfully. "But I must've dropped them somewhere!"
　　"A likely tale!" roared Sir Cadogan. Then, spotting Roberto and Diego: "Good even, my fine young yeomen! Come clap this loon in irons. He is trying to force entry to the chambers within!"
　　"Oh, shut up," said Diego as he and Roberto drew level with Mauricio.
　　"I've lost the passwords!" Mauricio told them miserably. "I made him tell me what passwords he was going to use this week, because he keeps changing them, and now I don't know what I've done with them!"
　　"Oddsbodikins," said Roberto to Sir Cadogan, who looked extremely disappointed and reluctantly swung forward to let them into the common room. There was a sudden, excited murmur as every head turned and the next moment, Roberto was surrounded by people exclaiming over his Firebolt.
　　"Where'd you get it, Roberto?"
　　"Will you let me have a go?" "Have you ridden it yet, Roberto?"
　　"Ravenclaw'll have no chance, they're all on Cleansweep Sevens!"
　　"Can I just hold it, Roberto?"
　　After ten minutes or so, during which the Firebolt was Passed around and admired from every angle, the crowd dispersed and Roberto and Diego had a clear view of Carolina, the only person who hadn't rushed over to them, bent over her work and carefully avoiding their eyes. Roberto and Diego approached her table and at last, she looked up.
　　"I got it back," said Roberto, grinning at her and holding up the Firebolt.
　　"See, Carolina? There wasn't anything wrong with it!" said Diego.
　　"Well -- there might have been!" said Carolina. "I mean, at least you know now that it's safe!"
　　"Yeah, I suppose so," said Roberto. "Id better put it upstairs."
　　"I'll take it!" said Diego eagerly. "I've got to give Scabbers his rat tonic."
　　He took the Firebolt and, holding it as if it were made of glass, carried it away up the boys' staircase.
　　"Can I sit down, then?" Roberto asked Carolina.
　　"I suppose so," said Carolina, moving a great stack of parchment off a chair.
　　Roberto looked around at the cluttered table, at the long Arithmancy essay on which the ink was still glistening, at the even longer Muggle Studies essay ("Explain Why Muggles Need Electricity" and at the rune translation Carolina was now poring over.
　　"How are you getting through all this stuff?" Roberto asked her.
　　"Oh, well -- you know -- working hard," said Carolina. Close-up, Roberto saw that she looked almost as tired as Cardozo.
　　"Why don't you just drop a couple of subjects?" Roberto asked, watching her lifting books as she searched for her rune dictionary.
　　"I couldn't do that!" said Carolina, looking scandalized.
　　"Arithmancy looks terrible," said Roberto, picking up a very complicated-looking number chart.
　　"Oh no, it's wonderful!" said Carolina earnestly. "It's my favorite subject! It's --"
　　But exactly what was wonderful about Arithmancy, Roberto never found out. At that precise moment, a strangled yell echoed down the boys' staircase. The whole common room fell silent, staring, petrified, at the entrance. Then came hurried footsteps, growing louder and louder -- and then Diego came leaping into view, dragging with him a bedsheet.
　　"LOOK!" he bellowed, striding over to Carolina's table.
　　"LOOK!" he yelled, shaking the sheets in her face.
　　"Diego, what --?"
　　"SCABBERS! LOOK! SCABBERS!"
　　Carolina was leaning away from Diego, looking utterly bewildered. Roberto looked down at the sheet Diego was holding. There was something red on it. Something that looked horribly like --
　　"BLOOD!" Diego yelled into the stunned silence. "HE'S GONE! AND YOU KNOW WHAT WAS ON THE FLOOR?"
　　"N -- no," said Carolina in a trembling voice.
　　Diego threw something down onto Carolina's rune translation. Carolina and Roberto leaned forward. Lying on top of the weird, spiky shapes were several long, ginger cat hairs.
　　CHAPTER THIRTEEN
　　GRYFFINDOR VERSUS RAVENCLAW
　　It looked like the end of Diego and Carolina's friendship. Each was so angry with the other that Roberto couldn't see how they'd ever make up.
　　Diego was enraged that Carolina had never taken Crookshanks's attempts to eat Scabbers seriously, hadn't bothered to keep a close enough watch on him, and was still trying to pretend that Crookshanks was innocent by suggesting that Diego look for Scabbers under all the boys' beds. Carolina, meanwhile, maintained fiercely that Diego had no proof that Crookshanks had eaten Scabbers, that the ginger hairs might have been there since Christmas, and that Diego had been prejudiced against her cat ever since Crookshanks had landed on Diego's head in the Magical Menagerie.
　　Personally, Roberto was sure that Crookshanks had eaten Scabbers, and when he tried to point out to Carolina that the evidence all pointed that way, she lost her temper with Roberto too.
　　"Okay, side with Diego, I knew you would!" she said shrilly. "First the Firebolt, now Scabbers, everything's my fault, isn't it! just leave me alone, Roberto, I've got a lot of work to do!"
　　Diego had taken the loss of his rat very hard indeed.
　　"Come on, Diego, you were always saying how boring Scabbers was," said Pablo bracingly. "And he's been off-color for ages, he was wasting away. It was probably better for him to snuff it quickly -- one swallow -- he probably didn't feel a thing."
　　"Pablo!" said Martina indignantly.
　　"All he did was eat and sleep, Diego, you said it yourself," said Luis.
　　"He bit Goyle for us once!" Diego said miserably. "Remember, Roberto?"
　　"Yeah, that's true," said Roberto.
　　"His finest hour," said Pablo, unable to keep a straight face. "Let the scar on Goyle's finger stand as a lasting tribute to his memory. Oh, come on, Diego, get yourself down to Hogsmeade and buy a new rat, what's the point of moaning?"
　　In a last-ditch attempt to cheer Diego up, Roberto persuaded him to come along to the Gryffindor team's final practice before the Ravenclaw match, so that he could have a ride on the Firebolt after they'd finished. This did seem to take Diego's mind off Scabbers for a moment ("Great! Can I try and shoot a few goals on it?") so they set off for the Quidditch field together.
　　Madam Hooch, who was still overseeing Gryffindor practices to keep an eye on Roberto, was just as impressed with the Firebolt as everyone else had been. She took it in her hands before takeoff and gave them the benefit of her professional opinion.
　　"Look at the balance on it! If the Nimbus series has a fault, it's a slight list to the tail end -- you often find they develop a drag after a few years. They've updated the handle too, a bit slimmer than the Cleansweeps, reminds me of the old Silver Arrows -- a Pity they've stopped making them. I learned to fly on one, and a very fine old broom it was too...."
　　She continued in this vein for some time, until Wood said, "Er -- Madam Hooch? Is it okay if Roberto has the Firebolt back? We need to practice...."
　　"Oh -- right -- here you are, then, Gonzales," said Madam Hooch. "I'll sit over here with Lopez...."
　　She and Diego left the field to sit in the stadium, and the Gryffindor team gathered around Wood for his final instructions for tomorrow's match.
　　"Roberto, I've just found out who Ravenclaw is playing as Seeker. It's Paula Mejia. She's a fourth year, and she's pretty good.... I really hoped she wouldn't be fit, she's had some problems with injuries...." Wood scowled his displeasure that Paula Mejia had made a full recovery, then said, "On the other hand, she rides a Comet Two Sixty, which is going to look like a joke next to the Firebolt." He gave Roberto's broom a look of fervent admiration, then said, "Okay, everyone, let's go -- "
　　And at long last, Roberto mounted his Firebolt, and kicked off from the ground.
　　It was better than he'd ever dreamed. The Firebolt turned with the lightest touch; it seemed to obey his thoughts rather than his grip; it sped across the field at such speed that the stadium turned into a green-and-gray blur; Roberto turned it so sharply that Alicia Spinnet screamed, then he went into a perfectly controlled dive, brushing the grassy field with his toes before rising thirty, forty, fifty feet into the air again.
　　"Roberto, I'm letting the Snitch out!" Wood called.
　　Roberto turned and raced a Bludger toward the goal posts; he outstripped it easily, saw the Snitch dart out from behind Wood, and within ten seconds had caught it tightly in his hand.
　　The team cheered madly. Roberto let the Snitch go again, gave it a minute's head start, then tore after it, weaving in and out of the others; he spotted it lurking near Katie Bell's knee, looped her easily, and caught it again.
　　It was the best practice ever; the team, inspired by the presence of the Firebolt in their midst, performed their best moves faultlessly, and by the time they hit the ground again, Wood didn't have a single criticism to make, which, as Luis Lopez pointed out, was a first.
　　"I can't see what's going to stop us tomorrow!" said Wood. "Not unless -- Roberto, you've sorted out your dementor problem, haven't you?"
　　"Yeah," said Roberto, thinking of his feeble Patronus and wishing it were stronger.
　　"The dementors won't turn up again, Oliver. Dominguez'd go ballistic," said Pablo confidently.
　　"Well, let's hope not," said Wood. "Anyway -- good work, everyone. Let's get back to the tower... turn in early --"
　　"I'm staying out for a bit; Diego wants a go on the Firebolt," Roberto told Wood, and while the rest of the team headed off to the locker rooms, Roberto strode over to Diego, who vaulted the barrier to the stands and came to meet him. Madam Hooch had fallen asleep in her seat.
　　"Here you go," said Roberto, handing Diego the Firebolt.
　　Diego, an expression of ecstasy on his face, mounted the broom and zoomed off into the gathering darkness while Roberto walked around the edge of the field, watching him. Night had fallen before Madam Hooch awoke with a start, told Roberto and Diego off for not waking her, and insisted that they go back to the castle.
　　Roberto shouldered the Firebolt and he and Diego walked out of the shadowy stadium, discussing the Firebolt's superbly smooth action, its phenomenal acceleration, and its pinpoint turning. They were halfway toward the castle when Roberto, glancing to his left, saw something that made his heart turn over -- a pair of eyes, gleaming out of the darkness.
　　Roberto stopped dead, his heart banging against his ribs.
　　"What's the matter?" said Diego.
　　Roberto pointed. Diego pulled out his wand and muttered, "Lumos!"
　　A beam of light fell across the grass, hit the bottom of a tree, and illuminated its branches; there, crouching among the budding leaves, was Crookshanks.
　　"Get out of here!" Diego roared, and he stooped down and seized a stone lying on the grass, but before he could do anything else, Crookshanks had vanished with one swish of his long ginger tail.
　　"See?" Diego said furiously, chucking the stone down again. "She's still letting him wander about wherever he wants -- probably washing down Scabbers with a couple of birds now...."
　　Roberto didn't say anything. He took a deep breath as relief seeped through him; he had been sure for a moment that those eyes had belonged to the Grim. They set off for the castle once more. slightly ashamed of his moment of panic, Roberto didn't say anything to Diego -- nor did he look left or right until they had reached the well-lit entrance hall.
　　Roberto went down to breakfast the next morning with the rest of the boys in his dormitory, all of whom seemed to think the Firebolt deserved a sort of guard of honor. As Roberto entered the Great Hall, heads turned in the direction of the Firebolt, and there was a good deal of excited muttering. Roberto saw, with enormous satisfaction, that the Slytherin team were all looking thunderstruck.
　　"Did you see his face?" said Diego gleefully, looking back at Malfay. "He can't believe it! This is brilliant!"
　　Wood, too, was basking in the reflected glory of the Firebolt.
　　"Put it here, Roberto," he said, laying the broom in the middle of the table and carefully turning it so that its name faced upward. People from the Ravenclaw and Hufflepuff tables were soon coming over to look. Nicolas Ortega came over to congratulate Roberto on having acquired such a superb replacement for his Nimbus, and Miguel's Ravenclaw girlfriend, Penelope Clearwater, asked if she could actually hold the Firebolt.
　　"Now, now, Penny, no sabotage!" said Miguel heartily as she examined the Firebolt closely. "Penelope and I have got a bet on," he told the team. "Ten Galleons on the outcome of the match!"
　　Penelope put the Firebolt down again, thanked Roberto, and went back to her table.
　　"Roberto -- make sure you win," said Miguel, in an urgent whisper. "I haven't got ten Galleons. Yes, I'm coming, Penny!" And-he bustled off to join her in a piece of toast.
　　"Sure you can manage that broom, Gonzales?" said a cold, drawling voice.
　　Javier Sosa had arrived for a closer look, Crabbe and Coyle right behind him.
　　"Yeah, reckon so," said Roberto casually.
　　"Got plenty of special features, hasn't it?" said Sosa, eyes glittering maliciously. "Shame it doesn't come with a parachute -- in case you get too near a dementor."
　　Crabbe and Goyle sniggered.
　　"Pity you can't attach an extra arm to yours, Sosa," said Roberto. "Then it could catch the Snitch for you."
　　The Gryffindor team laughed loudly. Sosa's pale eyes narrowed, and he stalked away. They watched him rejoin the rest of the Slytherin team, who put their heads together, no doubt asking Sosa whether Roberto's broom really was a Firebolt.
　　At a quarter to eleven, the Gryffindor team set off for the locker rooms. The weather couldn't have been more different from their match against Hufflepuff. It was a clear, cool day with a very light breeze; there would be no visibility problems this time, and Roberto, though nervous, was starting to feel the excitement only a Quidditch match could bring. They could hear the rest of the school moving into the stadium beyond. Roberto took off his black school robes, removed his wand from his pocket, and stuck it inside the T-shirt he was going to wear under his Quidditch robes. He only hoped he wouldn't need it. He wondered suddenly whether Professor Cardozo was in the crowd, watching.
　　"You know what we've got to do," said Wood as they prepared to leave the locker rooms. "If we lose this match, we're out of the running. just -- just fly like you did in practice yesterday, and we'll be okay!"
　　They walked out onto the field to tumultuous applause. The Ravenclaw team, dressed in blue, were already standing in the middle of the field. Their Seeker, Paula Mejia, was the only girl on their team. She was shorter than Roberto by about a head, and Roberto couldn't help noticing, nervous as he was, that she was extremely pretty. She smiled at Roberto as the teams faced each other behind their captains, and he felt a slight lurch in the region of his stomach that he didn't think had anything to do with nerves.
　　"Wood, Davies, shake hands," Madam Hooch said briskly, and Wood shook hands with the Ravenclaw Captain.
　　"Mount your brooms... on my whistle... three -- two -- one --"
　　Roberto kicked off into the air and the Firebolt zoomed higher and faster than any other broom; he soared around the stadium and began squinting around for the Snitch, listening all the while to the commentary, which was being provided by the Lopez twins' friend Lee Jordan.
　　"They're off, and the big excitement this match is the Firebolt that Roberto Gonzales is flying for Gryffindor. According to Which Broomstick, the Firebolt's going to be the broom of choice for the national teams at this year's World Championship --"
　　"Jordan, would you mind telling us what's going on in the match?" interrupted Professor Romero's voice.
　　"Right you are, Professor -- just giving a bit of background information -- the Firebolt, incidentally, has a built-in auto-brake and --"
　　"Jordan!"
　　"Okay, okay, Gryffindor in possession, Katie Bell of Gryffindor, heading for goal..."
　　Roberto streaked past Katie in the opposite direction, gazing around for a glint of gold and noticing that Paula Mejia was tailing him closely. She was undoubtedly a very good flier -- she kept cutting across him, forcing him to change direction.
　　"Show her your acceleration, Roberto!" Pablo yelled as he whooshed past in pursuit of a Bludger that was aiming for Alicia.
　　Roberto urged the Firebolt forward as they rounded the Ravenclaw goal posts and Paula fell behind. Just as Katie succeeded in scoring the first goal of the match, and the Gryffindor end of the field went wild, he saw it -- the Snitch was close to the ground, flitting near one of the barriers.
　　Roberto dived; Paula saw what he was doing and tore after him -- Roberto was speeding up, excitement flooding him; dives were his speciality, he was ten feet away --
　　Then a Bludger, hit by one of the Ravenclaw Beaters, came pelting out of nowhere; Roberto veered off course, avoiding it by an inch, and in those few, crucial seconds, the Snitch had vanished.
　　There was a great "Ooooooh" of disappointment from the Gryffindor supporters, but much applause for their Beater from the Ravenclaw end. Luis Lopez vented his feelings by hitting the second Bludger directly at the offending Beater, who was forced to roll right over in midair to avoid it.
　　"Gryffindor leads by eighty points to zero, and look at that Firebolt go! Gonzales's really putting it through its paces now, see it turn -- Mejia's Comet is just no match for it, the Firebolt's precision- balance is really noticeable in these long --"
　　"JORDAN! ARE YOU BEING PAID TO ADVERTISE FIREBOLTS? GET ON WITH THE COMMENTARY!"
　　Ravenclaw was pulling back; they had now scored three goals, which put Gryffindor only fifty points ahead -- if Paula got the Snitch before him, Ravenclaw would win. Roberto dropped lower, narrowly avoiding a Ravenclaw Chaser, scanning the field frantically -- a glint of gold, a flutter of tiny wings -- the Snitch was circling the Gryffindor goal post --
　　Roberto accelerated, eyes fixed on the speck of gold ahead -- but just then, Paula appeared out of thin air, blocking him --
　　"ROBERTO, THIS IS NO TIME TO BE A GENTLEMAN!" Wood roared as Roberto swerved to avoid a collision. "KNOCK HER OFF HER BROOM IF YOU HAVE TO!"
　　Roberto turned and caught sight of Paula; she was grinning. The Snitch had vanished again. Roberto turned his Firebolt upward and was soon twenty feet above the game. Out of the corner of his eye, he saw Paula following him.... She'd decided to mark him rather than search for the Snitch herself... All right, then... if she wanted to tail him, she'd have to take the consequences....
　　He dived again, and Paula, thinking he'd seen the Snitch, tried to follow; Roberto pulled out of the dive very sharply; she hurtled downward; he rose fast as a bullet once more, and then saw it, for the third time -- the Snitch was glittering way above the field at the Ravenclaw end.
　　He accelerated; so, many feet below, did Paula. He was winning, gaining on the Snitch with every second -- then --
　　"Oh!" screamed Paula, pointing.
　　Distracted, Roberto looked down.
　　Three dementors, three tall, black, hooded dementors, were looking up at him.
　　He didn't stop to think. Plunging a hand down the neck of his robes, he whipped out his wand and roared, "Expecto patronum!"
　　Something silver-white, something enormous, erupted from the end of his wand. He knew it had shot directly at the dementors but didn't pause to watch; his mind still miraculously clear, he looked ahead -- he was nearly there. He stretched out the hand still grasping his wand and just managed to close his fingers over the small, struggling Snitch.
　　Madam Hooch's whistle sounded. Roberto turned around in midair and saw six scarlet blurs bearing down on him; next moment, the whole team was hugging him so hard he was nearly pulled off his broom. Down below he could hear the roars of the Gryffindors in the crowd.
　　"That's my boy!" Wood kept yelling. Alicia, Angelina, and Katie had all kissed Roberto; Pablo had him in a grip so tight Roberto felt as though his head would come off In complete disarray, the team managed to make its way back to the ground. Roberto got off his broom and looked up to see a gaggle of Gryffindor supporters sprinting onto the field, Diego in the lead. Before he knew it, he had been engulfed by the cheering crowd.
　　"Yes!" Diego yelled, yanking Roberto's arm into the air. "Yes! Yes!"
　　"Well done, Roberto!" said Miguel, looking delighted. "Ten Galleons to me! Must find Penelope, excuse me --"
　　"Good for you, Roberto!" roared Seamus Finnigan.
　　"Ruddy brilliant!" boomed Villalba over the heads of the milling Gryffindors.
　　"That was quite some Patronus," said a voice in Roberto's ear.
　　Roberto turned around to see Professor Cardozo, who looked both shaken and pleased.
　　"The dementors didn't affect me at all!" Roberto said excitedly. "I didn't feel a thing!"
　　"That would be because they -- er -- weren't dementors," said Professor Cardozo. "Come and see -- "
　　He led Roberto out of the crowd until they were able to see the edge of the field.
　　"You gave Mr. Sosa quite a fright," said Cardozo.
　　Roberto stared. Lying in a crumpled heap on the ground were Sosa, Crabbe, Goyle, and Marcus Flint, the Slytherin team Captain, all struggling to remove themselves from long, black, hooded robes. It looked as though Sosa had been standing on Goyle's shoulders. Standing over them, with an expression of the utmost fury on her face, was Professor Romero.
　　"An unworthy trick!" she was shouting. "A low and cowardly attempt to sabotage the Gryffindor Seeker! Detention for all of you, and fifty points from Slytherin! I shall be speaking to Professor Dominguez about this, make no mistake! Ah, here he comes now!"
　　If anything could have set the seal on Gryffindor's victory, it was this. Diego, who had fought his way through to Roberto's side, doubled up with laughter as they watched Sosa fighting to extricate himself from the robe, Goyle's head still stuck inside it.
　　"Come on, Roberto!" said Luis, fighting his way over. "Party! Gryffindor common room, now!"
　　"Right," said Roberto, and feeling happier than he had in ages, he and the rest of the team led the way, still in their scarlet robes, out of the stadium and back up to the castle.
　　It felt as though they had already won the Quidditch Cup; the party went on all day and well into the night. Pablo and Luis Lopez disappeared for a couple of hours and returned with armfuls of bottles of butterbeer, pumpkin fizz, and several bags full of Honeydukes sweets.
　　"How did you do that?" squealed Angelina Johnson as Luis started throwing Peppermint Toads into the crowd.
　　"With a little help from Moony, Wormtail, Padfoot, and Prongs," Pablo muttered in Roberto's ear.
　　Only one person wasn't joining in the festivities. Carolina, incredibly, was sitting in a corner, attempting to read an enormous book entitled Home Life and Social Habits of British Muggles. Roberto broke away from the table where Pablo and Luis had started juggling butterbeer bottles and went over to her.
　　"Did you even come to the match?" he asked her.
　　"Of course I did," said Carolina in a strangely high-pitched voice, not looking up. "And I'm very glad we won, and I think you did really well, but I need to read this by Monday."
　　"Come on, Carolina, come and have some food," Roberto said, looking over at Diego and wondering whether he was in a good enough mood to bury the hatchet.
　　"I can't, Roberto. I've still got four hundred and twenty-two pages to read!" said Carolina, now sounding slightly hysterical. "Anyway..." She glanced over at Diego too. "He doesn't want me to join in."
　　There was no arguing with this, as Diego chose that moment to say loudly, "If Scabbers hadn't just been eaten, he could have had some of those Fudge Flies. He used to really like them --"
　　Carolina burst into tears. Before Roberto could say or do anything, she tucked the enormous book under her arm, and, still sobbing, ran toward the staircase to the girls' dormitories and out of sight.
　　"Can't you give her a break?" Roberto asked Diego quietly.
　　"No," said Diego flatly. "If she just acted like she was sorry -- but she'll never admit she's wrong, Carolina. She's still acting like Scabbers has gone on vacation or something."
　　The Gryffindor party ended only when Professor Romero turned up in her tartan dressing gown and hair net at one in the morning, to insist that they all go to bed. Roberto and Diego climbed the stairs to their dormitory, still discussing the match. At last, exhausted, Roberto climbed into bed, twitched the hangings of his four-poster shut to block out a ray of moonlight, lay back, and felt himself almost instantly drifting off to sleep....
　　He had a very strange dream. He was walking through a forest, his Firebolt over his shoulder, following something silvery-white. It was winding its way through the trees ahead, and he could only catch glimpses of it between the leaves. Anxious to catch up with it, he sped up, but as he moved faster, so did his quarry. Roberto broke into a run, and ahead he heard hooves gathering speed. Now he was running flat out, and ahead he could hear galloping. Then he turned a corner into a clearing and -
　　"AAARRGGHH! NOOO!"
　　Roberto woke as suddenly as though he'd been hit in the face. Disoriented in the total darkness, he fumbled with his hangings, he could hear movements around him, and Seamus Finnigan's voice from the other side of the room: "What's going on?"
　　Roberto thought he heard the dormitory door slam. At last finding the divide in his curtains, he ripped them back, and at the same moment, Dean Thomas lit his lamp.
　　Diego was sitting up in bed, the hangings torn from one side, a look of utmost terror on his face.
　　"Martinez! Gustavo Martinez! With a knife!"
　　"What?"
　　"Here! Just now! Slashed the curtains! Woke me up!"
　　"You sure you weren't dreaming, Diego?" said Dean.
　　"Look at the curtains! I tell you, he was here!"
　　They all scrambled out of bed; Roberto reached the dormitory door first, and they sprinted back down the staircase. Doors opened behind them, and sleepy voices called after them.
　　"Who shouted?"
　　"What're you doing?"
　　The common room was lit with the glow of the dying fire, still littered with the debris from the party. It was deserted.
　　"Are you sure you weren't dreaming, Diego?"
　　"I'm telling you, I saw him!"
　　"What's all the noise?"
　　"Professor Romero told us to go to bed!"
　　A few of the girls had come down their staircase, pulling or, dressing gowns and yawning. Boys, too, were reappearing.
　　"Excellent, are we carrying on?" said Pablo Lopez brightly.
　　"Everyone back upstairs!" said Miguel, hurrying into the common room and pinning his Head Boy badge to his pajamas as he spoke.
　　"Perce -- Gustavo Martinez!" said Diego faintly. "In our dormitory! With a knife! Woke me up!"
　　The common room went very still.
　　"Nonsense!" said Miguel, looking startled. "You had too much to eat, Diego -- had a nightmare --"
　　"I'm telling you --"
　　"Now, really, enough's enough!"
　　Professor Romero was back. She slammed the portrait behind her as she entered the common room and stared furiously around.
　　"I am delighted that Gryffindor won the match, but this is getting ridiculous! Miguel, I expected better of you!"
　　"I certainly didn't authorize this, Professor!" said Miguel, puffing himself up indignantly. "I was just telling them all to get back to bed! My brother Diego here had a nightmare --"
　　"IT WASN'T A NIGHTMARE!" Diego yelled. "PROFESSOR, I WOKE UP, AND GUSTAVO MARTINEZ WAS STANDING OVER ME, HOLDING A KNIFE!"
　　Professor Romero stared at him.
　　"Don't be ridiculous, Lopez, how could he possibly have gotten through the portrait hole?"
　　"Ask him!" said Diego, pointing a shaking finger at the back of Sir Cadogan's picture. "Ask him if he saw --"
　　Glaring suspiciously at Diego, Professor Romero pushed the Portrait back open and went outside. The whole common room listened with bated breath. "Sir Cadogan, did you just let a man enter Gryffindor Tower?" "Certainly, good lady!" cried Sir Cadogan.
　　There was a stunned silence, both inside and outside the common room.
　　"You -- you did?" said Professor Romero. "But -- but the password!"
　　"He had 'em!" said Sir Cadogan proudly. "Had the whole week's, my lady! Read 'em off a little piece of paper!"
　　Professor Romero pulled herself back through the portrait hole to face the stunned crowd. She was white as chalk.
　　"Which person," she said, her voice shaking, "which abysmally foolish person wrote down this week's passwords and left them lying around?"
　　There was utter silence, broken by the smallest of terrified squeaks. Mauricio Silva, trembling from head to fluffy slippered toes, raised his hand slowly into the air.
　　CHAPTER FOURTEEN
　　PERALTA'S GRUDGE
　　No one in Gryffindor Tower slept that night. They knew that the castle was being searched again, and the whole House stayed awake in the common room, waiting to hear whether Martinez had been caught. Professor Romero came back at dawn, to tell them that he had again escaped.
　　Throughout the day, everywhere they went they saw signs of tighter security; Professor Flitwick could be seen teaching the front doors to recognize a large picture of Gustavo Martinez; Filch was suddenly bustling up and down the corridors, boarding up everything from tiny cracks in the walls to mouse holes. Sir Cadogan had been fired. His portrait had been taken back to its lonely landing on the seventh floor, and the Fat Lady was back. She had been expertly restored, but was still extremely nervous, and had agreed to return to her job only on condition that she was given extra protection. A bunch of surly security trolls had been hired to guard her. They paced the corridor in a menacing group, talking in grunts and comparing the size of their clubs.
　　Roberto couldn't help noticing that the statue of the one-eyed witch on the third floor remained unguarded and unblocked. It seemed that Pablo and Luis had been right in thinking that they -- and now Roberto, Diego, and Carolina -- were the only ones who knew about the hidden passageway within it.
　　"D'you reckon we should tell someone?" Roberto asked Diego.
　　"We know he's not coming in through Honeyduke's," said Diego dismissively. "We'd've heard if the shop had been broken into."
　　Roberto was glad Diego took this view. If the one-eyed witch was boarded up too, he would never be able to go into Hogsmeade again.
　　Diego had become an instant celebrity. For the first time in his life, people were paying more attention to him than to Roberto, and it was clear that Diego was rather enjoying the experience. Though still severely shaken by the night's events, he was happy to tell anyone who asked what had happened, with a wealth of detail.
　　"... I was asleep, and I heard this ripping noise, and I thought it was in my dream, you know? But then there was this draft... I woke up and one side of the hangings on my bed had been pulled down.... I rolled over... and I saw him standing over me... like a skeleton, with loads of filthy hair ... holding this great long knife, must've been twelve inches... and he looked at me, and I looked at him, and then I yelled, and he scampered.
　　"Why, though?" Diego added to Roberto as the group of secondyear girls who had been listening to his chilling tale departed. "Why did he run?"
　　Roberto had been wondering the same thing. Why had Martinez, having got the wrong bed, not silenced Diego and proceeded to Roberto? Martinez had proved twelve years ago that he didn't mind murdering innocent people, and this time he had been facing five unarmed boys, four of whom were asleep.
　　"He must've known he'd have a job getting back out of the castle once you'd yelled and woken people up," said Roberto thoughtfully. "He'd've had to kill the whole House to get back through the portrait hole... then he would' ve met the teachers...."
　　Mauricio was in total disgrace. Professor Romero was so furious with him she had banned him from all future Hogsmeade visits, given him a detention, and forbidden anyone to give him the password into the tower. Poor Mauricio was forced to wait. outside the common room every night for somebody to let him in, while the security trolls leered unpleasantly at him. None of these punishments, however, came close to matching the one his grandmother had in store for him. Two days after Martinez's break-in, she sent Mauricio the very worst thing a Hogwarts student could receive over breakfast -- a Howler.
　　The school owls swooped into the Great Hall carrying the mail as usual, and Mauricio choked as a huge barn owl landed in front of him, a scarlet envelope clutched in its beak. Roberto and Diego, who were sitting opposite him, recognized the letter as a Howler at once -- Diego had got one from his mother the year before.
　　"Run for it, Mauricio," Diego advised.
　　Mauricio didn't need telling twice. He seized the envelope, and holding it before him like a bomb, sprinted out of the hall, while the Slytherin table exploded with laughter at the sight of him. They heard the Howler go off in the entrance hall -- Mauricio's grandmother's voice, magically magnified to a hundred times its Usual volume, shrieking about how he had brought shame on the whole family.
　　Roberto was too busy feeling sorry for Mauricio to notice immediately that he had a letter too. Hedwig got his attention by nipping him sharply on the wrist.
　　"Ouch! Oh -- thanks, Hedwig."
　　Roberto tore open the envelope while Hedwig helped herself to some of Mauricio's cornflakes. The note inside said:
　　Dear Roberto and Diego, How Abut having tea with me this afternoon 'round six? I'll come collect you from the castle. WAIT FOR ME IN THE ENTRANCE HALL; YOU'RE NOT ALLOWED OUT ON YOUR OWN. Cheers, Villalba
　　"He probably wants to hear all about Martinez!" said Diego.
　　So at six o'clock that afternoon, Roberto and Diego left Gryffindor Tower, passed the security trolls at a run, and headed down to the entrance hall.
　　Villalba was already waiting for them.
　　"All right, Villalba!" said Diego. "S'pose you want to hear about Saturday night, do you?"
　　"I've already heard all abou' it," said Villalba, opening the front doors and leading them outside.
　　"Oh," said Diego, looking slightly put out.
　　The first thing they saw on entering Villalba's cabin was Buckbeak, who was stretched out on top of Villalba's patchwork quilt, his enormous wings folded tight to his body, enjoying a large plate of dead ferrets. Averting his eyes from this unpleasant sight, Roberto saw a gigantic, hairy brown suit and a very horrible yellow-and-orange tie hanging from the top of Villalba's wardrobe door.
　　"What are they for, Villalba?" said Roberto.
　　"Buckbeaks case against the Committee fer the Disposal o' Dangerous Creatures," said Villalba. "This Friday. Him an' me'll be goin' down ter London together. I've booked two beds on the Knight Bus...."
　　Roberto felt a nasty pang of guilt. He had completely forgotten that Buckbeak's trial was so near, and judging by the uneasy look on Diego's face, he had too. They had also forgotten their promise about helping him prepare Buckbeak's defense; the arrival of the Firebolt had driven it clean out of their minds.
　　Villalba poured them tea and offered them a plate of Bath buns but they knew better than to accept; they had had too much experience with Villalba's cooking.
　　I got somethin' ter discuss with you two," said Villalba, sitting himself between them and looking uncharacteristically serious.
　　"What?" said Roberto.
　　"Carolina," said Villalba.
　　"What about her?" said Diego.
　　"She's in a righ' state, that's what. She's bin comin' down ter visit me a lot since Chris'mas. Bin feelin' lonely. Firs' yeh weren' talking to her because o' the Firebolt, now yer not talkin' to her because her cat --"
　　"-- ate Scabbers!" Diego interjected angrily.
　　"Because her cat acted like all cats do," Villalba continued doggedly. "She's cried a fair few times, yeh know. Goin' through a rough time at the moment. Bitten off more'n she can chew, if yeh ask me, all the work she's tryin' ter do. Still found time ter help me with Buckbeak's case, mind.... She's found some really good stuff fer me... reckon he'll stand a good chance now..."
　　"Villalba, we should've helped as well -- sorry --" Roberto began awkwardly.
　　"I'm not blamin' yeh!" said Villalba, waving Roberto's apology aside. "Gawd knows yeh've had enough ter be gettin' on with. I've seen yeh practicin' Quidditch ev'ry hour o' the day an' night -- but I gotta tell yeh, I thought you two'd value yer friend more'n broomsticks or rats. Tha's all."
　　Roberto and Diego exchanged uncomfortable looks.
　　"Really upset, she was, when Martinez nearly stabbed yeh, Diego. She's got her heart in the right place, Carolina has, an' you two not talkin' to her --"
　　"If she'd just get rid of that cat, I'd speak to her again!" Diego said angrily. "But she's still sticking up for it! It's a maniac, and she won't hear a word against it!"
　　"Ah, well, people can be a bit stupid abou' their pets," said Villalba wisely. Behind him, Buckbeak spat a few ferret bones onto Villalba's pillow.
　　They spent the rest of their visit discussing Gryffindor's improved chances for the Quidditch Cup. At nine o'clock, Villalba walked them back up to the castle.
　　A large group of people was bunched around the bulletin board when they returned to the common room.
　　"Hogsmeade, next weekend!" said Diego, craning over the heads to read the new notice. "What d'you reckon?" he added quietly to Roberto as they went to sit down.
　　"Well, Filch hasn't done anything about the passage into Honeydukes...." Roberto said, even more quietly.
　　"Roberto!" said a voice in his right ear. Roberto started and looked around at Carolina, who was sitting at the table right behind them and clearing a space in the wall of books that had been hiding her.
　　"Roberto, if you go into Hogsmeade again... I'll tell Professor Romero about that map!" said Carolina.
　　"Can you hear someone talking, Roberto?" growled Diego, not looking at Carolina.
　　"Diego, how can you let him go with you? After what Gustavo Martinez nearly did to you! I mean it, I'll tell --"
　　"So now you're trying to get Roberto expelled!" said Diego furiously. "Haven't you done enough damage this year?"
　　Carolina opened her mouth to respond, but with a soft hiss, Crookshanks leapt onto her lap. Carolina took one frightened look at the expression on Diego's face, gathered up Crookshanks, and hurried away toward the girls' dormitories.
　　"So how about it?" Diego said to Roberto as though there had been no interruption. "Come on, last time we went you didn't see anything. You haven't even been inside Zonko's yet!"
　　Roberto looked around to check that Carolina was well out of earshot.
　　"Okay," he said. "But I'm taking the Invisibility Cloak this time."
　　On Saturday morning, Roberto packed his Invisibility Cloak in his bag, slipped the Marauder's Map into his pocket, and went down to breakfast with everyone else. Carolina kept shooting suspicious looks down the table at him, but he avoided her eye and was careful to let her see him walking back up the marble staircase in the entrance hall as everybody else proceeded to the front doors.
　　"'Bye!" Roberto called to Diego. "See you when you get back!"
　　Diego grinned and winked.
　　Roberto hurried up to the third floor, slipping the Marauder's Map out of his pocket as he went. Crouching behind the one-eyed witch, he smoothed it out. A tiny dot was moving in his direction. Roberto squinted at it. The minuscule writing next to it read Mauricio Silva.
　　Roberto quickly pulled out his wand, muttered, "Dissendium!" and shoved his bag into the statue, but before he could climb in himself, Mauricio came around the corner.
　　"Roberto! I forgot you weren't going to Hogsmeade either!"
　　"Hi, Mauricio," said Roberto, moving swiftly away from the statue and pushing the map back into his pocket. "What are you up to?"
　　"Nothing," shrugged Mauricio. "Want a game of Exploding Snap?"
　　"Er -- not now -- I was going to go to the library and do that vampire essay for Cardozo --"
　　"I'll come with you!" said Mauricio brightly. I haven't done it either!"
　　"Er -- hang on -- yeah, I forgot, I finished it last night!"
　　"Great, you can help me!" said Mauricio, his round face anxious. "I don't understand that thing about the garlic at all -- do they have to eat it, or --"
　　He broke off with a small gasp, looking over Roberto's shoulder.
　　It was Peralta. Mauricio took a quick step behind Roberto.
　　"And what are you two doing here?" said Peralta, coming to a halt and looking from one to the other. "An odd place to meet --"
　　To Roberto's immense disquiet, Peralta's black eyes flicked to the doorways on either side of them, and then to the one-eyed witch.
　　"We're not -- meeting here," said Roberto. "We just -- met here."
　　"Indeed?" said Peralta. "You have a habit of turning up in unexpected places, Gonzales, and you are very rarely there for no good reason.... I suggest the pair of you return to Gryffindor Tower, where you belong."
　　Roberto and Mauricio set off without another word. As they turned the corner, Roberto looked back. Peralta was running one of his hands over the one-eyed witch's head, examining it closely.
　　Roberto managed to shake Mauricio off at the Fat Lady by telling him the password, then pretending he'd left his vampire essay in the library and doubling back. Once out of sight of the security trolls, he pulled out the map again and held it close to his nose.
　　The third floor corridor seemed to be deserted. Roberto scanned the map carefully and saw, with a leap of relief, that the tiny dot labeled Carlos Peralta was now back in its office.
　　He sprinted back to the one-eyed witch, opened her hump, heaved himself inside, and slid down to meet his bag at the bottom of the stone chute. He wiped the Marauder's Map blank again, then set off at a run.
　　Roberto, completely hidden beneath the Invisibility Cloak, emerged into the sunlight outside Honeydukes and prodded Diego in the back.
　　It's me," he muttered.
　　"What kept you?" Diego hissed.
　　"Peralta was hanging around."
　　They set off up the High Street.
　　"Where are you?" Diego kept muttering out of the corner of his mouth. "Are you still there? This feels weird...."
　　They went to the post office; Diego pretended to be checking the price of an owl to Bill in Egypt so that Roberto could have a good look around. The owls sat hooting softly down at him, at least three hundred of them; from Great Grays right down to tiny little Scops owls ("Local Deliveries Only"), which were so small they could have sat in the palm of Roberto's hand.
　　Then they visited Zonko's, which was so packed with students Roberto had to exercise great care not to tread on anyone and cause a panic. There were jokes and tricks to fulfill even Pablo's and Luis's wildest dreams; Roberto gave Diego whispered orders and passed him some gold from under the cloak. They left Zonko's with their money bags considerably lighter than they had been on entering, but their pockets bulging with Dungbombs, Hiccup Sweets, Frog Spawn Soap, and a Nose-Biting Teacup apiece.
　　The day was fine and breezy, and neither of them felt like staying indoors, so they walked past the Three Broomsticks and climbed a slope to visit the Shrieking Shack, the most haunted dwelling in Britain. It stood a little way above the rest of the village, and even in daylight was slightly creepy, with its boarded windows and dank overgrown garden.
　　"Even the Hogwarts ghosts avoid it," said Diego as they leaned on the fence, looking up at it. "I asked Nearly Headless Nick... he says he's heard a very rough crowd lives here. No one can get in. Pablo and Luis tried, obviously, but all the entrances are sealed shut...."
　　Roberto, feeling hot from their climb, was just considering taking off the cloak for a few minutes when they heard voices nearby. Someone was climbing toward the house from the other side of the hill; moments later, Sosa had appeared, followed closely by Crabbe and Goyle. Sosa was speaking.
　　"... should have an owl from Father any time now. He had to go to the hearing to tell them about my arm... about how I couldn't use it for three months...."
　　Crabbe and Goyle sniggered.
　　"I really wish I could hear that great hairy moron trying to defend himself... 'There's no 'arm in 'im, 'onest that hippogriff's as good as dead --"
　　Sosa suddenly caught sight of Diego. His pale face split in a malevolent grin.
　　"What are you doing, Lopez?"
　　Sosa looked up at the crumbling house behind Diego.
　　"Suppose You'd love to live here, wouldn't you, Lopez? Dreaming about having your own bedroom? I heard your family all sleep in one room -- is that true?"
　　Roberto seized the back of Diego's robes to stop him from leaping on Sosa. "Leave him to me," he hissed in Diego's ear.
　　The opportunity was too perfect to miss. Roberto crept silently around behind Sosa, Crabbe, and Goyle, bent down, and scooped a large handful of mud out of the path.
　　"We were just discussing your friend Villalba," Sosa said to Diego. "Just trying to imagine what he's saying to the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures. D'you think he'll cry when they cut off his hippogriff's
　　SPLAT.
　　Sosa's head jerked forward as the mud hit him; his silverblond hair was suddenly dripping in muck.
　　"What the --?"
　　Diego had to hold onto the fence to keep himself standing, he was laughing so hard. Sosa, Crabbe, and Goyle spun stupidly on the spot, staring wildly around, Sosa trying to wipe his hair clean.
　　"What was that? 'Who did that?"
　　"Very haunted up here, isn't it?" said Diego, with the air of one commenting on the weather.
　　Crabbe and Goyle were looking scared. Their bulging muscles were no use against ghosts. Sosa was staring madly around at the deserted landscape.
　　Roberto sneaked along the path, where a particularly sloppy puddle yielded some foul-smelling, green sludge.
　　SPLATTER.
　　Crabbe and Goyle caught some this time. Goyle hopped furiously on the spot, trying to rub it out of his small, dull eyes.
　　"It came from over there!" said Sosa, wiping his face, and staring at a spot some six feet to the left of Roberto.
　　Crabbe blundered forward, his long arms outstretched like a zombie. Roberto dodged around him, picked up a stick, and lobbed it at Crabbe's back. Roberto doubled up with silent laughter as Crabbe did a kind of pirouette in midair, trying to see who had thrown it. As Diego was the only person Crabbe could see, it was Diego he started toward, but Roberto stuck out his leg. Crabbe stumbled -- and his huge, flat foot caught the hem of Roberto's cloak. Roberto felt a great tug, then the cloak slid off his face.
　　For a split second, Sosa stared at him.
　　"AAARGH!" he yelled, pointing at Roberto's head. Then he turned tail and ran, at breakneck speed, back down the hill, Crabbe and Goyle behind him.
　　Roberto tugged the cloak up again, but the damage was done.
　　"Roberto!" Diego said, stumbling forward and staring hopelessly at the point where Roberto had disappeared, "you'd better run for it! If Sosa tells anyone -- you'd better get back to the castle, quick --" "See you later," said Roberto, and without another word, he tore back down the path toward Hogsmeade.
　　Would Sosa believe what he had seen? Would anyone believe
