　　Sosa? Nobody knew about the Invisibility Cloak -- nobody except Dominguez. Roberto's stomach turned over -- Dominguez would know exactly what had happened, if Sosa said any- thing --
　　Back into Honeydukes, back down the cellar steps, across the stone floor, through the trapdoor -- Roberto pulled off the cloak, tucked it under his arm, and ran, flat out, along the passage.... Sosa would get back first... how long would it take him to find a teacher? Panting, a sharp pain in his side, Roberto didn't slow down until he reached the stone slide. He would have to leave the cloak where it was, it was too much of a giveaway in case Sosa had tipped off a teacher -- he hid it in a shadowy corner, then started to climb, fast as he could, his sweaty hands slipping on the sides of the chute. He reached the inside of the witch's hump, tapped it with his wand, stuck his head through, and hoisted himself out; the hump closed, and just as Roberto jumped out from behind the statue, he heard quick footsteps approaching.
　　It was Peralta. He approached Roberto at a swift walk, his black robes swishing, then stopped in front of him.
　　"So," he said.
　　There was a look of surpressed triumph about him. Roberto tried to look innocent, all too aware of his sweaty face and his muddy hands, which he quickly hid in his pockets.
　　"Come with me, Gonzales," said Peralta.
　　Roberto followed him downstairs, trying to wipe his hands clean on the inside of his robes without Peralta noticing. They walked down the stairs to the dungeons and then into Peralta's office.
　　Roberto had been in here only once before, and he had been in very serious trouble then too. Peralta had aquired a few more slimy horrible things in jars since last time, all standing on shelves behind his desk, glinting in the firelight and adding to the threatening atmosphere.
　　"Sit," said Peralta.
　　Roberto sat. Peralta, however, remained, standing.
　　"Mr. Sosa has just been to see me with a strange story, Gonzales," said Peralta.
　　Roberto didn't say anything.
　　"He tells me that he was up by the Shrieking Shack when he ran into Lopez -- apparently alone."
　　Still, Roberto didn't speak.
　　"Mr. Sosa states that he was standing talking to Lopez, when a large amount of mud hit him in the back of the head. How do you think that could have happened?"
　　Roberto tried to look mildly surprised.
　　"I don't know, Professor."
　　Peralta's eyes were boring into Roberto's. It was exactly like trying to stare down a hippogriff. Roberto tried hard not to blink.
　　"Mr. Sosa then saw an extraordinary apparition. Can you imagine what it might have been, Gonzales?"
　　"No," said Roberto, now trying to sound innocently curious.
　　"It was your head, Gonzales. Floating in midair."
　　There was a long silence.
　　"Maybe he'd better go to Madam Pomfrey," said Roberto. "If he's seeing things like --"
　　"What would your head have been doing in Hogsmeade, Gonzales?" said Peralta softly. "Your head is not allowed in Hogsmeade. No part of your body has permission to be in Hogsmeade."
　　"I know that," said Roberto, striving to keep his face free of guilt or fear. "It sounds like Sosa's having hallucin --"
　　"Sosa is not having hallucinations," snarled Peralta, and he bent down, a hand on each arm of Roberto's chair, so that their faces were a foot apart. "If your head was in Hogsmeade, so was the rest of you."
　　"I've been up in Gryffindor Tower," said Roberto. "Like you told --" "Can anyone confirm that?"
　　Roberto didn't say anything. Peralta's thin mouth curled into a horrible smile.
　　"So," he said, straightening up again. "Everyone from the Minister of Magic downward has been trying to keep famous Roberto Gonzales safe from Gustavo Martinez. But famous Roberto Gonzales is a law unto himself Let the ordinary people worry about his safety! Famous Roberto Gonzales goes where he wants to, with no thought for the consequences.
　　Roberto stayed silent. Peralta was trying to provoke him into telling the truth. He wasn't going to do it. Peralta had no proof -- yet.
　　"How extraordinarily like your father you are, Gonzales," Peralta said suddenly, his eyes glinting. "He too was exceedingly arrogant. A small amount of talent on the Quidditch field made him think he was a cut above the rest of us too. Strutting around the place with his friends and admirers... The resemblance between you is uncanny."
　　"My dad didn't strut," said Roberto, before he could stop himself. "And neither do I."
　　"Your father didn't set much store by rules either," Peralta went on, pressing his advantage, his thin face full of malice. "Rules were for lesser mortals, not Quidditch Cup-winners. His head was so swollen --"
　　"SHUT UP!"
　　Roberto was suddenly on his feet. Rage such as he had not felt since his last night in Privet Drive was coursing through him. He didn't care that Peralta's face had gone rigid, the black eyes flashing dangerously.
　　"What did you say to me, Gonzales?"
　　"I told you to shut up about my dad!" Roberto yelled. I know the truth, all right? He saved your life! Dominguez told me! You wouldn't even be here if it wasn't for my dad!"
　　Peralta's sallow skin had gone the color of sour milk.
　　"And did the headmaster tell you the circumstances in which your father saved my life?" he whispered. "Or did he consider the details too unpleasant for precious Gonzales's delicate ears?"
　　Roberto bit his lip. He didn't know what had happened and didn't want to admit it -- but Peralta seemed to have guessed the truth.
　　I would hate for you to run away with a false idea of your father, Gonzales," he said, a terrible grin twisting his face. "Have you been imagining some act of glorious heroism? Then let me correct you -- your saintly father and his friends played a highly amusing joke on me that would have resulted in my death if your father hadn't got cold feet at the last moment. There was nothing brave about what he did. He was saving his own skin as much as mine. Had their joke succeeded, he would have been expelled from Hogwarts."
　　Peralta's uneven, yellowish teeth were bared.
　　"Turn out your pockets, Gonzales!" he spat suddenly.
　　Roberto didn't move. There was a pounding in his ears.
　　"Turn out your pockets, or we go straight to the headmaster! Pull them out, Gonzales!"
　　Cold with dread, Roberto slowly pulled out the bag of Zonko's tricks and the Marauder's Map.
　　Snap picked up the Zonko's bag.
　　"Diego gave them to me," said Roberto, praying he'd get a chance to tip Diego off before Peralta saw him. "He -brought them back from Hogsmeade last time --"
　　"Indeed? And you've been carrying them around ever since? How very touching... and what is this?"
　　Peralta had picked up the map. Roberto tried with all his might to keep his face impassive.
　　"Spare bit of parchment," he said with a shrug.
　　Peralta turned it over, his eyes on Roberto.
　　"Surely you don't need such a very old piece of parchment?" he said. "Why don't I just -- throw this away?"
　　His hand moved toward the fire.
　　"No!" Roberto said quickly.
　　"So!" said Peralta, his long nostrils quivering. "Is this another treasured gift from Mr. Lopez? Or is it -- something else? A letter, perhaps, written in invisible ink? Or -- instructions to get into Hogsmeade without passing the dementors?"
　　Roberto blinked. Peralta's eyes gleamed.
　　"Let me see, let me see...." he muttered, taking out his wand and smoothing the map out on his desk. "Reveal your secret!" he said, touching the wand to the parchment.
　　Nothing happened. Roberto clenched his hands to stop them from shaking.
　　"Show yourself!" Peralta said, tapping the map sharply.
　　It stayed blank. Roberto was taking deep, calming breaths.
　　"Professor Carlos Peralta, master of this school, commands you to yield the information you conceal!" Peralta said, hitting the map with his wand.
　　As though an invisible hand were writing upon it, words appeared on the smooth surface of the map.
　　Mooney presents his compliments to Professor Peralta, and begs him to keep his abnormally large nose out of other people's business."
　　Peralta froze. Roberto stared, dumbstruck, at the message. But the map didn't stop there. More writing was appearing beneath the first.
　　"Mr. Prongs agrees with Mr. Moony and would like to add that Professor Peralta is an ugle git."
　　It would have been very funny if the situation hadn't been so serious. And there was more....
　　"Mr. Padfoot would like to register his astonishment that an idiot like that ever became a professor."
　　Roberto closed his eyes in horror. When he'd opened them, the map had had its last word.
　　"Mr. Wormtail bids Professor Peralta good day, and advises him to wash his hair , the slimeball."
　　Roberto waited for the blow to fall.
　　"So..." said Peralta softly. "We'll see about this...."
　　He strode across to his fire, seized a fistful of glittering powder from a jar on the fireplace, and threw it into the flames.
　　"Cardozo!" Peralta called into the fire. "I want a word!"
　　Utterly bewildered, Roberto stared at the fire. A large shape had appeared in it, revolving very fast. Seconds later, Professor Cardozo was clambering out of the fireplace, brushing ash off his shabby robes.
　　"You called, Carlos?" said Cardozo mildly.
　　"I certainly did," said Peralta, his face contorted with fury as he strode back to his desk. "I have just asked Gonzales to empty his pockets. He was carrying this."
　　Peralta pointed at the parchment, on which the words of Messrs. Moony, Wormtail, Padfoot, and Prongs were still shining. An odd, closed expression appeared on Cardozo's face.
　　"Well?" said Peralta.
　　Cardozo continued to stare at the map. Roberto had the impression that Cardozo was doing some very quick thinking.
　　"Well?" said Peralta again. "This parchment is plainly full of Dark Magic. This is supposed to be your area of expertise, Cardozo. Where do you imagine Gonzales got such a thing?"
　　Cardozo looked up and, by the merest half-glance in Roberto's direction, warned him not to interrupt.
　　"Full of Dark Magic?" he repeated mildly. "Do you really think so, Carlos? It looks to me as though it is merely a piece of parchment that insults anybody who reads it. Childish, but surely not dangerous? I imagine Roberto got it from a joke shop --"
　　"Indeed?" said Peralta. His jaw had gone rigid with anger. "You think a joke shop could supply him with such a thing? You don't think it more likely that he got it directly from the manufacturers?"
　　Roberto didn't understand what Peralta was talking about. Nor, apparently, did Cardozo.
　　"You mean, by Mr. Wormtail or one of these people?" he said. "Roberto, do you know any of these men?"
　　"No," said Roberto quickly.
　　"You see, Carlos?" said Cardozo, turning back to Peralta. "It looks like a Zonko product to me --"
　　Right on cue, Diego came bursting into the office. He was completely out of breath, and stopped just short of Peralta's desk, clutching the stitch in his chest and trying to speak.
　　"I -- gave -- Roberto -- that -- stuff," he choked. "Bought -- it... in Zonko's... ages -- ago..."
　　"Well!" said Cardozo, clapping his hands together and looking around cheerfully. "That seems to clear that up! Carlos, I'll take this back, shall I?" He folded the map and tucked it inside his robes. "Roberto, Diego, come with me, I need a word about my vampire essay -- excuse us, Carlos --"
　　Roberto didn't dare look at Peralta as they left his office. He. Diego, and Cardozo walked all the way back into the entrance hall before speaking. Then Roberto turned to Cardozo.
　　"Professor, I --"
　　"I don't want to hear explanations," said Cardozo shortly. He glanced around the empty entrance hall and lowered his voice. "I happen to know that this map was confiscated by Mr. Filch many years ago. Yes, I know it' s a map," he said as Roberto and Diego looked amazed. "I don't want to know how it fell into your possession. I am, however, astounded that you didn't hand it in. Particularly after what happened the last time a student left information about the castle lying around. And I can't let you have it back, Roberto."
　　Roberto had expected that, and was too keen for explanations to protest.
　　"Why did Peralta think I'd got it from the manufacturers?"
　　"Because...," Cardozo hesitated, "because these mapmakers would have wanted to lure you out of school. They'd think it extremely entertaining."
　　"Do you know them?" said Roberto, impressed.
　　"We've met," he said shortly. He was looking at Roberto more seriously than ever before.
　　"Don't expect me to cover up for you again, Roberto. I cannot make you take Gustavo Martinez seriously. But I would have thought that what you have heard when the dementors draw near you would have had more of an effect on you. Your parents gave their lives to keep you alive, Roberto. A poor way to repay them -- gambling their sacrifice for a bag of magic tricks."
　　He walked away, leaving Roberto feeling worse by far than he had at any point in Peralta's office. Slowly, he and Diego mounted the marble staircase. As Roberto passed the one-eyed witch, he remembered the Invisibility Cloak -- it was still down there, but he didn't dare go and get it.
　　"It's my fault," said Diego abruptly. "I persuaded you to go. Cardozo's right, it was stupid, we shouldn't've done it --"
　　He broke off; they reached the corridor where the security trolls were pacing, and Carolina was walking toward them. One look at her face convinced Roberto that she had heard what had happened. His heart plummeted -- had she told Professor Romero?
　　"Come to have a good gloat?" said Diego savagely as she stopped in front of them. "Or have you just been to tell on us?"
　　"No," said Carolina. She was holding a letter in her hands and her lip was trembling. "I just thought you ought to know... Villalba lost his case. Buckbeak is going to be executed."
　　CHAPTER FIFTEEN
　　THE QUIDDITCH FINAL
　　He sent me this," Carolina said, holding out the letter.
　　Roberto took it. The parchment was damp, and enormous teardrops had smudged the ink so badly in places that it was very difficult to read.
　　Dear Carolina, We lost. I'm allowed to bring him back to Hogwarts. Execution date to be fixed. Beaky has enjoyed London. I won't forget all the help you gave us.
　　Villalba
　　"They can't do this," said Roberto. "They can't. Buckbeak isn't dangerous."
　　"Sosa's dad's frightened the Committee into it," said Carolina, wiping her eyes. "You know what he's like. They're a bunch of doddery old fools, and they were scared. There'll be an appeal, though, there always is. Only I can't see any hope.... Nothing will have changed."
　　"Yeah, it will," said Diego fiercely. "You won't have to do all the work alone this time, Carolina. I'll help."
　　"Oh, Diego!"
　　Carolina flung her arms around Diego's neck and broke down completely. Diego, looking quite terrified, patted her very awkwardly on the top of the head. Finally, Carolina drew away.
　　"Diego, I'm really, really sorry about Scabbers..." she sobbed.
　　"Oh -- well -- he was old," said Diego, looking thoroughly relieved that she had let go of him. "And he was a bit useless. You never know, Mum and Dad might get me an owl now."
　　The safety measures imposed on the students since Martinez's second break-in made it impossible for Roberto, Diego, and Carolina to go and visit Villalba in the evenings. Their only chance of talking to him was during Care of Magical Creatures lessons.
　　He seemed numb with shock at the verdict.
　　"S'all my fault. Got all tongue-tied. They was all sittin' there in black robes an' I kep' droppin' me notes and forgettin' all them dates yeh looked up fer me, Carolina. An' then Mariano Sosa stood up an' said his bit, and the Committee jus' did exac'ly what he told 'em...."
　　"There's still the appeal!" said Diego fiercely. "Don't give up Yet, we're working on it!"
　　They were walking back up to the castle with the rest of the class. Ahead they could see Sosa, who was walking with Crabbe and Goyle, and kept looking back, laughing derisively.
　　"S'no good, Diego," said Villalba sadly as they reached the castle steps. "That Committee's in Mariano Sosa's pocket. I'm jus' gonna make sure the rest o' Beaky's time is the happiest he's ever had. I owe him that...."
　　Villalba turned around and hurried back toward his cabin, his face buried in his handkerchief.
　　"Look at him blubber!"
　　Sosa, Crabbe, and Goyle had been standing just inside the castle doors, listening.
　　"Have you ever seen anything quite as pathetic?" said Sosa. "And he's supposed to be our teacher!"
　　Roberto and Diego both made furious moves toward Sosa, but Carolina got there first -- SMACK!
　　She had slapped Sosa across the face with all the strength she could muster. Sosa staggered. Roberto, Diego, Crabbe, and Goyle stood flabbergasted as Carolina raised her hand again.
　　"Don't you dare call Villalba pathetic, you foul -- you evil --"
　　"Carolina!" said Diego weakly, and he tried to grab her hand as she swung it back.
　　"Get off, Diego!"
　　Carolina pulled out her wand. Sosa stepped backward. Crabbe and Goyle looked at him for instructions, thoroughly bewildered.
　　"C'mon," Sosa muttered, and in a moment, all three of them had disappeared into the passageway to the dungeons.
　　"Carolina!" Diego said again, sounding both stunned and irnpressed.
　　"Roberto, you'd better beat him in the Quidditch final!" Carolina said shrilly. "You just better had, because I can't stand it if Slytherin wins!"
　　"We're due in Charms," said Diego, still goggling at Carolina. "We'd better go."
　　They hurried up the marble staircase toward Professor Flitwick's classroom.
　　"You're late, boys!" said Professor Flitwick reprovingly as Roberto opened the classroom door. "Come along, quickly, wands out, we're experimenting with Cheering Charms today, we've already divided into pairs --"
　　Roberto and Diego hurried to a desk at the back and opened their bags. Diego looked behind him.
　　"Where's Carolina gone?"
　　Roberto looked around too. Carolina hadn't entered the classroom, yet Roberto knew she had been right next to him when he had opened the door.
　　"That's weird," said Roberto, staring at Diego. "Maybe -- maybe she went to the bathroom or something?"
　　But Carolina didn't turn up all lesson.
　　"She could've done with a Cheering Charm on her too," said Diego as the class left for lunch, all grinning broadly -- the Cheering Charms had left them with a feeling of great contentment.
　　Carolina wasn't at lunch either. By the time they had finished their apple pie, the after-effects of the Cheering Charms were wearing off, and Roberto and Diego had started to get slightly worried.
　　"You don't think Sosa did something to her?" Diego said anxiously as they hurried upstairs toward Gryffindor Tower.
　　They passed the security trolls, gave the Fat Lady the password ("Flibbertigibbet"), and scrambled through the portrait hole into the common room.
　　Carolina was sitting at a table, fast asleep, her head resting on an open Arithmancy book. They went to sit down on either side of her. Roberto prodded her awake.
　　"Wh -- what?" said Carolina, waking with a start and staring wildly around. "Is it time to go? W -- which lesson have we got now?"
　　"Divination, but it's not for another twenty minutes," said Roberto. "Carolina, why didn't you come to Charms?"
　　"What? Oh no!" Carolina squeaked. "I forgot to go to Charms!"
　　"But how could you forget?" said Roberto. "You were with us till we were right outside the classroom!"
　　"I don't believe it!" Carolina wailed. "Was Professor Flitwick angry? Oh, it was Sosa, I was thinking about him and I lost track of things!"
　　"You know what, Carolina?" said Diego, looking down at the enormous Arithmancy book Carolina had been using as a pillow. "I reckon you're cracking up. You're trying to do too much."
　　"No, I'm not!" said Carolina, brushing her hair out of her eyes and staring hopelessly around for her bag. "I just made a mistake, that's all! I'd better go and see Professor Flitwick and say sorry... I'll see you in Divination!"
　　Carolina joined them at the foot of the ladder to Professor Trelawneys classroom twenty minutes later, looking extremely harrassed.
　　"I can't believe I missed Cheering Charms! And I bet they come up in our exams; Professor Flitwick hinted they might!"
　　Together they climbed the ladder into the dim, stifling tower room. Glowing on every little table was a crystal ball full of pearly white mist. Roberto, Diego, and Carolina sat down together at the same rickety table.
　　"I thought we weren't starting crystal balls until next term," Diego muttered, casting a wary eye around for Professor Trelawney, in case she was lurking nearby.
　　"Don't complain, this means we've finished palmistry," Roberto muttered back. "I was getting sick of her flinching every time she looked at my hands."
　　"Good day to you!" said the familiar, misty voice, and Professor Trelawney made her usual dramatic entrance out of the shadows. Parvati and Lavender quivered with excitement, their faces lit by the milky glow of their crystal ball.
　　"I have decided to introduce the crystal ball a little earlier than I had planned," said Professor Trelawney, sitting with her back to the fire and gazing around. "The fates have informed me that your examination in June will concern the Orb, and I am anxious to give you sufficient practice."
　　Carolina snorted.
　　"Well, honestly... 'the fates have informed her' who sets the exam? She does! What an amazing prediction!" she said, not troubling to keep her voice low. Roberto and Diego choked back laughs.
　　It was hard to tell whether Professor Trelawney had heard them as her face was hidden in shadow. She continued, however, as though she had not.
　　"Crystal gazing is a particularly refined art," she said dreamily. "I do not expect any of you to See when first you peer into the Orb's infinite depths. We shall start by practicing relaxing the conscious mind and external eyes" -- Diego began to snigger uncontrollably and had to stuff his fist in his mouth to stifle the noise -- "so as to clear the Inner Eye and the superconscious. Perhaps, if we are lucky, some of you will see before the end of the class."
　　And so they began. Roberto, at least, felt extremely foolish, staring blankly at the crystal ball, trying to keep his mind empty when thoughts such as "this is stupid" kept drifting across it. It didn't help that Diego kept breaking into silent giggles and Carolina kept tutting.
　　"Seen anything yet?" Roberto asked them after a quarter of an hour's quiet crystal gazing.
　　"Yeah, there's a burn on this table," said Diego, pointing. "Someone's spilled their candle."
　　"This is such a waste of time," Carolina hissed. "I could be practicing something useful. I could be catching up on Cheering Charms --"
　　Professor Trelawney rustled past.
　　"Would anyone like me to help them interpret the shadowy portents within their Orb?" she murmured over the clinking of her bangles.
　　I don't need help," Diego whispered. "It's obvious what this means. There's going to be loads of fog tonight."
　　Both Roberto and Carolina burst out laughing.
　　"Now, really!" said Professor Trelawney as everyone's heads turned in their direction. Parvati and Lavender were looking scandalized. "You are disturbing the clairvoyant vibrations!" She approached their table and peered into their crystal ball. Roberto felt his heart sinking. He was sure he knew what was coming --
　　"There is something here!" Professor Trelawney whispered, lowerng her face to the ball, so that it was reflected twice in her huge glasses. "Something moving... but what is it?"
　　Roberto was prepared to bet everything he owned, Including his Firebolt, that it wasn't good news, whatever it was. And sure enough --
　　"My dear Professor Trelawney breathed, gazing up at Roberto. "It is here, plainer than ever before... my dear, stalking toward you, growing ever closer... the Gr --"
　　"Oh, for goodness' sake!" said Carolina loudly. "Not that ridiculous Grim again!"
　　Professor Trelawney raised her enormous eyes to Carolina's face. Parvati whispered something to Lavender, and they both glared at Carolina too. Professor Trelawney stood up, surveying Carolina with unmistakable anger.
　　"I am sorry to say that from the moment you have arrived in this class my dear, it has been apparent that you do not have what the noble art of Divination requires. Indeed, I don't remember ever meeting a student whose mind was so hopelessly mundane."
　　There was a moment's silence. Then --
　　"Fine!" said Carolina suddenly, getting up and cramming Unfogging the Future back into her bag. "Fine!" she repeated, swinging the bag over her shoulder and almost knocking Diego off his chair. "I give up! I'm leaving!"
　　And to the whole class's amazement, Carolina strode over to the trapdoor, kicked it open, and climbed down the ladder out of sight.
　　It took a few minutes for the class to settle down again. Professor Trelawney seemed to have forgotten all about the Grim. She turned abruptly from Roberto and Diego's table, breathing rather heavily as she tugged her gauzy shawl more closely to her.
　　"Ooooo!" said Lavender suddenly, making everyone start. "Ooooo, Professor Trelawney, I've just remembered! You saw her leaving, didn't you? Didn't you, Professor? 'Around Easter, one of our number will leave us forever!' You said it ages ago, Professor!"
　　Professor Trelawney gave her a dewy smile.
　　"Yes, my dear, I did indeed know that Miss Fernandez would be leaving us. One hopes, however, that one might have mistaken the Signs.... The Inner Eye can be a burden, you know..."
　　Lavender and Parvati looked deeply impressed, and moved over so that Professor Trelawney could join their table instead.
　　"Some day Carolina's having, eh?" Diego muttered to Roberto, looking awed.
　　"Yeah..."
　　Roberto glanced into the crystal ball but saw nothing but swirling white mist. Had Professor Trelawney really seen the Grim again? Would he? The last thing he needed was another near-fatal accident, with the Quidditch final drawing ever nearer.
　　The Easter holidays were not exactly relaxing. The third years had never had so much homework. Mauricio Silva seemed close to a nervous collapse, and he wasn't the only one.
　　"Call this a holiday!" Seamus Finnigan roared at the common room one afternoon. "The exams are ages away, what're they playing at?"
　　But nobody had as much to do as Carolina. Even without Divination, she was taking more subjects than anybody else. She was usually last to leave the common room at night, first to arrive at the library the next morning; she had shadows like Cardozo's under her eyes, and seemed constantly close to tears.
　　Diego had taken over responsibility for Buckbeak's appeal. When he wasn't doing his own work, he was poring over enormously thick volumes with names like The Handbook of Hippogriff Psychology and Fowl or Foul? A Study of Hippogriff Brutality. He was so absorbed, he even forgot to be horrible to Crookshanks.
　　Roberto, meanwhile, had to fit in his homework around Quidditch practice every day, not to mention endless discussions of tactics with Wood. The Gryffindor-Slytherin match would take place on the first Saturday after the Easter holidays. Slytherin was leading the tournament by exactly two hundred points. This meant (as Wood constantly reminded his team) that they needed to win the match by more than that amount to win the Cup. It also meant that the burden of winning fell largely on Roberto, because capturing the Snitch was worth one hundred and fifty points.
　　"So you must catch it only if we're more than fifty points up," Wood told Roberto constantly. "Only if we're more than fifty points up, Roberto, or we win the match but lose the Cup. You've got that, Haven't you? You must catch the Snitch only if we're --"
　　"I KNOW, OLIVER!" Roberto yelled.
　　The whole of Gryffindor House was obsessed with the coming match. Gryffindor hadn't won the Quidditch Cup since the legendary Charlie Lopez (Diego's second oldest brother) had been seeker. But Roberto doubted whether any of them, even Wood, wanted to win as much as he did. The enmity between Roberto and Sosa was at its highest point ever. Sosa was still smarting ,bout the mud-throwing incident in Hogsmeade and was even more furious that Roberto had somehow wormed his way out of punishment. Roberto hadn't forgotten Sosa's attempt to sabotage him in the match against Ravenclaw, but it was the matter of Buckbeak that made him most determined to beat Sosa in front of the entire school.
　　Never, in anyone's memory, had a match approached in such a highly charged atmosphere. By the time the holidays were over, tension between the two teams and their Houses was at the breaking point. A number of small scuffles broke out in the corridors, culminating in a nasty incident in which a Gryffindor fourth year and a Slytherin sixth year ended up in the hospital wing with leeks sprouting out of their ears.
　　Roberto was having a particularly bad time of it. He couldn't walk to class without Slytherins sticking out their legs and trying to trip him up; Crabbe and Goyle kept popping up wherever he went, and slouching away looking disappointed when they saw him surrounded by people. Wood had given instructions that Roberto should be accompanied everywhere he went, in case the Slytherins tried to put him out of action. The whole of Gryffindor House took up the challenge enthusiastically, so that it was impossible for Roberto to get to classes on time because he was surrounded by a vast, chattering crowd. Roberto was more concerned for his Firebolt's safety than his own. When he wasn't flying it, he locked it securely in his trunk and frequently dashed back up to Gryffindor Tower at break times to check that it was still there.
　　All usual pursuits were abandoned in the Gryffindor common room the night before the match. Even Carolina had Put down her books.
　　"I can't work, I can't concentrate," she said nervously.
　　There was a great deal of noise. Pablo and Luis Lopez were dealing with the pressure by being louder and more exuberant than ever. Oliver Wood was crouched over a model of a Quidditch field in the corner, prodding little figures across it with his wand and muttering to himself Angelina, Alicia, and Katie were laughing at Pablo's and Luis's jokes. Roberto was sitting with Diego and Carolina, removed from the center of things, trying not to think about the next day, because every time he did, he had the horrible sensation that something very large was fighting to get out of his stomach.
　　"You're going to be fine," Carolina told him, though she looked positively terrified.
　　"You've got a Firebolt!" said Diego.
　　"Yeah..." said Roberto, his stomach writhing.
　　It came as a relief when Wood suddenly stood up and yelled, "Team! Bed!"
　　Roberto slept badly. First he dreamed that he had overslept, and that Wood was yelling, "Where were you? We had to use Mauricio instead!" Then he dreamed that Sosa and the rest of the Slytherin team arrived for the match riding dragons. He was flying at breakneck speed, trying to avoid a spurt of flames from Sosa's steed's mouth, when he realized he had forgotten his Firebolt. He fell through the air and woke with a start.
　　It was a few seconds before Roberto remembered that the match hadn't taken place yet, that he was safe in bed, and that the Slytherin team definitely wouldn't be allowed to play on dragons. He was feeling very thirsty. Quietly as he could, he got out of his four-poster and went to pour himself some water from the silver jug beneath the window.
　　The grounds were still and quiet. No breath of wind disturbed the treetops in the Forbidden Forest; the Whomping Willow was motionless and innocent-looking. It looked as though the conditions for the match would be perfect.
　　Roberto set down his goblet and was about to turn back to his bed when something caught his eye. An animal of some kind was prowling across the silvery lawn.
　　Roberto dashed to his bedside table, snatched up his glasses, and put them on, then hurried back to the window. It couldn't be the Grim -- not now -- not right before the match -
　　He peered out at the grounds again and, after a minute's frantic searching, spotted it. It was skirting the edge of the forest now... It wasn't the Grim at all ... it was a cat.... Roberto clutched the window ledge in relief as he recognized the bottlebrush tail. It was only Crookshanks....
　　Or was it only Crookshanks? Roberto squinted, pressing his nose flat against the glass. Crookshanks seemed to have come to a halt. Roberto was sure he could see something else moving in the shadow of the trees too.
　　And just then, it emerged -- a gigantic, shaggy black dog, moving stealthily across the lawn, Crookshanks trotting at its side. Roberto stared. What did this mean? If Crookshanks could see the dog as well, how could it be an omen of Roberto's death?
　　"Diego!" Roberto hissed. "Diego! Wake up!"
　　"Huh?"
　　I need you to tell me if you can see something!"
　　"S'all dark, Roberto," Diego muttered thickly. "What're you or, about?"
　　"Down here --"
　　Roberto looked quickly back out of the window.
　　Crookshanks and the dog had vanished. Roberto climbed onto the windowsill to look right down into the shadows of the castle, but they weren't there. Where had they gone?
　　A loud snore told him Diego had fallen asleep again.
　　Roberto and the rest of the Gryffindor team entered the Great Hall the next day to enormous applause. Roberto couldn't help grinning broadly as he saw that both the Ravenclaw and Hufflepuff tables were applauding them too. The Slytherin table hissed loudly as they passed. Roberto noticed that Sosa looked even paler than usual.
　　Wood spent the whole of breakfast urging his team to eat, while touching nothing himself Then he hurried them off to the field before anyone else had finished, so they could get an idea of the conditions. As they left the Great Hall, everyone applauded again.
　　"Good luck, Roberto!" called Paula. Roberto felt himself blushing.
　　"Okay -- no wind to speak of -- sun's a bit bright, that could impair your vision, watch out for it -- ground's fairly hard, good, that'll give us a fast kickoff --"
　　Wood paced the field, staring around with the team behind him. Finally, they saw the front doors of the castle open in the distance and the rest of the school spilling onto the lawn.
　　"Locker rooms," said Wood tersely.
　　None of them spoke as they changed into their scarlet robes. Roberto wondered if they were feeling like he was: as though he'd eaten something extremely wriggly for breakfast. In what seemed like no time at all, Wood was saying, "Okay, it's time, let's go --"
　　They walked out onto the field to a tidal wave of noise. Threequarters of the crowd was wearing scarlet rosettes, waving scarlet flags with the Gryffindor lion upon them, or brandishing banners with slogans like "GO GRYFFINDOR!" and "LIONS FOR THE CUK' Behind the Slytherin goal posts, however, two hundred people were wearing green; the silver serpent of Slytherin glittered on their flags, and Professor Peralta sat in the very front row, wearing green like everyone else, and a very grim smile.
　　"And here are the Gryffindors!" yelled Lee Jordan, who was acting as commentator as usual. "Gonzales, Bell, Johnson, Spinnet, Lopez, Lopez, and Wood. Widely acknowledged as the best team Hogwarts has seen in a good few years --"
　　Lee's comments were drowned by a tide of "boos" from the Slytherin end.
　　"And here come the Slytherin team, led by Captain Flint. He's Made some changes in the lineup and seems to be going for size rather than skill --"
　　More boos from the Slytherin crowd. Roberto, however, thought Lee had a point. Sosa was easily the smallest person On the Slytherin team; the rest of them were enormous.
　　"Captains, shake hands!" said Madam Hooch.
　　Flint and Wood approached each other and grasped each other's hand very tightly; it looked as though each was trying to break the other's fingers.
　　"Mount your brooms!" said Madam Hooch. "Three... two... one..."
　　The sound of her whistle was lost in the roar from the crowd as fourteen brooms rose into the air. Roberto felt his hair fly back off his forehead; his nerves left him in the thrill of the flight; he glanced around, saw Sosa on his tail, and sped off in search of the Snitch.
　　"And it's Gryffindor in possession, Alicia Spinner of Gryffindor with the Quaffle, heading straight for the Slytherin goal posts, looking good, Alicia! Argh, no -- Quaffle intercepted by Warrington, Warrington of Slytherin tearing UP the field -- WHAM! -- nice Bludger work there by Luis Lopez, Warrington drops the Quaffle, it's caught by -- Johnson, Gryffindor back in possession, come on, Angelina -- nice swerve around Montague -- duck, Angelina, that's a Bludger!- SHE SCORES! TEN-ZERO TO GRYFFINDOR!"
　　Angelina punched the air as she soared around the end of the field; the sea of scarlet below was screaming its delight
　　"OUCH!"
　　Angelina was nearly thrown from her broom as Marcus Flint went smashing into her.
　　"Sorry!" said Flint as the crowd below booed. "Sorry, didn't see her!"
　　A moment later, Pablo Lopez chucked his Beater's club at the back of Flint's head. Flint's nose smashed into the handle of his broom and began to bleed.
　　"That will do!" shrieked Madam Hooch, zooming between then. "Penalty shot to Gryffindor for an unprovoked attack on their Chaser! Penalty shot to Slytherin for deliberate damage to their Chaser!"
　　"Come off it, Miss!" howled Pablo, but Madam Hooch blew her whistle and Alicia flew forward to take the penalty.
　　"Come on, Alicia!" yelled Lee into the silence that had descended on the crowd. "YES! SHE'S BEATEN THE KEEPER! TWENTY-ZERO TO GRYFFINDOR!"
　　Roberto turned the Firebolt sharply to watch Flint, still bleeding freely, fly forward to take the Slytherin penalty. Wood was hovering in front of the Gryffindor goal posts, his jaw clenched.
　　"'Course, Wood's a superb Keeper!" Lee Jordan told the crowd as Flint waited for Madam Hooch's whistle. "Superb! Very difficult to pass -- very difficult indeed -- YES! I DON'T BELIEVE IT! HE'S SAVED IT!"
　　Relieved, Roberto zoomed away, gazing around for the Snitch, but still making sure he caught every word of Lee's commentary. It was essential that he hold Sosa off the Snitch until Gryffindor was more than fifty points up --
　　"Gryffindor in possession, no, Slytherin in possession -- no!
　　Gryffindor back in possession and it's Katie Bell, Katie Bell for Gryffindor with the Quaffle, she's streaking up the field -- THAT WAS DELIBERATE!"
　　Montague, a Slytherin Chaser, had swerved in front of Katie, and instead of seizing the Quaffle had grabbed her head. Katie cart wheeled in the air, managed to stay on her broom, but dropped the Quaffle.
　　Madam Hooch's whistle rang out again as she soared over to Montague and began shouting at him. A minute later, Katie had put another penalty past the Slytherin Seeker.
　　"THIRTY-ZERO! TAKE THAT, YOU DIRTY, CHEATING --"
　　"Jordan, if you can't commentate in an unbiased way --"
　　"I'm telling it like it is, Professor!"
　　Roberto felt a huge jolt of excitement. He had seen the Snitch it was shimmering at the foot of one of the Gryffindor goal posts -- but he mustn't catch it yet -- and if Sosa saw it -
　　Faking a look of sudden concentration, Roberto pulled his Firebolt around and sped off toward the Slytherin end -- it worked. Sosa went haring after him, clearly thinking Roberto had seen the Snitch there....
　　WHOOSH.
　　One of the Bludgers came streaking past Roberto's right ear, hit by the gigantic Slytherin Beater, Derrick. Then again
　　WHOOSH.
　　The second Bludger grazed Roberto's elbow. The other Beater, Bole, was closing in.
　　Roberto had a fleeting glimpse of Bole and Derrick zooming toward him, clubs raised --
　　He turned the Firebolt upward at the last second, and Bole and Derrick collided with a sickening crunch.
　　"Ha haaa!" yelled Lee Jordan as the Slytherin Beaters lurched away from each other, clutching their heads. "Too bad, boys! You'll need to get up earlier than that to beat a Firebold And it's Gryffindor in possession again, as Johnson takes the Quaffle -- Flint alongside her -- poke him in the eye, Angelina! -- it was a joke, Professor, it was a joke -- oh no -- Flint in possession, Flint flying toward the Gryffindor goal posts, come on now, Wood, save --!"
　　But Flint had scored; there was an eruption of cheers from the Slytherin end, and Lee swore so badly that Professor Romero tried to tug the magical megaphone away from him.
　　"Sorry, Professor, sorry! WoiA happen again! So, Gryffindor in the lead, thirty points to ten, and Gryffindor in possession --"
　　it was turning into the dirtiest game Roberto had ever played in. Enraged that Gryffindor had taken such an early lead, the Slytherins were rapidly resorting to any means to take the Quaffle. Bole hit Alicia with his club and tried to say he'd thought she was a Bludger. Luis Lopez elbowed Bole in the face in retaliation. Madam Hooch awarded both teams penalties, and Wood pulled off another spectacular save, making the score forty-ten to Gryffindor.
　　The Snitch had disappeared again. Sosa was still keeping close to Roberto as he soared over the match, looking around for it once Gryffindor was fifty points ahead -
　　Katie scored. Fifty-ten. Pablo and Luis Lopez were swooping around her, clubs raised, in case any of the Slytherins were thinking of revenge. Bole and Derrick took advantage of Pablo's and Luis's absence to aim both Bludgers at Wood; they caught him in the stomach, one after the other, and he rolled over in the air, clutching his broom, completely winded.
　　Madam Hooch was beside herself
　　"YOU DO NOT ATTACK THE KEEPER UNLESS THE QUAFFLE IS WITHIN THE SCORING AREA!" she shrieked at Bole and Derrick. "Gryffindor penalty!"
　　And Angelina scored. Sixty-ten. Moments later, Pablo Lopez pelted a Bludger at Warrington, knocking the Quaffle Out of his hands; Alicia seized it and put it through the Slytherin goal -- seventy-ten.
　　The Gryffindor crowd below was screaming itself hoarse -- Gryffindor was sixty points in the lead, and if Roberto caught the Snitch now, the Cup was theirs. Roberto could almost feel hundreds of eyes following him as he soared around the field, high above the rest of the game, with Sosa speeding along behind him.
　　And then he saw it. The Snitch was sparkling twenty feet above him.
　　Roberto put on a huge burst of speed; the wind was roaring in his ears; he stretched out his hand, but suddenly, the Firebolt was slowing down --
　　Horrified, he looked around. Sosa had thrown himself forward, grabbed hold of the Firebolt's tail, and was pulling it back.
　　"You --"
　　Roberto was angry enough to hit Sosa, but couldn't reach -- Sosa was panting with the effort of holding onto the Firebolt, but his eyes were sparkling maliciously. He had achieved what he'd wanted to do -- the Snitch had disappeared again.
　　"Penalty! Penalty to Gryffindor! I've never seen such tactics." Madam Hooch screeched, shooting up to where Sosa was sliding back onto his Nimbus Two Thousand and One.
　　"YOU CHEATING SCUM!" Lee Jordan was howling into the megaphone, dancing out of Professor Romero's reach. "YOU FILTHY, CHEATING B --"
　　Pprofessor Romero didn't even bother to tell him off She was actually shaking her finger in Sosas direction, her hat had fallen off, and she too was shouting furiously.
　　Alicia took Gryffindor's penalty, but she was so angry she missed by several feet. The Gryffindor team was losing concentration and the Slytherins, delighted by Sosa's foul on Roberto, were being spurred on to greater heights.
　　"Slytherin in possession, Slytherin heading for goal -- Montague scores --" Lee groaned. "Seventy- twenty to Gryffindor..."
　　Roberto was now marking Sosa so closely their knees kept hitting each other. Roberto wasn't going to let Sosa anywhere near the Snitch....
　　"Get out of it, Gonzales!" Sosa yelled in frustration as he tried to turn and found Roberto blocking him.
　　"Angelina Johnson gets the Quaffle for Gryffindor, come on, Angelina, COME ON!"
　　Roberto looked around. Every single Slytherin player apart from Sosa was streaking up the pitch toward Angelina, including the Slytherin Keeper -- they were all going to block her --
　　Roberto wheeled the Firebolt around, bent so low he was lying flat along the handle, and kicked it forward. Like a bullet, he shot toward the Slytherins.
　　"AAAAAAARRRGH!"
　　They scattered as the Firebolt zoomed toward them; Angelina's Way was clear.
　　"SHE SCORES! SHE SCORES! Gryffindor leads by eighty Points to twenty!"
　　Roberto, who had almost pelted headlong into the stands, skidded to a halt in midair, reversed, and zoomed back into the middle of the field.
　　And then he saw something to make his heart stand still. Sosa was diving, a look of triumph on his face -- there, a few feet above the grass below, was a tiny, golden glimmer -
　　Roberto urged the Firebolt downward, but Sosa was miles ahead -
　　"Go! Go! Go!" Roberto urged his broom. He was gaining on Malfay -- Roberto flattened himself to the broom handle as Bole sent a Bludger at him -- he was at Sosa's ankles -- he was level --
　　Roberto threw himself forward, took both hands off his broom. He knocked Sosa's arm out of the way and --
　　"YES!"
　　He pulled out of his dive, his hand in the air, and the stadium exploded. Roberto soared above the crowd, an odd ringing in his ears. The tiny golden ball was held tight in his fist, beating its wings hopelessly against his fingers.
　　Then Wood was speeding toward him, half-blinded by tears; he seized Roberto around the neck and sobbed unrestrainedly into his shoulder. Roberto felt two large thumps as Pablo and Luis hit them; then Angelina's, Alicia's, and Katie's voices, "We've won the Cup! We've won the Cup!" Tangled together in a many-armed hug, the Gryffindor team sank, yelling hoarsely, back to earth.
　　Wave upon wave of crimson supporters was pouring over the barriers onto the field. Hands were raining down on their backs. Roberto had a confused impression of noise and bodies pressing in on him. Then he, and the rest of the team, were hoisted onto the shoulders of the crowd. Thrust into the light, he saw Villalba, Plastered with crimson rosettes -- "Yeh beat 'em, Roberto, yeh beat 'em!
　　Wait till I tell Buckbeak!" There was Miguel, jumping up and down like a maniac, all dignity forgotten. Professor Romero was sobbing harder even than Wood, wiping her eyes with an enormous Gryffindor flag; and there, fighting their way toward Roberto, were Diego and Carolina. Words failed them. They simply beamed as Roberto was borne toward the stands, where Dominguez stood waiting with the enormous Quidditch Cup.
　　If only there had been a dementor around.... As a sobbing Wood passed Roberto the Cup, as he lifted it into the air, Roberto felt he could have produced the world's best Patronus.
　　CHAPTER SIXTEEN
　　PROFESSOR TRELAWNEY'S PREDICTION
　　Roberto's euphoria at finally winning the Quidditch Cup lasted at least a week. Even the weather seemed to be celebrating; as June approached, the days became cloudless and sultry, and all anybody felt like doing was strolling onto the grounds and flopping down on the grass with several pints of iced pumpkin juice, perhaps playing a casual game of Gobstones or watching the giant squid propel itself dreamily across the surface of the lake.
　　But they couldn't. Exams were nearly upon them, and instead of lazing around outside, the students were forced to remain inside the castle, trying to bully their brains into concentrating while enticing wafts of summer air drifted in through the windows. Even Pablo and Luis Lopez had been spotted working; they were about to take their O.W.L.s (Ordinary Wizarding Levels). Miguel was getting ready to take his N.E.W.T.s (Nastily Exhausting Wizarding Tests), the highest qualification Hogwarts offered. As Miguel hoped to enter the Ministry of Magic, he needed top grades. He was becoming increasingly edgy, and gave very severe punishments to anybody who disturbed the quiet of the common room in the evenings. In fact, the only person who seemed more anxious than Miguel was Carolina.
　　Roberto and Diego had given up asking her how she was managing to attend several classes at once, but they couldn't restrain themselves when they saw the exam schedule she had drawn up for herself. The first column read:
　　Monday
　　9 o'clock, Arithmancy
　　9 o'clock, Transfiguration
　　Lunch
　　1 o'clock, Charms
　　1 o'clock, Ancient Runes
　　"Carolina?" Diego said cautiously, because she was liable to explode when interrupted these days. "Er -- are you sure you've copied down these times right?"
　　"What?" snapped Carolina, picking up the exam schedule and examining it. "Yes, of course I have."
　　"Is there any point asking how you're going to sit for two exams at once?" said Roberto.
　　"No," said Carolina shortly. "Have either of you seen my copy of Numerology and Gramatica?"
　　"Oh, yeah, I borrowed it for a bit of bedtime reading," said Diego, but very quietly. Carolina started shifting heaps of parchment Roberto, Diego, and Carolina plenty of opportunity to speak to Villalba.
　　"Beaky's gettin' a bit depressed," Villalba told them, bending low on the pretense of checking that Roberto's flobberworm was still alive. "Bin cooped up too long. But still... we'll know day after tomorrow -- one way or the other --"
　　They had Potions that afternoon, which was an unqualified disaster. Try as Roberto might, he couldn't get his Confusing Concoction to thicken, and Peralta, standing watch with an air of vindictive pleasure, scribbled something that looked suspiciously like a zero onto his notes before moving away.
　　Then came Astronomy at midnight, up on the tallest tower; History of Magic on Wednesday morning, in which Roberto scribbled everything Florean Fortescue had ever told him about medieval witch-hunts, while wishing he could have had one of Fortescue's choco-nut sundaes with him in the stifling classroom. Wednesday afternoon meant Herbology, in the greenhouses under a baking-hot sun; then back to the common room once more, with sunburnt necks, thinking longingly of this time next day, when it would all be over.
　　Their second to last exam, on Thursday morning, was Defense Against the Dark Arts. Professor Cardozo had compiled the most unusual exam any of them had ever taken; a sort of obstacle course outside in the sun, where they had to wade across a deep paddling pool containing a grindylow, cross a series of potholes full of Red Caps, squish their way across a patch of marsh while ignoring misleading directions from a hinkypunk, then climb into an old trunk and battle with a new boggart.
　　"Excellent, Roberto," Cardozo muttered as Roberto climbed out of the trunk, grinning. "Full marks."
　　Flushed with his success, Roberto hung around to watch Diego and Carolina. Diego did very well until he reached the hinkypunk, which successfully confused him into sinking waist-high into the quagmire. Carolina did everything perfectly until she reached the trunk with the boggart in it. After about a minute inside it, she burst out again, screaming.
　　"Carolina!" said Cardozo, startled. "What's the matter?"
　　"P -- P -- Professor Romero!" Carolina gasped, pointing into the trunk. "Sh -- she said I'd failed everything!"
　　It took a little while to calm Carolina down. When at last she had regained a grip on herself, she, Roberto, and Diego went back to the castle. Diego was still slightly inclined to laugh at Carolina's boggart, but an argument was averted by the sight that met them on the top of the steps.
　　Cornelius Fudge, sweating slightly in his pinstriped cloak, was standing there staring out at the grounds. He started at the sight of Roberto.
　　"Hello there, Roberto!" he said. "Just had an exam, I expect? Nearly finished?"
　　"Yes," said Roberto. Carolina and Diego, not being on speaking terms with the Minister of Magic, hovered awkwardly in the background.
　　"Lovely day," said Fudge, casting an eye over the lake.
　　"Pity... pity..."
　　He sighed deeply and looked down at Roberto.
　　"I'm here on an unpleasant mission, Roberto. The Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures required a witness to the execution of a mad hippogriff. As I needed to visit Hogwarts to check on the Martinez situation, I was asked to step in."
　　"Does that mean the appeal's already happened?" Diego interrupted, stepping forward.
　　"No, no, it's scheduled for this afternoon," said Fudge, looking curiously at Diego.
　　"Then you might not have to witness an execution at A!" said Eon stoutly. "The hippogriff might get off!"
　　Before Fudge could answer, two wizards came through the castle doors behind him. One was so ancient he appeared to be withering before their very eyes; the other was tall and strapping, with a thin back mustache. Roberto gathered that they were representatives of the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures, because tie very old wizard squinted toward Villalba's cabin and said in a feeble voice, "Dear, dear, I'm getting too old for this.... Two o'clock, isn't it, Fudge?"
　　The black-mustached man was fingering something in his belt; Roberto looked and saw that he was running one broad thumb along the blade of a shining axe. Diego opened his mouth to say something, but Carolina nudged him hard in the ribs and jerked her head toward the entrance hall.
　　"Why'd you stop me?" said Diego angrily as they entered the Great Hall for lunch. "Did you see them? They've even got the axe ready! This isn't justice!"
　　"Diego, your dad works for the Ministry, you can't go saying things like that to his boss!" said Carolina, but she too looked very upset. "As long as Villalba keeps his head this time, and argue, hi case properly, they can't possibly execute Buckbeak...."
　　But Roberto could tell Carolina didn't really believe what she was saying. All around them, people were talking excitedly as they ate their lunch, happily anticipating the end of the exams that afternoon, but Roberto, Diego, and Carolina, lost in worry about Villalba and Buckbeak, didn't join in.
　　Roberto's and Diego's last exam was Divination; Carolina's, Muggle Studies. They walked up the marble staircase together; Carolina left them on the first floor and Roberto and Diego proceeded all the way up to the seventh, where many of their class were sitting on the spiral staircase to Professor Trelawney's classroom, trying to cram in a bit of last-minute studying.
　　"She's seeing us all separately," Mauricio informed them as they went to sit down next to him. He had his copy of Unfogging the Future open on his lap at the pages devoted to crystal gazing. "Have either of you ever seen anything in a crystal ball?" he asked them unhappily.
　　"Nope," said Diego in an offhand voice. He kept checking his watch; Roberto. knew that he was counting down the time until Buckbeak's appeal started.
　　The line of people outside the classroom shortened very slowly. As each person climbed back down the silver ladder, the rest of the class hissed, "What did she ask? Was it okay?"
　　But they all refused to say.
　　"She says the crystal ball's told her that if I tell you, I'll have a horrible accident!" squeaked Mauricio as he clambered back down the ladder toward Roberto and Diego, who had now reached the landing.
　　"That's convenient," snorted Diego. "You know, I'm starting to think Carolina was right about her" -- he jabbed his thumb toward the trapdoor overhead -- "she's a right old fraud."
　　"Yeah," said Roberto, looking at his own watch. It-was now two o'clock. "Wish she'd hurry up..."
　　Parvati came back down the ladder glowing with pride.
　　"She says I've got all the makings of a true Seer," she informed Roberto and Diego. "I saw loads of stuff... Well, good luck!"
　　She hurried off down the spiral staircase toward Lavender.
　　"Diegoald Lopez," said the familiar, misty voice from over their heads. Diego grimaced at Roberto and climbed the silver ladder out of sight. Roberto was now the only person left to be tested. He settled himself on the floor with his back against the wall, listening to a fly buzzing in the sunny window, his mind across the grounds with Villalba.
　　Finally, after about twenty minutes, Diego's large feet reappeared on the ladder.
　　"How'd it go?" Roberto asked him, standing up.
　　"Rubbish," said Diego. "Couldn't see a thing, so I made some stuff up. Don't think she was convinced, though...."
　　"Meet you in the common room," Roberto muttered as Professor Trelawney's voice called, "Roberto Gonzales!"
　　The tower room was hotter than ever before; the curtains were closed, the fire was alight, and the usual sickly scent made Roberto cough as he stumbled through the clutter of chairs and table to where Professor Trelawney sat waiting for him before a large crystal ball.
　　"Good day, my dear," she said softly. "If you would kindly gaze into the Orb.... Take your time, now... then tell me what you see within it...."
　　Roberto bent over the crystal ball and stared, stared as hard as he could, willing it to show him something other than swirling white fog, but nothing happened.
　　"Well?" Professor Trelawney prompted delicately. "What do you see?"
　　The heat was overpowering and his nostrils were stinging with the perfumed smoke wafting from the fire beside them. He thought of what Diego had just said, and decided to pretend.
　　"Er --" said Roberto, "a dark shape... um..."
　　"What does it resemble?" whispered Professor Trelawney. "Think, now..."
　　Roberto cast his mind around and it landed on Buckbeak.
　　"A hippogriff," he said firmly.
　　"Indeed!" whispered Professor Trelawney, scribbling keenly on the parchment perched upon her knees. "My boy, you may well be seeing the outcome of poor Villalba's trouble with the Ministry of Magic! Look closer... Does the hippogriff appear to... have its head?"
　　"Yes," said Roberto firmly.
　　"Are you sure?" Professor Trelawney urged him. "Are you quite sure, dear? You don't see it writhing on the ground, perhaps, and a shadowy figure raising an axe behind it?"
　　"No!" said Roberto, starting to feel slightly sick.
　　"No blood? No weeping Villalba?"
　　"No!" said Roberto again, wanting more than ever to leave the room and the heat. "It looks fine, it's - - flying away..."
　　Professor Trelawney sighed.
　　"Well, dear, I think we'll leave it there.... A little disappointing... but I'm sure you did your best."
　　Relieved, Roberto got up, picked up his bag and turned to go, but then a loud, harsh voice spoke behind him.
　　"IT WILL HAPPEN TONIGHT."
　　Roberto wheeled around. Professor Trelawney had gone rigid in her armchair; her eyes were unfocused and her mouth sagging.
　　"S -- sorry?" said Roberto.
　　But Professor Trelawney didn't seem to hear him. Her eyes started to roll. Roberto sat there in a panic. She looked as though she was about to have some sort of seizure. He hesitated, thinking of running to the hospital wing -- and then Professor Trelawney spoke again, in the same harsh voice, quite unlike her own:
　　"THE DARK LORD LIES ALONE AND FRIENDLESS, ABANDONED BY HIS FOLLOWERS. HIS SERVANT HAS BEEN CHAINED THESE TWELVE YEARS. TONIGHT, BEFORE MIDNIGHT... THE SERVANT WILL BREAK FREE AND SET OUT TO REJOIN HIS MASTER. THE DARK LORD WILL RISE AGAIN WITH HIS SERVANTS AID, GREATER AND MORE TERRIBLE THAN EVER HE WAS. TONIGHT... BEFORE MIDNIGHT... THE SERVANT... WILL SET OU... TO REJOIN... HIS MASTER....
　　Professor Trelawney's head fell forward onto her chest. She made a grunting sort of noise. Roberto sat there, staring at her. Then, quite suddenly, Professor Trelawney's head snapped up again.
　　"I'm so sorry, dear boy," she said dreamily, "the heat of the day, you know... I drifted off for a moment...."
　　Roberto sat there, staring at her.
　　"Is there anything wrong, my dear?"
　　"You -- you just told me that the -- the Dark Lord's going to rise again... that his servant's going to go back to him.
　　Professor Trelawney looked thoroughly startled.
　　"The Dark Lord? He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named? My dear boy, that's hardly something to joke about.... Rise again, indeed --"
　　,'But you just said it! You. said the Dark Lord --"
　　"I think you must have dozed off too, dear!" said Professor Trelawney. "I would certainly not presume to predict anything quite as far-fetched as that!"
　　Roberto climbed back down the ladder and the spiral staircase, wondering... had he just heard Professor Trelawney make a real prediction? Or had that been her idea of an impressive end to the test?
　　Five minutes later he was dashing past the security trolls outside the entrance to Gryffindor Tower, Professor Trelawney's words still resounding in his head. People were striding past him in the opposite direction, laughing and joking, heading for the grounds and a bit of long-awaited freedom; by the time he had reached the portrait hole and entered the common room, it was almost deserted. Over in the corner, however, sat Diego and Carolina.
　　"Professor Trelawney," Roberto panted, "just told me --"
　　But he stopped abruptly at the sight of their faces.
　　"Buckbeak lost," said Diego weakly. "Villalba's just sent this."
　　Villalba's note was dry this time, no tears had splattered it, yet his hand seemed to have shaken so much as he wrote that it was hardly legible.
　　Lost appeal. They're going to execute at sunset. Nothing you can do. Don't come down. I don't want you to see it.
　　Villalba
　　"We've got to go," said Roberto at once. "He can't just sit there on his own, waiting for the executioner!"
　　"Sunset, though," said Diego, who was staring out the window ill a glazed sort of way. "We'd never be allowed... 'specially you, Roberto...."
　　Roberto sank his head into his hands, thinking.
　　"If we only had the Invisibility Cloak...."
　　"Where is it?" said Carolina.
　　Roberto told her about leaving it in the passageway under the one-eyed witch.
　　"... if Peralta sees me anywhere near there again, I'm in serious trouble," he finished.
　　"That's true," said Carolina, getting to her feet. "If he sees you.... How do you open the witch's hump again?"
　　"You -- you tap it and say, 'Dissendium,'" said Roberto. "But --"
　　Carolina didn't wait for the rest of his sentence; she strode across the room, pushed open the Fat Lady's portrait and vanished from sight.
　　"She hasn't gone to get it?" Diego said, staring after her.
　　She had. Carolina returned a quarter of an hour later with the silvery cloak folded carefully under her robes.
　　"Carolina, I don't know what's gotten, into you lately!" said Diego, astounded. "First you hit Sosa, then you walk out on Professor Trelawney --"
　　Carolina looked rather flattered.
　　They went down to dinner with everybody else, but did not return to Gryffindor Tower afterward. Roberto had the cloak hidden down tie front of his robes; he had to keep his arms folded to hide the lump. They skulked in an empty chamber off the entrance hall, listening, until they were sure it was deserted. They heard a last pair of people hurrying across the hall and a door slamming. Carolina poked her head around the door.
　　"Okay," she whispered, "no one there -- cloak on --"
　　Walking very close together so that nobody would see them, they crossed the hall on tiptoe beneath the cloak, then walked down the stone front steps into the grounds. The sun was already sinking behind the Forbidden Forest, gilding the top branches of the trees.
　　They reached Villalba's cabin and knocked. He was a minute in answering, and when he did, he looked all around for his visitor, pale-faced and trembling.
　　"It's us," Roberto hissed. "We're wearing the Invisibility Cloak. Let us in and we can take it off."
　　"Yeh shouldn've come!" Villalba whispered, but he stood back, and they stepped inside. Villalba shut the door quickly and Roberto pulled off the cloak.
　　Villalba was not crying, nor did he throw himself upon their necks. He looked like a man who did not know where he was or what to do. This helplessness was worse to watch than tears.
　　"Wan' some tea?" he said. His great hands were shaking as he reached for the kettle.
　　"Where's Buckbeak, Villalba?" said Carolina hesitantly.
　　I -- I took him outside," said Villalba, spilling milk all over the table as he filled up the jug. "He's tethered in me pumpkin patch. Thought he oughta see the trees an' -- an' smell fresh air -- before
　　Villalba's hand trembled so violently that the milk jug slipped from his grasp and shattered all over the floor.
　　"I'll do it, Villalba," said Carolina quickly, hurrying over and starting to clean up the mess.
　　"There's another one in the cupboard," Villalba said, sitting down and wiping his forehead on his sleeve. Roberto glanced at Diego, who looked back hopelessly.
　　"Isn't there anything anyone can do, Villalba?" Roberto asked fiercely, sitting down next to him. "Dominguez --"
　　"He's tried," said Villalba. "He's got no power ter overrule the Committee. He told 'em Buckbeak's all right, but they're scared.... Yeh know what Mariano Sosa's like... threatened 'em, I expect... an' the executioner, Macnair, he's an old pal o' Sosa's... but it'll be quick an' clean... an' I'll be beside him.... "
　　Villalba swallowed. His eyes were darting all over the cabin as though looking for some shred of hope or comfort.
　　"Dominguez's gonna come down while it -- while it happens. Wrote me this mornin'. Said he wants ter -- ter be with me. Great man, Dominguez...."
　　Carolina, who had been rummaging in Villalba's cupboard for another milk jug, let out a small, quickly stifled sob. She straightened up with the new jug in her hands, fighting back tears.
　　"We'll stay with you too, Villalba," she began, but Villalba shook his shaggy head.
　　"Yeh're ter go back up ter the castle. I told yeh, I don' wan' yeh watchin'. An' yeh shouldn' be down here anyway... If Fudge an' Dominguez catch yeh out without permission, Roberto, yeh'll be in big trouble."
　　Silent tears were now streaming down Carolina's face, but she hid them from Villalba, bustling around making tea. Then, as she picked up the milk bottle to pour some into the jug, she let out a shriek.
　　"Diego, I don't believe it -- it's Scabbers!"
　　Diego gaped at her.
　　"What are you talking about?"
　　Carolina carried the milk jug over to the table and turned it upside down. With a frantic squeak, and much scrambling to get back inside, Scabbers the rat came sliding out onto the table.
　　"Scabbers!" said Diego blankly. "Scabbers, what are you doing here?"
　　He grabbed the struggling rat and held him up to the light. Scabbers looked dreadful. He was thinner than ever, large tufts of hair had fallen out leaving wide bald patches, and he writhed in Diego's hands as though desperate to free himself
　　"It's okay, Scabbers!" said Diego. "No cats! There's nothing here to hurt you!"
　　Villalba suddenly stood up, his eyes fixed on the window. His normally ruddy face had gone the color of parchment.
　　"They're comin'...."
　　Roberto, Diego, and Carolina whipped around. A group of men was walking down the distant castle steps. In front was Alfonso Dominguez, his silver beard gleaming in the dying sun. Next to him trotted Cornelius Fudge. Behind them came the feeble old Committee member and the executioner, Macnair.
　　"Yeh gotta go," said Villalba. Every inch of him was trembling. "They mustn' find yeh here.... Go now..."
　　Diego stuffed Scabbers into his pocket and Carolina picked up the cloak. "I'll let yeh out the back way," said Villalba.
　　They followed him to the door into his back garden. Roberto felt strangely unreal, and even more so when he saw Buckbeak a few yards away, tethered to a tree behind Villalba's Pumpkin patch. Buckbeak seemed to know something was happening. He turned his sharp head from side to side and pawed the ground nervously.
　　"It's okay, Beaky," said Villalba softly. "It's okay..." He turned to Roberto, Diego, and Carolina. "Go on," he said. "Get goin'."
　　But they didn't move.
　　"Villalba, we can't --"
　　"We'll tell them what really happened --"
　　"They can't kill him --"
　　"Go!" said Villalba fiercely. "It's bad enough without you lot in trouble an' all!"
　　They had no choice. As Carolina threw the cloak over Roberto and Diego, they heard voices at the front of the cabin. Villalba looked at the place where they had just vanished from sight.
　　"Go quick," he said hoarsely. "Don' listen...."
　　And he strode back into his cabin as someone knocked at the front door.
　　Slowly, in a kind of horrified trance, Roberto, Diego, and Carolina set off silently around Villalba's house. As they reached the other side, the front door closed with a sharp snap.
　　"Please, let's hurry," Carolina whispered. "I can't stand it, I can't bear it...."
　　They started up the sloping lawn toward the castle. The sun was sinking fast now; the sky had turned to a clear, purple-tinged grey, but to the west there was a ruby-red glow.
　　Diego stopped dead.
　　"Oh, please, Diego," Carolina began.
　　"It's Scabbers -- he won't -- stay put --"
　　Diego was bent over, trying to keep Scabbers in his pocket, but the rat was going berserk; squeaking madly, twisting and flailing, trying to sink his teeth into Diego's hand.
　　"Scabbers, it's me, you idiot, it's Diego," Diego hissed.
　　They heard a door open behind them and men's voices.
　　"Oh, Diego, please let's move, they're going to do it!" Carolina breathed.
　　"Okay -- Scabbers, stay put --"
　　They walked forward; Roberto, like Carolina, was trying not to listen to the rumble of voices behind them. Diego stopped again.
　　"I can't hold him -- Scabbers, shut up, everyone'll hear us --"
　　The rat was squealing wildly, but not loudly enough to cover up the sounds drifting from Villalba's garden. There was a jumble of indistinct male voices, a silence, and then, without warning, the unmistakable swish and thud of an axe.
　　Carolina swayed on the spot.
　　"They did it!" she whispered to Roberto. "I d -- don't believe it -- they did it!"
　　CHAPTER SEVENTEEN
　　CAT, RAT, AND DOG
　　Roberto's mind had gone blank with shock. The three of them stood transfixed with horror under the Invisibility Cloak. The very last rays of the setting sun were casting a bloody light over the long- shadowed grounds. Then, behind them, they heard a wild howling.
　　"Villalba," Roberto muttered. Without thinking about what he was doing, he made to turn back, but both Diego and Carolina seized his arms.
　　"We can't," said Diego, who was paper-white. "He'll be in worse trouble if they know we've been to see him...."
　　Carolina's breathing was shallow and uneven.
　　"How -- could -- they?" she choked. "How could they?"
　　"Come on," said Diego, whose teeth seemed to be chattering.
　　They set off back toward the castle, walking slowly to keep themselves hidden under the cloak. The light was fading fast now.
　　By the time they reached open ground, darkness was settling like a spell around them.
　　"Scabbers, keep still," Diego hissed, clamping his hand over his chest. The rat was wriggling madly. Diego came to a sudden halt, trying to force Scabbers deeper into his pocket. "What's the matter with you, You stupid rat? Stay still -- OUCH! He bit me!"
　　"Diego, be quiet!" Carolina whispered urgently. "Fudge'll be out here in a minute --"
　　"He won't -- stay -- put --"
　　Scabbers was plainly terrified. He was writhing with all his might, trying to break free of Diego's grip.
　　"What's the matter with him?"
　　But Roberto had just seen -- stinking toward them, his body low to the ground, wide yellow eyes glinting eerily in the darkness -- Crookshanks. Whether he could see them or was following the sound of Scabbers's squeaks, Roberto couldn't tell.
　　"Crookshanks!" Carolina moaned. "No, go away, Crookshanks! Go away!"
　　But the cat was getting nearer --
　　"Scabbers -- NO!"
　　Too late -- the rat had slipped between Diego's clutching fingers, hit the ground, and scampered away. In one bound, Crookshanks sprang after him, and before Roberto or Carolina could stop him, Diego had thrown the Invisibility Cloak off himself and pelted away into the darkness.
　　"Diego!" Carolina moaned.
　　She and Roberto looked at each other, then followed at a sprint; it ""as impossible to run full out under the cloak; they pulled it off and it streamed behind them like a banner as they hurtled after Diego; they could hear his feet thundering along ahead and his shouts at Crookshanks.
　　"Get away from him -- get away -- Scabbers, come here --"
　　There was a loud thud.
　　"Gotcha! Get off, you stinking cat --"
　　Roberto and Carolina almost fell over Diego; they skidded to a stop right in front of him. He was sprawled on the ground, but Scabbers was back in his pocket; he had both hands held tight over the quivering lump.
　　"Diego -- come on back under the cloak --" Carolina panted. "Dominguez the Minister -- they'll be coming back out in a minute --"
　　But before they could cover themselves again, before they could even catch their breath, they heard the soft pounding of gigantic paws.... Something was bounding toward them, quiet as a shadow -- an enormous, pale-eyed, jet-black dog.
　　Roberto reached for his wand, but too late -- the dog had made an enormous leap and the front paws hit him on the chest; he keeled over backward in a whirl of hair; he felt its hot breath, saw inch- long teeth -
　　But the force of its leap had carried it too far; it rolled off him. Dazed, feeling as though his ribs were broken, Roberto tried to stand up; he could hear it growling as it skidded around for a new attack.
　　Diego was on his feet. As the dog sprang back toward them he pushed Roberto aside; the dog's jaws fastened instead around Diego's outstretched arm. Roberto lunged forward, he seized a handful of the brute's hair, but it was dragging Diego away as easily as though he were a rag doll --
　　Then, out of nowhere, something hit Roberto so hard across the face he was knocked off his feet again. He heard Carolina shriek with pain and fall too.
　　Roberto groped for his wand, blinking blood out of his eyes
　　"Lumos!"he whispered.
　　The wandlight showed him the trunk of a thick tree; they had chased Scabbers into the shadow of the Whomping Willow and its branches were creaking as though in a high wind, whipping backward and forward to stop them going nearer.
　　And there, at the base of the trunk, was the dog, dragging Diego backward into a large gap in the roots -- Diego was fighting furiously, but his head and torso were slipping out of sight --
　　"Diego!" Roberto shouted, trying to follow, but a heavy branch whipped lethally through the air and he was forced backward again.
　　All they could see now was one of Diego's legs, which he had hooked around a root in an effort to stop the dog from pulling him farther underground -- but a horrible crack cut the air like a gunshot; Diego's leg had broken, and a moment later, his foot vanished from sight.
　　"Roberto -- we've got to go for help --" Carolina gasped; she was bleeding too; the Willow had cut her across the shoulder.
　　"No! That thing's big enough to eat him; we haven't got time --"
　　"Roberto -- we're never going to get through without help --"
　　Another branch whipped down at them, twigs clenched like knuckles.
　　"If that dog can get in, we can," Roberto panted, darting here and there, trying to find a way through the vicious, swishing branches, but he couldn't get an inch nearer to the tree roots without being in range of the tree's blows.
　　"Oh, help, help," Carolina whispered frantically, dancing U._ certainly on the spot, "Please..."
　　Crookshanks darted forward. He slithered between the battering branches like a snake and placed his front paws upon a knot on the trunk.
　　Abruptly, as though the tree had been turned to marble, it stopped moving. Not a leaf twitched or shook.
　　"Crookshanks!" Carolina whispered uncertainly. She now grasped Roberto's arm painfully hard. "How did he know --?"
　　"He's friends with that dog," said Roberto grimly. "I've seen them together. Come on -- and keep your wand out --"
　　They covered the distance to the trunk in seconds, but before they had reached the gap in the roots, Crookshanks had slid into it with a flick of his bottlebrush tail. Roberto went next; he crawled forward, headfirst, and slid down an earthy slope to the bottom of a very low tunnel. Crookshanks was a little way along, his eyes flashing in the light from Roberto's wand. Seconds later, Carolina slithered down beside him.
　　"Where's Diego?" she whispered in a terrified voice.
　　"This way," said Roberto, setting off, bent-backed, after Crookshanks.
　　"Where does this tunnel come out?" Carolina asked breathlessly from behind him.
　　"I don't know... It's marked on the Marauder's Map but Pablo and Luis said no one's ever gotten into it.... It goes off the edge of the map, but it looked like it was heading for Hogsmeade..."
　　They moved as fast as they could, bent almost double; ahead of them, Crookshanks's tail bobbed in and out of view. On and on went the passage; it felt at least as long as the one to Honeydukes.... All Roberto could think of was Diego and what the enormous dog might be doing to him.... He was drawing breath in sharp, painful gasps, running at a crouch....
　　And then the tunnel began to rise; moments later it twisted, and Crookshanks had gone. instead, Roberto could see a patch of dim light through a small opening.
　　He and Carolina paused, gasping for breath, edging forward. Both raised their wands to see what lay beyond.
　　It was a room, a very disordered, dusty room. Paper was peeling from the walls; there were stains all over the floor; every piece of furniture was broken as though somebody had smashed it. The windows were all boarded up.
　　Roberto glanced at Carolina, who looked very frightened but nodded.
　　Roberto pulled himself out of the hole, staring around. The room was deserted, but a door to their right stood open, leading to a shadowy hallway. Carolina suddenly grabbed Roberto's arm again. Her wide eyes were traveling around the boarded windows.
　　"Roberto," she whispered, "I think we're in the Shrieking Shack."
　　Roberto looked around. His eyes fell on a wooden chair near them. Large chunks had been torn out of it; one of the legs had been ripped off entirely.
　　"Ghosts didn't do that," he said slowly.
　　At that moment, there was a creak overhead. Something had Moved upstairs. Both of them looked up at the ceiling. Carolina's grip on Roberto's arm was so tight he was losing feeling in-his fingers. He raised his eyebrows at her; she nodded again and let go.
　　Quietly as they could, they crept out into the hall and UP the crumbling staircase. Everything was covered in a thick layer of dust except the floor, where a wide shiny stripe had been made by something being dragged upstairs.
　　They reached the dark landing.
　　"Nox," they whispered together, and the lights at the end of their wands went out. Only one door was open. As they crept toward it, they heard movement from behind it; a low moan, and then a deep, loud purring. They exchanged a last look, a last nod.
　　Wand held tightly before him, Roberto kicked the door wide open.
　　On a magnificent four-poster bed with dusty hangings lay Crookshanks, purring loudly at the sight of them. On the floor beside him, clutching his leg, which stuck out at a strange angle, was Diego.
　　Roberto and Carolina dashed across to him.
　　"Diego -- are you okay?"
　　"Where's the dog?"
　　"Not a dog," Diego moaned. His teeth were gritted with pain. "Roberto, it's a trap --"
　　"What --"
　　"He's the dog... he's an Animagus."
　　Diego was staring over Roberto's shoulder. Roberto wheeled around. With a snap, the man in the shadows closed the door behind them.
