　　A mass of filthy, matted hair hung to his elbows. If eyes hadn't been shining out of the deep, dark sockets, he might have been a corpse. The waxy skin was stretched so tightly over the bones of his face, it looked like a skull. His yellow teeth were bared in a grin. It was Gustavo Martinez.
　　"Expelliarmus!"he croaked, pointing Diego's wand at them.
　　Roberto's and Carolina's wands shot out of their hands, high in the air, and Martinez caught them. Then he took a step closer. His eyes were fixed on Roberto.
　　"I thought you'd come and help your friend," he said hoarsely.
　　His voice sounded as though he had long since lost the habit of using it. "Your father would have done the same for me. Brave of you) not to run for a teacher. I'm grateful... it will make everything much easier...."
　　The taunt about his father rang in Roberto's ears as though Martinez had bellowed it. A boiling hate erupted in Roberto's chest, leaving no place for fear. For the first time in his life, he wanted his wand back in his hand, not to defend himself, but to attack... to kill. Without knowing what he was doing, he started forward, but there was a sudden movement on either side of him and two pairs of hands grabbed him and held him back.... "No, Roberto!" Carolina gasped in a petrified whisper; Diego, however, spoke to Martinez.
　　"If you want to kill Roberto, you'll have to kill us too!" he said fiercely, though the effort of standing upright was draining him of still more color, and he swayed slightly as he spoke.
　　Something flickered in Martinez's shadowed eyes.
　　"Lie down," he said quietly to Diego. "You will damage that leg even more."
　　"Did you hear me?" Diego said weakly, though he was clinging painfully to Roberto to stay upright. "You'll have to kill all three of us!"
　　"There'll be only one murder here tonight," said Brack, and his grin widened.
　　"Why's that?" Roberto spat, trying to wrench himself free of Diego, and Carolina. "Didn't care last time, did you? Didn't mind slaughtering all those Muggles to get at Salazar... What's the matter, gone soft in Azkaban?"
　　"Roberto!" Carolina whimpered. "Be quiet!"
　　"HE KILLED MY MUM AND DAD!" Roberto roared, and with a huge effort he broke free of Carolina's and Diego's restraint and lunged forward -
　　He had forgotten about magic -- he had forgotten that he was short and skinny and thirteen, whereas Martinez was a tall, full-grown man -- all Roberto knew was that he wanted to hurt Martinez as badly as he could and that he didn't care how much he got hurt in return --
　　Perhaps it was the shock of Roberto doing something so stupid, but Martinez didn't raise the wands in time -- one of Roberto's hands fastened over his wasted wrist, forcing the wand tips away; the knuckles of Roberto's other hand collided with the side of Martinez's head and they fell, backward, into the wall -
　　Carolina was screaming; Diego was yelling; there was a blinding flash as the wands in Martinez's hand sent a jet of sparks into the air that missed Roberto's face by inches; Roberto felt the shrunken arm under his fingers twisting madly, but he clung on, his other hand punching every part of Martinez it could find.
　　But Martinez's free hand had found Roberto's throat
　　"No," he hissed, "I've waited too long --"
　　The fingers tightened, Roberto choked, his glasses askew.
　　Then he saw Carolina's foot swing out of nowhere. Martinez let go of Roberto with a grunt of pain; Diego had thrown himself on Martinez's wand hand and Roberto heard a faint clatter --
　　He fought free of the tangle of bodies and saw his own wand rolling across the floor; he threw himself toward it but
　　"Argh!"
　　Crookshanks had joined the fray; both sets of front claws had sunk themselves deep into Roberto's arm; Roberto threw him off, but Crookshanks now darted toward Roberto's wand --
　　"NO YOU DON'T!" roared Roberto, and he aimed a kick at Crookshanks that made the cat leap aside, spitting; Roberto snatched up his wand and turned -
　　"Get out of the way!" he shouted at Diego and Carolina.
　　They didn't need telling twice. Carolina, gasping for breath, her lip bleeding, scrambled aside, snatching up her and Diego's wands. Diego crawled to the four-poster and collapsed onto it, panting, his white face now tinged with green, both hands clutching his broken leg.
　　Martinez was sprawled at the bottom of the wall. His thin chest rose and fell rapidly as he watched Roberto walking slowly nearer, his wand pointing straight at Martinez's heart.
　　"Going to kill me, Roberto?" he whispered.
　　Roberto stopped right above him, his wand still pointing at Martinez's chest, looking down at him. A livid bruise was rising around Martinez's left eye and his nose was bleeding.
　　"You killed my parents," said Roberto, his voice shaking slightly, but his wand hand quite steady.
　　Martinez stared up at him out of those sunken eyes.
　　"I don't deny it," he said very quietly. "But if you knew the whole story."
　　"The whole story?" Roberto repeated, a furious pounding in his ears. "You sold them to Salvador. That's all I need to know."
　　"You've got to listen to me," Martinez said, and there was a note of urgency in his voice now. "You'll regret it if you don't.... You don't understand...."
　　"I understand a lot better than you think," said Roberto, and his voice shook more than ever. "You never heard her, did you? My mum... trying to stop Salvador killing me... and you did that... you did it...."
　　Before either of them could say another word, something ginger streaked past Roberto; Crookshanks leapt onto Martinez's chest and settled himself there, right over Martinez's heart. Martinez blinked and looked down at the cat.
　　"Get off," he murmured, trying to push Crookshanks off him.
　　But Crookshanks sank his claws into Martinez's robes and wouldn't shift. He turned his ugly, squashed face to Roberto and looked up at him with those great yellow eyes. To his right, Carolina gave a dry sob.
　　Roberto stared down at Martinez and Crookshanks, his grip tightening on the wand. So what if he had to kill the cat too? It was in league with Martinez.... If it was prepared to die, trying to protect Martinez, that wasn't Roberto's business.... If Martinez wanted to save it, that only proved he cared more for Crookshanks than for Roberto's parents....
　　Roberto raised the wand. Now was the moment to do it. Now was the moment to avenge his mother and father. He was going to kill Martinez. He had to kill Martinez. This was his chance....
　　The seconds lengthened. And still Roberto stood frozen there, wand poised, Martinez staring up at him, Crookshanks on his chest. Diego's ragged breathing came from near the bed; Carolina was quite silent.
　　And then came a new sound -
　　Muffled footsteps were echoing up through the floor -- someone was moving downstairs.
　　"WE'RE UP HERE!" Carolina screamed suddenly. "WE'RE UP HERE -- GUSTAVO MARTINEZ - QUICK!"
　　Martinez made a startled movement that almost dislodged Crookshanks; Roberto gripped his wand convulsively -- Do it now! said a voice in his head -- but the footsteps were thundering up the stairs and Roberto still hadn't done it.
　　The door of the room burst open in a shower of red sparks and Roberto wheeled around as Professor Cardozo came hurtling into the room, his face bloodless, his wand raised and ready. His eyes flickered over Diego, lying on the floor, over Carolina, cowering next to the door, to Roberto, standing there with his wand covering Martinez, and then to Martinez himself, crumpled and bleeding at Roberto's feet.
　　"Expelliarmus!" Cardozo shouted.
　　Roberto's wand flew once more out of his hand; so did the two Carolina was holding. Cardozo caught them all deftly, then moved into the room, staring at Martinez, who still had Crookshanks lying Protectively across his chest.
　　Roberto stood there, feeling suddenly empty. He hadn't done it. His nerve had failed him. Martinez was going to be handed back to the dementors.
　　Then Cardozo spoke, in a very tense voice.
　　"Where is he, Gustavo?"
　　Roberto looked quickly at Cardozo. He didn't understannd what Cardozo meant. Who was Cardozo talking about? He turned to look at Martinez again.
　　Martinez's face was quite expressionless. For a few seconds, he didn't move at all. Then, very slowly, he raised his empty hand and pointed straight at Diego. Mystified, Roberto glanced around at Diego, who looked bewildered.
　　"But then..." Cardozo muttered, staring at Martinez so intently it seemed he was trying to read his mind, "... why hasn't he shown himself before now? Unless" -- Cardozo's eyes suddenly widened, as though he was seeing something beyond Martinez, something none of the rest could see, "-- unless he was the one... unless you switched... without telling me?"
　　Very slowly, his sunken gaze never leaving Cardozo's face, Martinez nodded.
　　"Professor," Roberto interrupted loudly, "what's going on --?"
　　But he never finished the question, because what he saw made his voice die in his throat. Cardozo was lowering his wand, gazing fixed at Martinez. The Professor walked to Martinez's side, seized his hand, pulled him to his feet so that Crookshanks fell to the floor, and embraced Martinez like a brother.
　　Roberto felt as though the bottom had dropped out of his stomach.
　　"DON'T BELIEVE IT!" Carolina screamed.
　　Cardozo let go of Martinez and turned to her. She had raised herself off the floor and was pointing at Cardozo, wild-eyed. "You -- you --"
　　"Carolina --"
　　"-- you and him!"
　　"Carolina, calm down --"
　　"I didn't tell anyone!" Carolina shrieked. "I've been covering up for you --"
　　"Carolina, listen to me, please'" Cardozo shouted. "I can explain --"
　　Roberto could feel himself shaking, not with fear, but with a fresh wave of fury.
　　"I trusted you," he shouted at Cardozo, his voice wavering, out of control, "and all the time you've been his friend!"
　　"You're wrong," said Cardozo. "I haven't been Gustavo's friend, but I am now -- Let me explain...."
　　"NO!" Carolina screamed. "Roberto, don't trust him, he's been helping Martinez get into the castle, he wants you dead too -- he's a werewolf!"
　　There was a ringing silence. Everyone's eyes were now on Cardozo, who looked remarkably calm, though rather pale.
　　"Not at all up to your usual standard, Carolina," he said. "Only one out of three, I'm afraid. I have not been helping Gustavo get into the castle and I certainly don't want Roberto dead. An odd shiver passed over his face. "But I won't deny that I am a werewolf."
　　Diego made a valiant effort to get up again but fell back with a whimper of pain. Cardozo made toward him, looking concerned, but Diego gasped, "Get away ftom me, werewolf!"
　　Cardozo stopped dead. Then, with an obvious effort, he turned to Carolina and said, "How long have you known?"
　　"Ages," Carolina whispered. "Since I did Professor Peralta's essay..."
　　"He'll be delighted," said Cardozo coolly. "He assigned that essay hoping someone would realize what my symptoms meant.... Did you check the lunar chart and realize that I was always ill at the full moon? Or did you realize that the boggart changed into the moon when it saw me?"
　　"Both," Carolina said quietly.
　　Cardozo forced a laugh.
　　"You're the cleverest witch of your age I've ever met, Carolina."
　　"I'm not," Carolina whispered. "If I'd been a bit cleverer, I'd have told everyone what you are!"
　　"But they already know," said Cardozo. "At least, the staff do."
　　"Dominguez hired you when he knew you were a werewolf. Diego gasped. "Is he mad?"
　　"Some of the staff thought so," said Cardozo. "He had to work very hard to convince certain teachers that I'm trustworthy --"
　　"AND HE WAS WDIEGOG!" Roberto yelled. "YOUVE BEEN HELPING HIM ALL THE TIME!" He was pointing at Martinez, who suddenly crossed to the four-poster bed and sank onto it, his face hidden in one shaking hand. Crookshanks leapt up beside him and stepped onto his lap, purring. Diego edged away from both of them, dragging his leg.
　　I have not been helping Gustavo," said Cardozo. "If you'll give me a chance, I'll explain. Look --"
　　He separated Roberto's, Diego's and Carolina's wands and threw each back to its owner; Roberto caught his, stunned.
　　There, said Cardozo, sticking his own wand back into his belt "You're armed, we're not. Now will you listen?"
　　Roberto didn't know what to think. Was it a trick?
　　"If you haven't been helping him," he said, with a furious glance at Martinez, "how did you know he was here?"
　　"The map," said Cardozo. "The Marauder's Map. I was in my office examining it --"
　　"You know how to work it?" Roberto said suspiciously.
　　"Of course I know how to work it," said Cardozo, waving his hand impatiently. "I helped write it. I'm Moony -- that was my friends' nickname for me at school."
　　"You wrote --?"
　　"The important thing is, I was watching it carefully this evening, because I had an idea that you, Diego, and Carolina might try and sneak out of the castle to visit Villalba before his hippogriff was executed. And I was right, wasn't I"
　　He had started to pace up and down, looking at them. Little patches of dust rose at his feet.
　　"You might have been wearing your father's old cloak, Roberto--"
　　"How d'you know about the cloak?"
　　"The number of times I saw Ricardo disappearing under it...," said Cardozo, waving an impatient hand again. "The point is, even if you're wearing an Invisibility Cloak, you still show up on the Marauder's Map. I watched you cross the grounds and enter Villalba's hut. Twenty minutes later, you left Villalba, and set off back toward the castle. But you were now accompanied by somebody else."
　　"What?" said Roberto. "No, we weren't!"
　　I couldn't believe my eyes," said Cardozo, still pacing, and ignoring Roberto's interruption. "I thought the map must be malfunctioning. How could he be with you?" "No one was with us!" said Roberto.
　　"And then I saw another dot, moving fast toward you, labeled Gustavo Martinez.... I saw him collide with you; I watched as he pulled two of you into the Whomping Willow --"
　　"One of us!" Diego said angrily.
　　"No, Diego," said Cardozo. "Two of you."
　　He had stopped his pacing, his eyes moving over Diego.
　　"Do you think I could have a look at the rat?" he said evenly.
　　"What?" said Diego. "What's Scabbers got to do with it?"
　　"Everything," said Cardozo. "Could I see him, please?"
　　Diego hesitated, then put a hand inside his robes. Scabbers emerged, thrashing desperately; Diego had to seize his long bald tail to stop him escaping. Crookshanks stood up on Martinez's leg and made a soft hissing noise.
　　Cardozo moved closer to Diego. He seemed to be holding his breath as he gazed intently at Scabbers.
　　"What?" Diego said again, holding Scabbers close to him, looking scared. "What's my rat got to do with anything?"
　　"That's not a rat," croaked Gustavo Martinez suddenly.
　　"What d'you mean -- of course he's a rat --"
　　"No, he's not," said Cardozo quietly. "He's a wizard."
　　"An Animagus," said Martinez, "by the name of Gonzalo Salazar."
　　CHAPTER EIGHTEEN
　　MOONY, WORMTAIL, PADDFOOT, AND PDIEGOGS
　　It took a few seconds for the absurdity of this statement to sink in. Then Diego voiced what Roberto was thinking.
　　"You're both mental."
　　"Ridiculous!" said Carolina faintly.
　　"Gonzalo Salazar's dead!" said Roberto. "He killed him twelve years ago!" He pointed at Martinez, whose face twitched convulsively.
　　"I meant to," he growled, his yellow teeth bared, "but little Gonzalo got the better of me... not this time, though!"
　　And Crookshanks was thrown to the floor as Martinez lunged at Scabbers; Diego yelled with pain as Martinez's weight fell on his broken leg.
　　."Gustavo, NO!" Cardozo yelled, launching himself forwards and dragging Martinez away from Diego again, "WAIT! You can't do it just like that -- they need to understand -- we've got to explain --"
　　"We can explain afterwards!" snarled Martinez, trying to throw Cardozo off. One hand was still clawing the air as it tried to reach Scabbers, who was squealing like a piglet, scratching Diego's face and neck as he tried to escape.
　　"They've -- got -- a -- right -- to -- know -- -everything!" Cardozo panted, still trying to restrain Martinez. "Diego's kept him as a pet! There are parts of it even I don't understand, and Roberto -- you owe Roberto the truth, Gustavo!"
　　Martinez stopped struggling, though his hollowed eyes were still fixed on Scabbers, who was clamped tightly under Diego's bitten, scratched, ad bleeding hands.
　　"All right, then," Martinez said, without taking his eyes off the rat.
　　"Tell them whatever you like. But make it quick, Pedro. I want to commit the murder I was imprisoned for..."
　　"You're nutters, both of you," said Diego shakily, looking round at Roberto and Carolina for support. "I've had enough of this. I'm off."
　　He tried to heave himself up on his good leg, but Cardozo raised his wand again, pointing it at Scabbers.
　　"You're going to hear me out, Diego," he said quietly. "Just keep a tight hold on Gonzalo while you listen."
　　"HE'S NOT GONZALO, HE'S SCABBERS!" Diego yelled, trying to fore the rat back into his front pocket, but Scabbers was fighting to hard; Diego swayed and overbalanced, and Roberto caught him am pushed him back down to the bed. Then, ignoring Martinez, Roberto turned to Cardozo.
　　There were witnesses who saw Salazar die," he said. "A whole street full of them..."
　　"They didn't see what they thought they saw!" said Martinez savagely, still watching Scabbers struggling in Diego's hands.
　　"Everyone thought Gustavo killed Gonzalo," said Cardozo, nodding. "I believed it myself -- until I saw the map tonight. Because the Marauder's map never lies... Gonzalo's alive. Diego's holding him, Roberto."
　　Roberto looked down at Diego, and as their eyes met, they agreed, silently: Martinez and Cardozo were both out of their minds. Their story made no sense whatsoever. How could Scabbers be Gonzalo Salazar? Azkaban must have unhinged Martinez after all -- but why was Cardozo playing along with him?
　　Then Carolina spoke, in a trembling, would-be calm sort of voice, as though trying to will Professor Cardozo to talk sensibly.
　　"But Professor Cardozo... Scabbers can't be Salazar... it just can't be true, you know it can't..."
　　"Why can't it be true?" Cardozo said calmly, as though they were in class, and Carolina had simply spotted a problem in an experiment with grindylows.
　　"Because... because people would know if Gonzalo Salazar had been an Animagus. We did Animagi in class with Professor Romero. And I looked them up when I did my homework -- the Ministry of Magic keeps tabs on witches and wizards who can become animals; there's a register showing what animal they become, and their markings and things... and I went and looked Professor Romero up on the register, and there have been only seven Animagi this century, and Salazar's name wasn't on the list."
　　Roberto had barely had time to marvel inwardly at the effort Carolina put into her homework, when Cardozo started to laugh.
　　"Light again, Carolina!" he said. "But the Ministry never knew that here used to be three unregistered Animagi running around Hogwarts."
　　"I you're going to tell them the story, get a move on, Pedro," said Martinez, who was still watching Scabbers's every desperate move. "I've waited twelve years, I'm not going to wait much longer."
　　"All right... but you'll need to help me, Gustavo," said Cardozo, I only know how it began..."
　　Cardozo broke off. There had been a loud creak behind him. The bedroom door had opened of its own accord. All five of them stared at it. Then Cardozo strode toward it and looked out into the landing.
　　"No one there..."
　　"This place is haunted!" said Diego.
　　"It's not," said Cardozo, still looking at the door in a puzzled way. "The Shrieking Shack was never haunted.... The screams and howls the villagers used to hear were made by me."
　　He pushed his graying hair out of his eyes, thought for a moment then said, "That's where all of this starts -- with my becoming a werewolf, None of this could have happened if I hadn't been bitter... and if I hadn't been so foolhardy..."
　　He looked sober and tired. Diego started to interrupt, but Carolina, said, "Shh!" She was watching Cardozo very intently.
　　"I as a very small boy when I received the bite. My parents tried everything, but in those days there was no cure. The potion that Professor Peralta has been making for me is a very recent discovery. It makes me safe, you see. As long as I take it in the week, preceding the full moon, I keep my mind when I transform.... I'm able to curl up in my office, a harmless wolf, and wait for the moon to wane again.
　　"Before the Wolfsbane Potion was discovered, however, I became a fully fledged monster once a month. It seemed impossible that I would be able to come to Hogwarts. Other parents weren't likely to want their children exposed to me.
　　"But then Dominguez became Headmaster, and he was sympathetic. He said that as long as we took certain precautions, there was no reason I shouldn't come to school...." Cardozo sighed, and looked directly at Roberto. "I told you, months ago, that the Whomping Willow was planted the year I came to Hogwarts. The truth is that it was planted because I came to Hogwarts. This house" -- Cardozo looked miserably around the room, -- "the tunnel that leads to it -- they were built for my use. Once a month, I was smuggled out of the castle, into this place, to transform. The tree was placed at the tunnel mouth to stop anyone coming across me while I was dangerous."
　　Roberto couldn't see where this story was going, but he was listening raptly all the same. The only sound apart from Cardozo's voice was Scabbers's frightened squeaking.
　　"My transformations in those days were -- were terrible. It is very painful to turn into a werewolf. I was separated from humans to bite, so I bit and scratched myself instead. The villagers heard the noise and the screaming and thought they were hearing particularly violent spirits. Dominguez encouraged the rumor.... Even now, when the house has been silent for years, the villagers don't dare approach it...."
　　"But apart from my transformations, I was happier than I had ever been in my life. For the first time ever, I had friends, three great friends. Gustavo Martinez... Gonzalo Salazar... and, of course, your father, Roberto -- Ricardo Gonzales."
　　"Now, my three friends could hardly fail to notice that I disappeared once a month. I made up all sorts of stories. I told them my mother was ill, and that I had to go home to see her... I was terrified they would desert me the moment they found out what I was. But of course, they, like you, Carolina, worked out the truth...."
　　"And they didn't desert me at all. Instead, they did something for me that would make my transformations not only bearable, but the best times of my life. They became Animagi."
　　"My dad too?" said Roberto, astounded.
　　"Yes, indeed," said Cardozo. "It took them the best part of three years to work out how to do it. Your father and Gustavo here were the cleverest students in the school, and lucky they were, because the Animagus transformation can go horribly wrong -- one reason the Ministry keeps a close watch on those attempting to do it. Gonzalo needed all the help he could get from Ricardo and Gustavo. Finally, in our fifth year, they managed it. They could each turn into a different animal at will."
　　"But how did that help you?" said Carolina, sounding puzzled.
　　"They couldn't keep me company as humans, so they kept me company as animals," said Cardozo. "A werewolf is only a danger to people. They sneaked out of the castle every month under Ricardo's Invisibility Cloak. They transformed... Gonzalo, as the smallest, could slip beneath the Willow's attacking branches and touch the knot that freezes it. They would then slip down the tunnel and join me. Under their influence, I became less dangerous. My body was still wolfish, but my mind seemed to become less so while I was with them."
　　"Hurry up, Pedro," snarled Martinez, who was still watching Scabbers with a horrible sort of hunger on his face.
　　"I'm getting there, Gustavo, I'm getting there... well, highly exciting possibilities were open to us now that we could all transform. Soon we were leaving the Shrieking Shack and roaming the school grounds and the village by night. Gustavo and Ricardo transformed into such large animals, they were able to keep a werewolf in check. I doubt whether any Hogwarts students ever found out more about the Hogwarts grounds and Hogsmeade than we did.... And that's how we came to write the Marauder's Map, and sign it with our nicknames. Gustavo is Padfoot. Gonzalo is Wormtail. Ricardo was Prongs."
　　"What sort of animal --?" Roberto began, but Carolina cut him off.
　　"That was still really dangerous! Running around in the dark with a werewolf! What if you'd given the others the slip, and bitten somebody?"
　　"A thought that still haunts me," said Cardozo heavily. "And there were near misses, many of them. We laughed about them afterwards. We were young, thoughtless -- carried away with our own cleverness."
　　I sometimes felt guilty about betraying Dominguez's trust, of course... he had admitted me to Hogwarts when no other headmaster would have done so, and he had no idea I was breaking the rules he had set down for my own and others' safety. He never knew I had led three fellow students into becoming Animagi illegally. But I always managed to forget my guilty feelings every time we sat down to plan our next month's adventure. And I haven't changed..."
　　Cardozo's face had hardened, and there was self-disgust in his voice. "All this year, I have been battling with myself, wondering whether I should tell Dominguez that Gustavo was an Animagus. But I didn't do it. Why? Because I was too cowardly. It would have meant admitting that I'd betrayed his trust while I was at school, admitting that I'd led others along with me... and Dominguez's trust has meant everything to me. He let me into Hogwarts as a boy, and he gave me a job when I have been shunned all my adult life, unable to find paid work because of what I am. And so I convinced myself that Gustavo was getting into the school using dark arts he learned from Salvador, that being an Animagus had nothing to do with it... so, in a way, Peralta's been right about me all along."
　　"Peralta?" said Martinez harshly, taking his eyes off Scabbers; for the first time in minutes and looking up at Cardozo. "What's Peralta got to do with it?"
　　"He's here, Gustavo," said Cardozo heavily. "He's teaching here as well." He looked up at Roberto, Diego, and Carolina.
　　"Professor Peralta was at school with us. He fought very hard against my appointment to the Defense Against the Dark Arts job. He has been telling Dominguez A year that I am not to be trusted. He has his reasons... you see, Gustavo here played a trick on him which nearly killed him, a trick which involved me --"
　　Martinez made a derisive noise.
　　"It served him right," he sneered. "Sneaking around, trying to find out what we were up to... hoping he could get us expelled...."
　　"Carlos was very interested in where I went every month." Cardozo told Roberto, Diego, and Carolina. "We were in the same year, you know, and we -- er -- didn't like each other very much. He especially disliked Ricardo. Jealous, I think, of Ricardo's talent on the Quidditch field... anyway Peralta had seen me crossing the grounds with Madam Pomfrey one evening as she led me toward the Whomping Willow to transform. Gustavo thought it would be -- er -- amusing, to tell Peralta all he had to do was prod the knot on the tree trunk with a long stick, and he'd be able to get in after me. Well, of course, Peralta tried it -- if he'd got as far as this house, he'd have met a fully grown werewolf -- but your father, who'd heard what Gustavo had done, went after Peralta and pulled him back, at great risk to his life... Peralta glimpsed me, though, at the end of the tunnel. He was forbidden by Dominguez to tell anybody, but from that time on he knew what I was...."
　　"So that's why Peralta doesn't like you," said Roberto slowly, "because he thought you were in on the joke?"
　　"That's right," sneered a cold voice from the wall behind Cardozo.
　　Carlos Peralta was pulling off the Invisibility Cloak, his wand pointing, directly at Cardozo.
　　CHAPTER NINETEEN
　　THE SERVANT OF LORD SALVADOR
　　Carolina screamed. Martinez leapt to his feet. Roberto felt as though he'd received a huge electric shock.
　　"I found this at the base of the Whomping Willow," said Peralta, throwing the cloak aside, careful to keep this wand pointing directly at Cardozo's chest. "Very useful, Gonzales, I thank you...."
　　Peralta was slightly breathless, but his face was full of suppressed triumph. "You're wondering, perhaps, how I knew you were here?" he said, his eyes glittering. "I've just been to your office, Cardozo. You forgot to take your potion tonight, so I took a gobletful along. And very lucky I did... lucky for me, I mean. Lying on your desk was a certain map. One glance at it told me all I needed to know. I saw you running along this passageway and out of sight."
　　"Carlos --" Cardozo began, but Peralta overrode him.
　　"I've told the headmaster again and again that you're helping your old friend Martinez into the castle, Cardozo, and here's the proof. Not even I dreamed you would have the nerve to use this old place as your hideout --"
　　"Carlos, you're making a mistake," said Cardozo urgently. "You haven't heard everything -- I can explain -- Gustavo is not here to kill Roberto --"
　　"Two more for Azkaban tonight," said Peralta, his eyes now gleaming fanatically. "I shall be interested to see how Dominguez takes this.... He was quite convinced you were harmless, you know, Cardozo... a tame werewolf --"
　　"You fool," said Cardozo softly. "Is a schoolboy grudge worth putting an innocent man back inside Azkaban?"
　　BANG! Thin, snakelike cords burst from the end of Peralta's wand and twisted themselves around Cardozo's mouth, wrists, and ankles; he overbalanced and fell to the floor, unable to move. With a roar of rage, Martinez started toward Peralta, but Peralta pointed his wand straight between Martinez's eyes.
　　"Give me a reason," he whispered. "Give me a reason to do it, and I swear I will."
　　Martinez stopped dead. It would have been impossible to say which face showed more hatred.
　　Roberto stood there, paralyzed, not knowing what to do or whom to believe. He glanced around at Diego and Carolina. Diego looked just as confused as he did, still fighting to keep hold on the struggling Scabbers. Carolina, however, took an uncertain step toward Peralta and said, in a very breathless voice, "Professor Peralta -- it it wouldn't hurt to hear what they've got to say, w -- would it?"
　　"Miss Fernandez, you are already facing suspension from this school," Peralta spat. "You, Gonzales, and Lopez are out-of-bounds, in the company of a convicted murderer and a werewolf. For once in your life, hold your tongue."
　　"But if -- if there was a mistake --"
　　"KEEP QUIET, YOU STUPID GIRL!" Peralta shouted, looking suddenly quite deranged. "DON'T TALK ABOUT WHAT YOU DON'T UNDERSTAND!" A few sparks shot out of the end of his wand, which was still pointed at Martinez's face. Carolina fell silent.
　　"Vengeance is very sweet," Peralta breathed at Martinez. "How I hoped I would be the one to catch you...."
　　"The joke's on you again, Carlos," Martinez snarled. "As long as this boy brings his rat up to the castle" -- he jerked his head at Diego -- "I'll come quietly...."
　　"Up to the castle?" said Peralta silkily. "I don't think we need to go that far. All I have to do is call the dementors once we get out of the Willow. They'll be very pleased to see you, Martinez... pleased enough to give you a little kiss, I daresay... I --"
　　What little color there was in Martinezs face left it.
　　"You -you've got to hear me out," he croaked. "The rat -- look at the rat --"
　　But there was a mad glint in Peralta's eyes that Roberto had never seen before. He seemed beyond reason.
　　"Come on, all of you," he said. He clicked his fingers, and the ends of the cords that bound Cardozo flew to his hands. "I'll drag the werewolf. Perhaps the dementors will have a kiss for him too --"
　　Before he knew what he was doing, Roberto had crossed the room in three strides and blocked the door.
　　"Get out of the way, Gonzales, you're in enough trouble already," snarled Peralta. "If I hadn't been here to save your skin --"
　　"Professor Cardozo could have killed me about a hundred times this year," Roberto said. "I've been alone with him loads of times, having defense lessons against the dementors. If he was helping Martinez, why didn't he just finish me off then?"
　　"Don't ask me to fathom the way a werewolf's mind works," hissed Peralta. "Get out of the way, Gonzales."
　　"YOURE PATHETIC!" Roberto yelled. "JUST BECAUSE THEY MADE A FOOL OF YOU AT SPAULAOL YOU WON'T EVEN LISTEN --"
　　"SILENCE! I WILL NOT BE SPOKEN TO LIKE THAT!" Peralta shrieked, looking madder than ever. "Like father, like son, Gonzales! I have just saved your neck; you should be thanking me on bended knee! You would have been well served if he'd killed you! You'd have died like your father, too arrogant to believe you might be mistaken in Martinez -- now get out of the way, or I will make you. GET OUT OF THE WAY, GONZALES!"
　　Roberto made up his mind in a split second. Before Peralta could take even one step toward him, he had raised his wand.
　　"Expelliarmus!" he yelled -- except that his wasn't the only voice that shouted. There was a blast that made the door rattle on its hinges; Peralta was lifted off his feet and slammed into the wall, then slid down it to the floor, a trickle of blood oozing from under his hair. He had been knocked out.
　　Roberto looked around. Both Diego and Carolina had tried to disarm Peralta at exactly the same moment. Peralta's wand soared in a high arc and landed on the bed next to Crookshanks.
　　"You shouldn't have done that," said Martinez, looking at Roberto.
　　"You should have left him to me...."
　　Roberto avoided Martinez's eyes. He wasn't sure, even now, that he'd done the right thing.
　　"We attacked a teacher... We attacked a teacher..." Carolina whimpered, staring at the lifeless Peralta with frightened eyes. "Oh, we're going to be in so much trouble --"
　　Cardozo was struggling against his bonds. Martinez bent down quickly and untied him. Cardozo straightened up, rubbing his arms where the ropes had cut into them.
　　"Thank you, Roberto," he said.
　　"I'm still not saying I believe you," he told Cardozo.
　　"Then it's time we offered you some proof," said Cardozo. "You, boy -- give me Gonzalo, please. Now."
　　Diego clutched Scabbers closer to his chest.
　　"Come off it," he said weakly. "Are you trying to say he broke out of Azkaban just to get his hands on Scabbers? I mean..." He looked up at Roberto and Carolina for support, "Okay, say Salazar could turn into a rat -- there are millions of rats -- how's he supposed to know which one he's after if he was locked up in Azkaban?"
　　"You know, Gustavo, that's a fair question," said Cardozo, turning to Martinez and frowning slightly. "How did you find out where he was?"
　　Martinez put one of his clawlike hands inside his robes and took out a crumpled piece of paper, which he smoothed flat and held out to show the others.
　　It was the photograph of Diego and his family that had appeared in the Daily Prophet the previous summer, and there, on Diego's shoulder, was Scabbers.
　　"How did you get this?" Cardozo asked Martinez, thunderstruck.
　　"Fudge," said Martinez. "When he came to inspect Azkaban last year, he gave me his paper. And there was Gonzalo, on the front page on this boy's shoulder... I knew him at once... how many times had I seen him transform? And the caption said the boy would be going back to Hogwarts... to where Roberto was...
　　"My God," said Cardozo softly, staring from Scabbers to the picture in the paper and back again. "His front paw..."
　　"What about it?" said Diego defiantly.
　　"He's got a toe missing," said Martinez.
　　"Of course," Cardozo breathed. "So simple... so brilliant... he cut it off himself?"
　　"Just before he transformed," said Martinez. "When I cornered him, he yelled for the whole street to hear that I'd betrayed Sofia and Ricardo. Then, before I could curse him, he blew apart the street with the wand behind his back, killed everyone within twenty feet of himself -- and sped down into the sewer with the other rats...."
　　"Didn't you ever hear, Diego?" said Cardozo. "The biggest bit of Gonzalo they found was his finger."
　　"Look, Scabbers probably had a fight with another rat or something! He's been in my family for ages, right --"
　　"Twelve years, in fact," said Cardozo. "Didn't you ever wonder why he was living so long?"
　　"We -- we've been taking good care of him!" said Diego.
　　"Not looking too good at the moment, though, is he?" said Cardozo. "I'd guess he's been losing weight ever since he heard Gustavo was on the loose again...."
　　"He's been scared of that mad cat!" said Diego, nodding toward Crookshanks, who was still purring on the bed.
　　But that wasn't right, Roberto thought suddenly... Scabbers had been looking ill before he met Crookshanks... ever since Diego's return from Egypt... since the time when Martinez had escaped....
　　"This cat isn't mad," said Martinez hoarsely. He reached out a bony hand and stroked Crookshanks's fluffy head. "He's the most intelligent of his kind I've ever met. He recognized Gonzalo for what he was right away. And when he met me, he knew I was no dog. It was a while before he trusted me.... Finally, I managed to communicate to him what I was after, and he's been helping me. .. "What do you mean?" breathed Carolina.
　　"He tried to bring Gonzalo to me, but couldn't... so he stole the passwords into Gryffindor Tower for me.... As I understand it, he took them from a boy's bedside table...."
　　Roberto's brain seemed to be sagging under the weight of what he was hearing. It was absurd... and yet...
　　"But Gonzalo got wind of what was going on and ran for it." croaked Martinez. "This cat -- Crookshanks, did you call him? -- told me Gonzalo had left blood on the sheets.... I supposed he bit himself... Well, faking his own death had worked once."
　　These words jolted Roberto to his senses.
　　"And why did he fake his death?" he said furiously. "Because he knew you were about to kill him like you killed my parents!"
　　"No," said Cardozo, "Roberto-"
　　"And now you've come to finish him off!"
　　"Yes, I have," said Martinez, with an evil look at Scabbers.
　　"Then I should've let Peralta take you!" Roberto shouted.
　　"Roberto," said Cardozo hurriedly, "don't you see? All this time we've thought Gustavo betrayed your parents, and Gonzalo tracked him down -- but it was the other way around, don't you see? Gonzalo betrayed your mother and father -- Gustavo tracked Gonzalo down --"
　　"THAT'S NOT TRUE!" Roberto yelled. "HE WAS THEIR SECRET-KEEPER! HE SAID SO BEFORE YOU TURNED UP. HE SAID HE KILLED THEM!"
　　He was pointing at Martinez, who shook his head slowly; the sunken eyes were suddenly over bright.
　　"Roberto... I as good as killed them," he croaked. "I persuaded Sofia and Ricardo to change to Gonzalo at the last moment, persuaded them to use him as Secret-Keeper instead of me.... I'm to blame, I know it.... The night they died, I'd arranged to check on Gonzalo, make sure he was still safe, but when I arrived at his hiding place, he'd gone. Yet there was no sign of a struggle. It didn't feel right. I was scared. I set out for your parents' house straight away. And when I saw their house, destroyed, and their bodies... I realized what Gonzalo must've done... what I'd done...."
　　His voice broke. He turned away.
　　"Enough of this," said Cardozo, and there was a steely note in his voice Roberto had never heard before. "There's one certain way to prove what really happened. Diego, give me that rat."
　　"What are you going to do with him if I give him to you?" Diego asked Cardozo tensely.
　　"Force him to show himself," said Cardozo. "If he really is a rat, it won't hurt him."
　　Diego hesitated. Then at long last, he held out Scabbers and Cardozo took him. Scabbers began to squeak without stopping, twisting and turning, his tiny black eyes bulging in his head. "Ready, Gustavo?" said Cardozo.
　　Martinez had already retrieved Peralta's wand from the bed. He approached Cardozo and the struggling rat, and his wet eyes suddenly seemed to be burning in his face.
　　"Together?" he said quietly.
　　"I think so,,, said Cardozo, holding Scabbers tightly in one hand and his wand in the other. "On the count of three. One -- two -- THREE!"
　　A flash of blue-white light erupted from both wands; for a moment, Scabbers was frozen in midair, his small gray form twisting madly -- Diego yelled -- the rat fell and hit the floor. There was another blinding flash of light and then --
　　It was like watching a speeded-up film of a growing tree. A head was shooting upward from the ground; limbs were sprouting; a moment later, a man was standing where Scabbers had been, cringing and wringing his hands. Crookshanks was spitting and snarling on the bed; the hair on his back was standing up.
　　He was a very short man, hardly taller than Roberto and Carolina. His thin, colorless hair was unkempt and there was a large bald patch on top. He had the shrunken appearance of a plump man who has lost a lot of weight in a short time. His skin looked grubby, almost like Scabbers's fur, and something of the rat lingered around his pointed nose and his very small, watery eyes. He looked around at them all, his breathing fast and shallow. Roberto saw his eyes dart to the door and back again.
　　"Well, hello, Gonzalo," said Cardozo pleasantly, as though rats frequently erupted into old school friends around him. "Long time, no see.
　　"S -- Gustavo... R -- Pedro..." Even Salazar's voice was squeaky. Again, his eyes darted toward the door. "My friends... my old friends..."
　　Martinez's wand arm rose, but Cardozo seized him around the wrist, gave him a warning took, then turned again to Salazar, his voice light and casual.
　　"We've been having a little chat, Gonzalo, about what happened the night Sofia and Ricardo died. You might have missed the finer points while you were squeaking around down there on the bed --"
　　"Pedro," gasped Salazar, and Roberto could see beads of sweat breaking out over his pasty face, "you don't believe him, do you...? He tried to kill me, Pedro...."
　　"So we've heard," said Cardozo, more coldly. "I'd like to clear up one or two little matters with you, Gonzalo, if you'll be so --"
　　"He's come to try and kill me again!" Salazar squeaked suddenly, pointing at Martinez, and Roberto saw that he used his middle finger, because his index was missing. "He killed Sofia and Ricardo and now he's going to kill me too.... You've got to help me, Pedro...."
　　Martinez's face looked more skull-like than ever as he stared at Salazar with his fathomless eyes.
　　"No one's going to try and kill you until we've sorted a few things out," said Cardozo.
　　"Sorted things out?" squealed Salazar, looking wildly about him once more, eyes taking in the boarded windows and, again' the only door. "I knew he'd come after me! I knew he'd be back for me! I've been waiting for this for twelve years!"
　　"You knew Gustavo was going to break out of Azkaban?" said Cardozo, his brow furrowed. "When nobody has ever done it before?"
　　"He's got dark powers the rest of us can only dream of!" Salazar shouted shrilly. "How else did he get out of there? I suppose He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named taught him a few tricks!"
　　Martinez started to laugh, a horrible, mirthless laugh that filled the whole room.
　　"Salvador, teach me tricks?" he said.
　　Salazar flinched as though Martinez had brandished a whip at him.
　　"What, scared to hear your old master's name?" said Martinez. I don't blame you, Gonzalo. His lot aren't very happy with you, are they?"
　　"Don't know what you mean, Gustavo --" muttered Salazar, his breathing faster than ever. His whole face was shining with sweat now.
　　"You haven't been hiding from me for twelve years," said Martinez. "You've been hiding from Salvador's old supporters. I heard things in Azkaban, Gonzalo... They all think you're dead, or you'd have to answer to them.... I've heard them screaming all sorts of things in their sleep. Sounds like they think the double-crosser double-crossed them. Salvador went to the Gonzaless' on your information... and Salvador met his downfall there. And not all Salvador's supporters ended up in Azkaban, did they? There are still plenty out here, biding their time, pretending they've seen the error of their ways.
　　If they ever got wind that you were still alive, Gonzalo --"
　　"Don't know... what you're talking about...," said Salazar again, more shrilly than ever. He wiped his face on his sleeve and looked up at Cardozo. "You don't believe this -- this madness, Pedro --"
　　"I must admit, Gonzalo, I have difficulty in understanding why an innocent man would want to spend twelve years as a rat," said Cardozo evenly.
　　"Innocent, but scared!" squealed Salazar. "If Salvador's supporters were after me, it was because I put one of their best men in Azkaban -- the spy, Gustavo Martinez!"
　　Martinez's face contorted.
　　"How dare you," he growled, sounding suddenly like the bearsized dog he had been. I, a spy for Salvador? When did I ever sneak around people who were stronger and more powerful than myself? But you, Gonzalo -- I'll never understand why I didn't see you were the spy from the start. You always liked big friends who'd look after you, didn't you? It used to be us... me and Pedro... and Ricardo....
　　Salazar wiped his face again; he was almost panting for breath.
　　"Me, a spy... must be out of your mind... never... don't know how you can say such a --"
　　"Sofia and Ricardo only made you Secret-Keeper because I suggested it," Martinez hissed, so venomously that Salazar took a step backward. "I thought it was the perfect plan... a bluff... Salvador would be sure to come after me, would never dream they'd use a weak, talentless thing like you.... It must have been the finest moment of your miserable life, telling Salvador you could hand him the Gonzaless."
　　Salazar was muttering distractedly; Roberto caught words like "far-fetched" and "lunacy," but he couldn't help paying more attention to the ashen color of Salazar's face and the way his eyes continued to dart toward the windows and door.
　　"Professor Cardozo?" said Carolina timidly. "Can -- can I say something?"
　　"Certainly, Carolina," said Cardozo courteously.
　　"Well -- Scabbers -- I mean, this -- this man -- he's been sleeping in Roberto's dormitory for three years. If he's working for You-Know-Who, how come he never tried to hurt Roberto before now?"
　　"There!" said Salazar shrilly, pointing at Diego with his maimed hand. "Thank you! You see, Pedro? I have never hurt a hair of Roberto's head! Why should I?"
　　"I'll tell you why," said Martinez. "Because you never did anything for anyone unless you could see what was in it for you. Salvador's been in hiding for fifteen years, they say he's half dead. You weren't about to commit murder right under Alfonso Dominguez's nose, for a wreck of a wizard who'd lost all of his power, were you? You'd want to be quite sure he was the biggest bully in the playground before you went back to him, wouldn't you? Why else did you find a wizard family to take you in? Keeping an ear out for news, weren't YOU, Gonzalo? Just in case your old protector regained strength, and it was safe to rejoin him...."
　　Salazar opened his mouth and closed it several times. He seemed to have lost the ability to talk.
　　"Er -- Mr. Martinez -- Gustavo?" said Carolina.
　　Martinez jumped at being addressed like this and stared at Carolina as though he had never seen anything quite like her.
　　"If you don't mind me asking, how -- how did you get out of Azkaban, if you didn't use Dark Magic?"
　　"Thank you!" gasped Salazar, nodding frantically at her. "Exactly! Precisely what I --"
　　But Cardozo silenced him with a look. Martinez was frowning slightly at Carolina, but not as though he were annoyed with her. He seemed to be pondering his answer.
　　"I don't know how I did it," he said slowly. "I think the only reason I never lost my mind is that I knew I was innocent. That wasn't a happy thought, so the dementors couldn't suck it out of me... but it kept me sane and knowing who I am... helped me keep my powers... so when it all became ... too much... I could transform in my cell... become a dog. Dementors can't see, you know...." He swallowed. "They feel their way toward people by feeding off their emotions.... They could tell that my feelings were less -- less human, less complex when I was a dog... but they thought, of course, that I was losing my mind like everyone else in there, so it didn't trouble them. But I was weak, very weak, and I had no hope of driving them away from me without a wand...."
　　"But then I saw Gonzalo in that picture... I realized he was at Hogwarts with Roberto... perfectly positioned to act, if one hint reached his ears that the Dark Side was gathering strength again...."
　　Salazar was shaking his head, mouthing noiselessly, but staring all the while at Martinez as though hypnotized.
　　"... ready to strike at the moment he could be sure of allies... and to deliver the last Gonzales to them. if he gave them Roberto, who'd dare say he'd betrayed Lord Salvador? He'd be welcomed back with honors....
　　"So you see, I had to do something. I was the only one who knew Gonzalo was still alive...."
　　Roberto remembered what Mr. Lopez had told Mrs. Wealsey. "The guards say he's been talking in his sleep... always the same words... 'He's at Hogwarts.'"
　　"It was as if someone had lit a fire In my head, and the dementors couldn't destroy it.... It wasn't a happy feeling... it was an obsession... but it gave me strength, it cleared my mind. So, one night when they opened my door to bring food, I slipped past them as a dog.... It's so much harder for them to sense animal emotions that they were confused.... I was thin, very thin... thin enough to slip through the bars.... I swam as a dog back to the mainland.... I journeyed north and slipped into the Hogwarts grounds as a dog. I've been living in the forest ever since, except when I came to watch the Quidditch, of course. You fly as well as your father did, Roberto...."
　　He looked at Roberto, who did not look away.
　　"Believe me," croaked Martinez. "Believe me, Roberto. I never betrayed Ricardo and Sofia. I would have died before I betrayed them."
　　And at long last, Roberto believed him. Throat too tight to speak, he nodded.
　　"No!"
　　Salazar had fallen to his knees as though Roberto's nod had been his own death sentence. He shuffled forward on his knees, groveling, his hands clasped in front of him as though praying.
　　"Gustavo -- it's me... it's Gonzalo... your friend... you wouldn't --"
　　Martinez kicked out and Salazar recoiled.
　　"There's enough filth on my robes without you touching them," said Martinez.
　　"Pedro!" Salazar squeaked, turning to Cardozo instead, writhing imploringly in front of him. "You don't believe this wouldn't Gustavo have told you they'd changed the plan?"
　　"Not if he thought I was the spy, Gonzalo," said Cardozo. "I assume that's why you didn't tell me, Gustavo?" he said casually over Salazars head.
　　"Forgive me, Pedro," said Martinez.
　　"Not at all, Padfoot, old friend," said Cardozo, who was now rolling up his sleeves. "And will you, in turn, forgive me for believing you were the spy?"
　　"Of course," said Martinez, and the ghost of a grin flitted across his gaunt face. He, too, began rolling up his sleeves. "Shall we kill him together?"
　　"Yes, I think so," said Cardozo grimly.
　　"You wouldn't... you won't...," gasped Salazar. And he scrambled around to Diego.
　　"Diego... haven't I been a good friend... a good pet? You won't let them kill me, Diego, will you... you're on my side, aren't you.
　　But Diego was staring at Salazar with the utmost revulsion.
　　"I let you sleep in my bed!" he said.
　　"Kind boy... kind master..." Salazar crawled toward Diego "You won't let them do it.... I was your rat.... I was a good pet...."
　　"If you made a better rat than a human, it's not much to boast about, Gonzalo," said Martinez harshly. Diego, going still paler with pain, wrenched his broken leg out of Salazar's reach. Salazar turned on his knees, staggered forward, and seized the hem of Carolina's robes.
　　"Sweet girl... clever girl... you -- you won't let them.... Help me...."
　　Carolina pulled her robes out of Salazar's clutching hands and backed away against the wall, looking horrified.
　　Salazar knelt, trembling uncontrollably, and-turned his head slowly toward Roberto.
　　"Roberto... Roberto... you look just like your father... just like him...."
　　"HOW DARE YOU SPEAK TO ROBERTO?" roared Martinez. "HOW DARE YOU FACE HIM? HOW DARE YOU TALK ABOUT RICARDO IN FDIEGOT OF HIM?"
　　"Roberto," whispered Salazar, shuffling toward him, hands outstretched. "Roberto, Ricardo wouldn't have wanted me killed.... Ricardo would have understood, Roberto... he would have shown me mercy..."
　　Both Martinez and Cardozo strode forward, seized Salazar's shoulders, and threw him backward onto the floor. He sat there, twitching with terror, staring up at them.
　　"You sold Sofia and Ricardo to Salvador," said Martinez, who was shaking too. "Do you deny it?"
　　Salazar burst into tears. It was horrible to watch, like an oversized, balding baby, cowering on the floor.
　　"Gustavo, Gustavo, what could I have done? The Dark Lord... you have no idea... he has weapons you can't imagine.... I was scared, Gustavo, I was never brave like you and Pedro and Ricardo. I never meant it to happen.... He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named forced me --"
　　"DON'T LIE!" bellowed Martinez. "YOU'D BEEN PASSING INFORMATION TO HIM FOR A YEAR BEFORE SOFIA AND RICARDO DIED! YOU WERE HIS SPY!"
　　"He -- he was taking over everywhere!" gasped Salazar. "Wh -- what was there to be gained by refusing him?"
　　"What was there to be gained by fighting the most evil wizard who has ever existed?" said Martinez, with a terrible fury in his face. "Only innocent lives, Gonzalo!"
　　"You don't understand!" whined Salazar. "He would have killed me, Gustavo!"
　　"THEN YOU SHOULD HAVE DIED!" roared Martinez. "DIED RATHER THAN BETRAY YOUR FRIENDS, AS WE WOULD HAVE DONE FOR YOU!"
　　Martinez and Cardozo stood shoulder to shoulder, wands raised.
　　"You should have realized," said Cardozo quietly, "if Salvador didn't kill you, we would. Good-bye, Gonzalo."
　　Carolina covered her face with her hands and turned to the wall.
　　"NO!" Roberto yelled. He ran forward, placing himself in front Salazar, facing the wands. "You can't kill him," he said breathlessly. "You can't."
　　Martinez and Cardozo both looked staggered.
　　"Roberto, this piece of vermin is the reason you have no parents," Martinez snarled. "This cringing bit of filth would have seen you die too, without turning a hair. You heard him. His own stinking skin meant more to him than your whole family."
　　"I know," Roberto panted. "We'll take him up to the castle. We'll hand him over to the dementors.... He can go to Azkaban... but don't kill him."
　　"Roberto!" gasped Salazar, and he flung his arms around Roberto's knees. "You -- thank you -- it's more than I deserve -- thank you --"
　　"Get off me," Roberto spat, throwing Salazar's hands off him in disgust. "I'm not doing this for you. I'm doing it because -- I don't reckon my dad would've wanted them to become killers -- just for you."
　　No one moved or made a sound except Salazar, whose breath was coming in wheezes as he clutched his chest. Martinez and Cardozo were looking at each other. Then, with one movement, they lowered their wands.
　　"You're the only person who has the right to decide, Roberto," said Martinez. "But think... think what he did...."
　　"He can go to Azkaban," Roberto repeated. "If anyone deserves that place, he does...."
　　Salazar was still wheezing behind him.
　　"Very well," said Cardozo. "Stand aside, Roberto."
　　Roberto hesitated.
　　"I'm going to tie him up," said Cardozo. "That's all, I swear."
　　Roberto stepped out of the way. Thin cords shot from Cardozo's wand this time, and next moment, Salazar was wriggling on the floor, bound and gagged.
　　"But if you transform, Gonzalo," growled Martinez, his own wand pointing at Salazar too, "we will kill you. You agree, Roberto?"
　　Roberto looked down at the pitiful figure on the floor and nodded so that Salazar could see him.
　　"Right," said Cardozo, suddenly businesslike. "Diego, I can't mend bones nearly as well as Madam Pomfrey, so I think it's best if we just strap your leg up until we can get you to the hospital wing."
　　He hurried over to Diego, bent down, tapped Diego's leg with his wand, and muttered, "Ferula." Bandages spun up Diego's leg, strapping it tightly to a splint. Cardozo helped him to his feet; Diego put his weight gingerly on the leg and didn't wince.
　　"That's better," he said. "Thanks."
　　"What about Professor Peralta?" said Carolina in a small voice, looking down at Peralta's prone figure.
　　"There's nothing seriously wrong with him," said Cardozo, bending over Peralta and checking his pulse. "You were just a little -- overenthusiastic. Still out cold. Er -- perhaps it will be best if we don't revive him until we're safety back in the castle. We can take him like this...."
　　He muttered, "Mobilicorpus." As though invisible strings were tied to Peralta's wrists, neck, and knees, he was pulled into a standing position, head still lolling unpleasantly, like a grotesque puppet. He hung a few inches above the ground, his limp feet dangling. Cardozo picked up the Invisibility Cloak and tucked it safely into his pocket.
　　"And two of us should be chained to this," said Martinez, nudging Salazar with his toe. "Just to make sure."
　　"I'll do it," said Cardozo.
　　"And me," said Diego savagely, limping forward.
　　Martinez conjured heavy manacles from thin air; soon Salazar was upright again, left arm chained to Cardozo's right, right arm to Diego's left. Diego's face was set. He seemed to have taken Scabbers's true identity as a personal insult. Crookshanks leapt lightly off the bed and led the way out of the room, his bottlebrush tail held jauntily high.
　　CHAPTER TWENTY
　　THE DEMENTOR'S KISS
　　Roberto had never been part of a stranger group. Crookshanks led the way down the stairs; Cardozo, Salazar, and Diego went next, looking like entrants in a six-legged race. Next came Professor Peralta, drifting creepily along, his toes hitting each stair as they descended, held up by his own wand, which was being pointed at him by Gustavo. Roberto and Carolina brought up the rear.
　　Getting back into the tunnel was difficult. Cardozo, Salazar, and Diego had to turn sideways to manage it; Cardozo still had Salazar covered with his wand. Roberto could see them edging awkwardly along the tunnel in single file. Crookshanks was still in the lead. Roberto went right after Martinez, who was still making Peralta drift along ahead of them; he kept bumping his lolling head on the low ceiling. Roberto had the impression Martinez was making no effort to prevent this.
　　"You know what this means?" Martinez said abruptly to Roberto as they made their slow progress along the tunnel. "Turning Salazar in?"
　　"You' re free," said Roberto.
　　"Yes...," said Martinez. "But I'm also -- I don't know if anyone ever told you -- I'm your godfather."
　　"Yeah, I knew that," said Roberto.
　　"Well... your parents appointed me your guardian," said Martinez stiffly. "If anything happened to them..."
　　Roberto waited. Did Martinez mean what he thought he meant?
　　"I'll understand, of course, if you want to stay with your aunt and uncle," said Martinez. "But... well... think about it. Once my name's cleared... if you wanted a... a different home..."
　　Some sort of explosion took place in the pit of Roberto's stomach.
　　"What -- live with you?" he said, accidentally cracking his head on a bit of rock protruding from the ceiling. "Leave the Carrizos?"
　　"Of course, I thought you wouldn't want to," said Martinez quickly. "I understand, I just thought I'd --"
　　"Are you insane?" said Roberto, his voice easily as croaky as Martinez's.
　　"Of course I want to leave the Carrizos! Have you got a house? When can I move in?"
　　Martinez turned right around to look at him; Peralta's head was scraping the ceiling but Martinez didn't seem to care.
　　"You want to?" he said. "You mean it?"
　　"Yeah, I mean it!" said Roberto.
　　Martinez's gaunt face broke into the first true smile Roberto had seen upon it. The difference it made was startling, as though a person ten years younger were shining through the starved mask; for a moment, he was recognizable as the man who had laughed at Roberto's parents' wedding.
　　They did not speak again until they had reached the end of the tunnel. Crookshanks darted up first; he had evidently pressed his paw to the knot on the trunk, because Cardozo, Salazar, and Diego clambered upward without any sound of savaging branches.
　　Martinez saw Peralta up through the hole, then stood back for Roberto and Carolina to pass. At last, all of them were out.
　　The grounds were very dark now; the only light came from the distant windows of the castle. Without a word, they set off. Salazar was still wheezing and occasionally whimpering. Roberto's mind was buzzing. He was going to leave the Carrizos. He was going to live with Gustavo Martinez, his parents' best friend.... He felt dazed.... What would happen when he told the Carrizos he was going to live with the convict they'd seen on television... !
　　"One wrong move, Gonzalo," said Cardozo threateningly ahead. His wand was still pointed sideways at Salazar's chest.
　　Silently they tramped through the grounds, the castle lights growing slowly larger. Peralta was still drifting weirdly ahead of Martinez, his chin bumping on his chest. And then -
　　A cloud shifted. There were suddenly dim shadows on the ground. Their party was bathed in moonlight.
　　Peralta collided with Cardozo, Salazar, and Diego, who had stopped abruptly. Martinez froze. He flung out one arm to make Roberto and Carolina stop.
　　Roberto could see Cardozo's silhouette. He had gone rigid. Then his limbs began to shake.
　　"Oh, my --" Carolina gasped. "He didn't take his potion tonight! He's not safe!"
　　"Run," Martinez whispered. "Run. Now."
　　But Roberto couldn't run. Diego was chained to Salazar and Cardozo. He leapt forward but Martinez caught him around the chest and threw him back.
　　"Leave it to me -- RUN!"
　　There was a terrible snarling noise. Cardozo's head was lengthening. So was his body. His shoulders were hunching. Hair was sprouting visibly on his face and hands, which were curling into clawed paws. Crookshanks's hair was on end again; he was backing away --
　　As the werewolf reared, snapping its long jaws, Gustavo disappeared from Roberto's side. He had transformed. The enormous, bearlike dog bounded forward. As the werewolf wrenched itself free of the manacle binding it, the dog seized it about the neck and pulled it backward, away from Diego and Salazar. They were locked, jaw to jaw, claws ripping at each other.
　　Roberto stood, transfixed by the sight, too intent upon the battle to notice anything else. It was Carolina's scream that alerted him --
　　Salazar had dived for Cardozo's dropped wand. Diego, unsteady on his bandaged leg, fell. There was a bang, a burst of light -- and Diego lay motionless on the ground. Another bang -- Crookshanks flew into the air and back to the earth in a heap.
　　"Expelliarmus." Roberto yelled, pointing his own wand at Salazar; Cardozo's wand flew high into the air and out of sight. "Stay where you are!" Roberto shouted, running forward.
　　Too late. Salazar had transformed. Roberto saw his bald tail whip through the manacle on Diego's outstretched arm and heard a scurrying through the grass.
　　There was a howl and a rumbling growl; Roberto turned to see the werewolf taking flight; it was galloping into the forest --
　　"Gustavo, he's gone, Salazar transformed!" Roberto yelled.
　　Martinez was bleeding; there were gashes across his muzzle and back, but at Roberto's words he scrambled up again, and in an instant, the sound of his paws faded to silence as he pounded away across the grounds.
　　Roberto and Carolina dashed over to Diego.
　　"What did he do to him?" Carolina whispered. Diego's eyes were only half-closed, his mouth hung open; he was definitely alive, they could hear him breathing, but he didn't seem to recognize them.
　　"I don't know...."
　　Roberto looked desperately around. Martinez and Cardozo both gone... they had no one but Peralta for company, still hanging, unconscious, in midair.
　　"We'd better get them up to the castle and tell someone," said Roberto, pushing his hair out of his eyes, trying to think straight. "Come --"
　　But then, from beyond the range of their vision, they heard a yelping, a whining: a dog in pain....
　　"Gustavo," Roberto muttered, staring into the darkness.
　　He had a moment's indecision, but there was nothing they could do for Diego at the moment, and by the sound of it, Martinez was in trouble --
　　Roberto set off at a run, Carolina right behind him. The yelping seemed to be coming from the ground near the edge of the lake. They pelted toward it, and Roberto, running flat out, felt the cold without realizing what it must mean -
　　The yelping stopped abruptly. As they reached the lakeshore, they saw why -- Gustavo had turned back into a man. He was crouched on all fours, his hands over his head.
　　'Nooo," he moaned. 'Nooo... please...."
　　And then Roberto saw them. Dementors, at least a hundred of them, gliding in a black mass around the lake toward them. He spun around, the familiar, icy cold penetrating his insides, fog starting to obscure his vision; more were appearing out of the darkness on every side; they were encircling them....
　　"Herrnione, think of something happy!" Roberto yelled, raising his wand, blinking furiously to try and clear his vision, shaking his head to rid it of the faint screaming that had started inside it --
　　I'm going to live with my godfather. I'm leaving the Carrizos.
　　He forced himself to think of Martinez, and only Martinez, and began to chant: "Expecto patronum! Expecto patronum!"
　　Martinez gave a shudder, rolled over, and lay motionless on the ground, pale as death.
　　He'll be all right. I'm going to go and live with him.
　　"Expecto patronum! Carolina, help me! Expecto patronum!"
　　"Expecto --" Carolina whispered, "expecto -- expecto --"
　　But she couldn't do it. The dementors were closing in, barely ten feet from them. They formed a solid wall around Roberto and Carolina, and were getting closer....
　　"EXPECTO PATDIEGOUM!" Roberto yelled, trying to blot the screaming from his ears. "EXPECTO PATDIEGOUM!"
　　A thin wisp of silver escaped his wand and hovered like mist before him. At the same moment, Roberto felt Carolina collapse next to him. He was alone... completely alone....
　　"Expecto -- expecto patronum --"
　　Roberto felt his knees hit the cold grass. Fog was clouding his eyes. With a huge effort, he fought to remember -- Gustavo was innocent -- innocent -- We'll be okay -- I' mgoing to live with him --
　　"Ex ecto patronum!" he gasped.
　　By the feeble light of his formless Patronus, He saw a dementor halt, very close to him. It couldn't walk through the cloud of silver mist Roberto had conjured. A dead, slimy hand slid out from under the cloak. It made a gesture as though to sweep the Patronus aside.
　　"No -- no --" Roberto gasped. "He's innocent... expecto expecto patronum --"
　　He could feet them watching him, hear their rattling breath like an evil wind around him. The nearest dementor seemed to be considering him. Then it raised both its rotting hands -- and lowered its hood.
　　Where there should have been eyes, there was only thin, gray scabbed skin, stretched blankly over empty sockets. But there was a mouth... a gaping, shapeless hole, sucking the air with the sound of a death rattle.
　　A paralyzing terror filled Roberto so that he couldn't move or speak. His Patronus flickered and died.
　　White fog was blinding him. He had to fight... expecto patronum ... he couldn't see... and in the distance, he heard the familiar screaming... expecto patronum... he groped in the mist for Gustavo, and found his arm... they weren't going to take him....
　　But a pair of strong, clammy hands suddenly attached themselves around Roberto's neck. They were forcing his face upward.... He could feel its breath.... It was going to get rid of him first.... He could feel its putrid breath.... His mother was screaming in his ears.... She was going to be the last thing he ever heard --
　　And then, through the fog that was drowning him, he thought he saw a silvery light growing brighter and brighter... He felt himself fall forward onto the grass.... Facedown, too weak to move, sick and shaking, Roberto opened his eyes. The dementor must have released him. The blinding light was illuminating the grass around him.... The screaming had stopped, the cold was ebbing away...
　　Something was driving the dementors back.... It was circling around him and Martinez and Carolina.... They were leaving....
　　The air was warm again....
　　With every ounce of strength he could muster, Roberto raised his head a few inches and saw an animal amid the light, galloping away across the lake.... Eyes blurred with sweat, Roberto tried to make out what it was.... It was as bright as a unicorn.... Fighting to stay conscious, Roberto watched it canter to a halt as it reached the opposite shore. For a moment, Roberto saw, by its brightness, somebody welcoming it back... raising his hand to pat it... someone who looked strangely familiar ... but it couldn't be...
　　Roberto didn't understand. He couldn't think anymore. He felt the last of his strength leave him, and his head hit the ground as he fainted.
　　CHAPTER TWENTY-ONE
　　CAROLINA'S SECRET
　　Shocking business... shocking... miracle none of them died... never heard the like... by thunder, it was lucky you were there, Peralta...."
　　"Thank you, Minister."
　　"Order of Merlin, Second Class, I'd say. First Class, if I can wangle it!"
　　"Thank you very much indeed, Minister."
　　"Nasty cut you've got there.... Martinez's work, I suppose?"
　　"As a matter of fact, it was Gonzales, Lopez, and Fernandez, Minister...."
　　"No!"
　　"Martinez had bewitched them, I saw it immediately. A Confundus Charm, to judge by their behavior. They seemed to think there was a possibility he was innocent. They weren't responsible for their actions. On the other hand, their interference might have permitted Martinez to escape.... They obviously thought they were going to catch Martinez single-handed. They've got away with a great deal before now... I'm afraid it's given them a rather high opinion of themselves... and of course Gonzales has always been allowed an extraordinary amount of license by the headmaster --"
　　"Ah, well, Peralta... Roberto Gonzales, you know... we've all got a bit of a blind spot where he's concerned."
　　"And yet -- is it good for him to be given so much special treatment? Personally, I try and treat him like any other student. And any other student would be suspended -- at the very least -- for leading his friends into such danger. Consider, Minister -- against all school rules -- after all the precautions put in place for his protection -- out-of-bounds, at night, consorting with a werewolf and a murderer -- and I have reason to believe he has been visiting Hogsmeade illegally too --"
　　"Well, well... we shall see, Peralta, we shall see.... The boy has undoubtedly been foolish...."
　　Roberto lay listening with his eyes tight shut. He felt very groggy. The words he was hearing seemed to be traveling very slowly from his ears to his brain, so that it was difficult to understand.... His limbs felt like lead; his eyelids too heavy to lift.... He wanted to lie here, on this comfortable bed, forever....
　　"What amazes me most is the behavior of the dementors... you've really no idea what made them retreat, Peralta?"
　　"No, Minister... by the time I had come 'round they were heading back to their positions at the entrances...."
　　"Extraordinary. And yet Martinez, and Roberto, and the girl --"
　　"All unconscious by the time I reached them. I bound and gagged Martinez, naturally, conjured stretchers, and brought them all straight back to the castle."
　　There was a pause. Roberto's brain seemed to be moving a little faster, and as it did, a gnawing sensation grew in the pit of his stomach....
　　He opened his eyes.
　　Everything was slightly blurred. Somebody had removed his glasses. He was lying in the dark hospital wing. At the very end of the ward, he could make out Madam Pomfrey with her back to him, bending over a bed. Roberto squinted. Diego's red hair was visible beneath Madam Pomfrey's arm.
　　Roberto moved his head over on the pillow. In the bed to his right lay Carolina. Moonlight was falling across her bed. Her eyes were open too. She looked petrified, and when she saw that Roberto was awake, pressed a finger to her lips, then pointed to the hospital wing door. It was ajar, and the voices of Cornelius Fudge and Peralta were coming through it from the corridor outside.
　　Madam Pomfrey now came walking briskly up the dark ward to Roberto's bed. He turned to took at her. She was carrying the largest block of chocolate he had ever seen in his life. It looked like a small boulder.
　　"Ah, you're awake!" she said briskly. She placed the chocolate on Roberto's bedside table and began breaking it apart with a small hammer.
　　"How's Diego?" said Roberto and Carolina together.
　　"He'll live, said Madam Pomfrey grimly. "As for you two you'll be staying here until I'm satisfied you're -- Gonzales, what do you think you're doing?"
　　Roberto was sitting up, putting his glasses back on, and picking up his wand.
　　"I need to see the headmaster," he said.
　　"Gonzales," said Madam Pomfrey soothingly, "it's all right. They've got Martinez. He's locked away upstairs. The dementors will be performing the kiss any moment now --"
　　"WHAT?"
　　Roberto jumped up out of bed; Carolina had done the same. But his shout had been heard in the corridor outside; next second, Cornelius Fudge and Peralta had entered the ward.
　　"Roberto, Roberto, what's this?" said Fudge, looking agitated. "You should be in bed -- has he had any chocolate?" he asked Madam Pomfrey anxiously.
　　"Minister, listen!" Roberto said. "Gustavo Martinez's innocent! Gonzalo Salazar faked his own death! We saw him tonight! You can't let the dementors do that thing to Gustavo, he's --"
　　But Fudge was shaking his head with a small smile on his face.
　　"Roberto, Roberto, you're very confused, you've been through a dreadful ordeal, lie back down, now, we've got everything under control...."
　　"YOU HAVEN'T!" Roberto yelled. "YOUVE GOT THE WDIEGOG MAN!"
　　"Minister, listen, please," Carolina said; she had hurried to Roberto's side and was gazing imploringly into Fudge's face. "I saw him too. It was Diego's rat, he's an Animagus, Salazar, I mean, and --"
　　"You see, Minister?" said Peralta. "Confunded, both of them.... Martinez's done a very good job on them...." "WE'RE NOT CONFUNDED!" Roberto roared.
　　"Minister! Professor!" said Madam Pomfrey angrily. "I must insist that you leave. Gonzales is my patient, and he should not be distressed!"
　　"I'm not distressed, I'm trying to tell them what happened!" Roberto said furiously. "If they'd just listen --"
　　But Madam Pomfrey suddenly stuffed a large chunk of chocolate into Roberto's mouth; he choked, and she seized the opportunity to force him back onto the bed.
　　"Now, please, Minister, these children need care. Please leave
　　The door opened again. It was Dominguez. Roberto swallowed his mouthful of chocolate with great difficulty and got up again.
　　"Professor Dominguez, Gustavo Martinez --"
　　"For heaven's sake!" said Madam Pomfrey hysterically. "Is this a hospital wing or not? Headmaster, I must insist --"
　　"My apologies, Poppy, but I need a word with Mr. Gonzales and Miss Fernandez," said Dominguez calmly. "I have just been talking to Gustavo Martinez --"
　　"I suppose he's told you the same fairy tale he's planted in Gonzales's mind?" spat Peralta. "Something about a rat, and Salazar being alive --"
　　"That, indeed, is Martinez's story," said Dominguez, surveying Peralta closely through his half-moon spectacles.
　　"And does my evidence count for nothing?" snarled Peralta. "Gonzalo Salazar was not in the Shrieking Shack, nor did I see any sign of him on the grounds."
　　"That was because you were knocked out, Professor!" said Carolina earnestly. "You didn't arrive in time to hear
　　"Miss Fernandez, HOLD YOUR TONGUE!"
　　"Now, Peralta," said Fudge, startled, "the young lady is disturbed in her mind, we must make allowances --"
　　"I would like to speak to Roberto and Carolina alone," said Dominguez abruptly. "Cornelius, Carlos, Poppy -- please leave us."
　　"Headmaster!" sputtered Madam Pomfrey. "They need treatment, they need rest --"
　　"This cannot wait," said Dominguez. "I must insist."
　　Madam Pomfrey pursed her lips and strode away into her office at the end of the ward, slamming the door behind her. Fudge consulted the large gold pocket watch dangling from his waistcoat.
　　"The dementors should have arrived by now," he said. "I'll go and meet them. Dominguez, I'll see you upstairs."
　　He crossed to the door and held it open for Peralta, but Peralta hadn't moved.
　　"You surely don't believe a word of Martinez's story?" Peralta whispered, his eyes fixed on Dominguez's face.
　　"I wish to speak to Roberto and Carolina alone," Dominguez repeated.
　　Peralta took a step toward Dominguez.
　　"Gustavo Martinez showed he was capable of murder at the age of sixteen," he breathed. "You haven't forgotten that, Headmaster? You haven't forgotten that he once tried to kill me?"
　　"My memory is as good as it ever was, Carlos," said Dominguez quietly.
　　Peralta turned on his heel and marched through the door Fudge was still holding. It closed behind them, and Dominguez turned to Roberto and Carolina. They both burst into speech at the same time.
　　"Professor, Martinez's telling the truth -- we saw Salazar "-- he escaped when Professor Cardozo turned into a werewolf --"
　　"-- he's a rat --"
　　"-- Salazar's front paw, I mean, finger, he cut it off --"
　　"-- Salazar attacked Diego, it wasn't Gustavo --"
　　But Dominguez held up his hand to stem the flood of explanations.
　　"It is your turn to listen, and I beg you will not interrupt me, because there is very little time," he said quietly. "There is not a shred of proof to support Martinez's story, except your word -- and the word of two thirteen-year-old wizards will not convince anybody. A street full of eyewitnesses swore they saw Gustavo murder Salazar. I myself gave evidence to the Ministry that Gustavo had been the Gonzaless' Secret-Keeper."
　　"Professor Cardozo can tell you --" Roberto said, unable to stop himself
　　"Professor Cardozo is currently deep in the forest, unable to tell anyone anything. By the time he is human again, it will be too late, Gustavo will be worse than dead. I might add that werewolves are so mistrusted by most of our kind that his support will count for very little -- and the fact that he and Gustavo are old friends --"
　　"But --"
