　　"Listen to me, Roberto. It is too late, you understand me? You must see that Professor Peralta's version of events is far more convincing than yours."
　　"He hates Gustavo," Carolina said desperately. "All because of some stupid trick Gustavo played on him --"
　　"Gustavo has not acted like an innocent man. The attack on the Fat Lady -- entering Gryffindor Tower with a knife -- without Salazar, alive or dead, we have no chance of overturning Gustavo's sentence."
　　"But you believe us."
　　"Yes, I do," said Dominguez quietly. "But I have no power to make other men see the truth, or to overrule the Minister of Magic...."
　　Roberto stared up into the grave face and felt as though the ground beneath him were falling sharply away. He had grown used to the idea that Dominguez could solve anything. He had expected Dominguez to pull some amazing solution out of the air. But no ... their last hope was gone.
　　"What we need," said Dominguez slowly, and his light blue eyes moved from Roberto to Carolina, "is more time."
　　"But --" Carolina began. And then her eyes became very round. "OH!"
　　"Now, pay attention," said Dominguez, speaking very low, and very clearly. "Gustavo is locked in Professor Flitwick's office on the seventh floor. Thirteenth window from the right of the West Tower. If all goes well, you will be able to save more than one innocent life tonight. But remember this, both of you: you must not be seen. Miss Fernandez, you know the law -- you know what is at stake.... You -- must -- not -- be -- seen."
　　Roberto didn't have a clue what was going on. Dominguez had turned on his heel and looked back as he reached the door.
　　"I am going to lock you in. It is --" he consulted his watch, "five minutes to midnight. Miss Fernandez, three turns should do it. Good luck."
　　"Good luck?" Roberto repeated as the door closed behind Dominguez. "Three turns? What's he talking about? What are we supposed to do?"
　　But Carolina was fumbling with the neck of her robes, pulling from beneath them a very long, very fine gold chain.
　　"Roberto, come here," she said urgently. "Quick!"
　　Roberto moved toward her, completely bewildered. She was holding the chain out. He saw a tiny, sparkling hourglass hanging from it.
　　"Here --"
　　She had thrown the chain around his neck too.
　　"Ready?" she said breathlessly.
　　"What are we doing?" Roberto said, completely lost.
　　Carolina turned the hourglass over three times.
　　The dark ward dissolved. Roberto had the sensation that he was flying very fast, backward. A blur of colors and shapes rushed past him, his ears were pounding, he tried to yell but couldn't hear his own voice --
　　And then he felt solid ground beneath his feet, and everything came into focus again --
　　He was standing next to Carolina in the deserted entrance hall and a stream of golden sunlight was falling across the paved floor from the open front doors. He looked wildly around at Carolina, the chain of the hourglass cutting into his neck.
　　"Carolina, what --?"
　　"In here!" Carolina seized Roberto's arm and dragged him across the hall to the door of a broom closet; she opened it, pushed him inside among the buckets and mops, then slammed the door behind them.
　　"What -- how -- Carolina, what happened?"
　　"We've gone back in time," Carolina whispered, lifting the chain off Roberto's neck in the darkness. "Three hours back..."
　　Roberto found his own leg and gave it a very hard pinch. It hurt a lot, which seemed to rule out the possibility that he was having a very bizarre dream.
　　"But --"
　　"Shh! Listen! Someone's coming! I think -- I think it might be us!" Carolina had her ear pressed against the cupboard door.
　　"Footsteps across the hall... yes, I think it's us going down to Villalba's!"
　　"Are you telling me," Roberto whispered, "that we're here in this cupboard and we're out there too?"
　　"Yes," said Carolina, her ear still glued to the cupboard door. "I'm sure it's us. It doesn't sound like more than three people... and we're walking slowly because we're under the Invisibility Cloak -- "
　　She broke off, still listening intently.
　　"We've gone down the front steps...."
　　Carolina sat down on an upturned bucket, looking desperately anxious, but Roberto wanted a few questions answered.
　　"Where did you get that hourglass thing?"
　　"It's called a Time-Turner," Carolina whispered, "and I got it from Professor Romero on our first day back. I've been using it all year to get to all my lessons. Professor Romero made me swear I wouldn't tell anyone. She had to write all sorts of letters to the Ministry of Magic so I could have one. She had to tell them that I was a model student, and that I'd never, ever use it for anything except my studies.... I've been turning it back so I could do hours over again, that's how I've been doing several lessons at once, see? But...
　　"Roberto, I don't understand what Dominguez wants us to do. Why did he tell us to go back three hours? How's that going to help Gustavo?"
　　Roberto stared at her shadowy face.
　　"There must be something that happened around now he wants us to change," he said slowly. "What happened? We were walking down to Villalba's three hours ago...."
　　"This is three hours ago, and we are walking down to Villalba's," said Carolina. "We just heard ourselves leaving...."
　　Roberto frowned; he felt as though he were screwing up his whole brain in concentration.
　　"Dominguez just said -- just said we could save more than one innocent life...." And then it hit him. "Carolina, we're going to save Buckbeak!"
　　"But -- how will that help Gustavo?"
　　"Dominguez said -- he just told us where the window is -- the window of Flitwick's office! Where they've got Gustavo locked up! We've got to fly Buckbeak up to the window and rescue Gustavo! Gustavo can escape on Buckbeak -- they can escape together!"
　　From what Roberto could see of Carolina's face, she looked terrified.
　　"If we manage that without being seen, it'll be a miracle!"
　　"Well, we've got to try, haven't we?" said Roberto. He stood up and pressed his ear against the door. "Doesn't sound like anyone's there.... Come on, let's go."
　　Roberto pushed open the closet door. The entrance hall was deserted. As quietly and quickly as they could, they darted out of the closet and down the stone steps. The shadows were already lengthening, the tops of the trees in the Forbidden Forest gilded once more with gold.
　　"If anyone's looking out of the window --" Carolina squeaked, looking up at the castle behind them.
　　"We'll run for it," said Roberto determinedly. "Straight into the forest, all right? We'll have to hide behind a tree or something and keep a lookout --"
　　"Okay, but we'll go around by the greenhouses!" said Carolina breathlessly. "We need to keep out of sight of Villalba's front door, or we'll see us! We must be nearly at Villalba's by now!"
　　Still working out what she meant, Roberto set off at a sprint, Carolina behind him. They tore across the vegetable gardens to the greenhouses, paused for a moment behind them, then set off again, fast as they could, skirting around the Whomping Willow, tearing toward the shelter of the forest....
　　Safe in the shadows of the trees, Roberto turned around; seconds later, Carolina arrived beside him, panting.
　　"Right," she gasped. "We need to sneak over to Villalba's.... Keep out of sight, Roberto...."
　　They made their way silently through the trees, keeping to the very edge of the forest. Then, as they glimpsed the front of Villalba's house, they heard a knock upon his door. They moved quickly behind a wide oak trunk and peered out from either side. Villalba had appeared in his doorway, shaking and white, looking around to see who had knocked. And Roberto heard his own voice.
　　"It's us. We're wearing the Invisibility Cloak. Let us in and we can take it off."
　　"Yeh shouldn've come!" Villalba whispered. He stood back, then shut the door quickly.
　　"This is the weirdest thing we've ever done," Roberto said fervently.
　　"Let's move along a bit," Carolina whispered. "We need to get nearer to Buckbeak!"
　　They crept through the trees until they saw the nervous hippogriff, tethered to the fence around Villalba's pumpkin patch.
　　"Now?" Roberto whispered.
　　"No!" said Carolina. "If we steal him now, those Committee people will think Villalba set him free! We've got to wait until they've seen he's tied outside!"
　　"That's going to give us about sixty seconds," said Roberto. This was starting to seem impossible.
　　At that moment, there was a crash of breaking china from inside Villalba's cabin.
　　"That's Villalba breaking the milk jug," Carolina whispered. "I'm going to find Scabbers in a moment --"
　　Sure enough, a few minutes later, they heard Carolina's shriek of surprise.
　　"Carolina," said Roberto suddenly, "what if we -- we just run in there and grab Salazar --"
　　"No!" said Carolina in a terrified whisper. "Don't you understand? We're breaking one of the most important wizarding laws! Nobody's supposed to change time, nobody! You heard Dominguez, if we're seen --"
　　"We'd only be seen by ourselves and Villalba!"
　　"Roberto, what do you think you'd do if you saw yourself bursting into Villalba's house?" said Carolina.
　　"I'd -- I'd think I'd gone mad," said Roberto, "or I'd think there was some Dark Magic going on --"
　　"Exactly! You wouldn't understand, you might even attack yourself! Don't you see? Professor Romero told me what awful things have happened when wizards have meddled with time.... Loads of them ended up killing their past or future selves by mistake!"
　　"Okay!" said Roberto. "It was just an idea, I just thought
　　But Carolina nudged him and pointed toward the castle. Roberto moved his head a few inches to get a clear view of the distant front doors. Dominguez, Fudge, the old Committee member, and Macnair the executioner were coming down the steps.
　　"We're about to come out!" Carolina breathed.
　　And sure enough, moments later, Villalba's back door opened, and Roberto saw himself, Diego, and Carolina walking out of it with Villalba. It was, without a doubt, the strangest sensation of his life, standing behind the tree, and watching himself in the pumpkin patch.
　　"It's Okay, Beaky, it's okay..." Villalba said to Buckbeak. Then he turned to Roberto, Diego, and Carolina. "Go on. Get goin'."
　　"Villalba, we can't --"
　　"We'll tell them what really happened
　　"They can't kill him --"
　　"Go! It's bad enough without you lot in trouble an' all!"

　　There was a knock on Villalba's front door. The execution party had arrived. Villalba turned, around and headed back into his cabin, leaving the back door ajar. Roberto watched the grass flatten in patches all around the cabin and heard three pairs of feet retreating. He, Diego, and Carolina had gone... but the Roberto and Carolina hidden in the trees could now hear what was happening inside the cabin through the back door.
　　"Where is the beast?" came the cold voice of Macnair.

　　"It is the decision of the Committee for the Disposal of Dangerous Creatures that the hippogriff Buckbeak, hereafter called the condemned, shall he executed on the sixth of June at sundown --"
　　Careful not to blink, Roberto stared up into Buckbeak's fierce orange eyes once more and bowed. Buckbeak sank to his scaly knees and then stood up again. Roberto began to fumble with the knot of rope tying Buckbeak to the fence.

　　"Well, let's get this over with," said the reedy voice of the Committee member from inside Villalba's cabin. "Villalba, perhaps it will be better if you stay inside --"

They were still ten feet away from the forest, in plain view of Villalba's back door. "One moment, please, Macnair," came Dominguez's voice. "You need to sign too." The footsteps stopped. Roberto heaved on the rope. Buckbeak snapped his beak and walked a little faster.
　　Carolina's white face was sticking out from behind a tree.
　　"Roberto, hurry!" she mouthed.
　　Roberto could still hear Dominguez's voice talking from within the cabin. He gave the rope another wrench. Buckbeak broke into a grudging trot. They had reached the trees....
　　"Quick! Quick!" Carolina moaned, darting out from behind her tree, seizing the rope too and adding her weight to make Buckbeak move faster. Roberto looked over his shoulder; they were now blocked from sight; they couldn't see Villalba's garden at all.
　　"Stop!" he whispered to Carolina. "They might hear us
　　Villalba's back door had opened with a bang. Roberto, Carolina, and Buckbeak stood quite still; even the hippogriff seemed to be listening intently.
　　Silence... then --
　　"Where is it?" said the reedy voice of the Committee member. "Where is the beast?"
　　"It was tied here!" said the executioner furiously. I saw it! just here!"
　　"How extraordinary," said Dominguez. There was a note of amusement in his voice.
　　"Beaky!" said Villalba huskily.
　　There was a swishing noise, and the thud of an axe. The executioner seemed to have swung it into the fence in anger. And then came the howling, and this time they could hear Villalba's words through his sobs.
　　"Gone! Gone! Bless his little beak, he's gone! Musta pulled himself free! Beaky, yeh clever boy!"
　　Buckbeak started to strain against the rope, trying to get back to Villalba. Roberto and Carolina tightened their grip and dug their heels into the forest floor to stop him.
　　"Someone untied him!" the executioner was snarling. "We should search the grounds, the forest."
　　"Macnair, if Buckbeak has indeed been stolen, do you really think the thief will have led him away on foot?" said Dominguez, still sounding amused. "Search the skies, if you will.... Villalba, I could do with a cup of tea. Or a large brandy."
　　"O' -- o' course, Professor," said Villalba, who sounded weak with happiness. "Come in, come in...."
　　Roberto and Carolina listened closely. They heard footsteps, the soft cursing of the executioner, the snap of the door, and then silence once more.
　　"Now what?" whispered Roberto, looking around.
　　"We'll have to hide in here," said Carolina, who looked very shaken. "We need to wait until they've gone back to the castle. Then we wait until it's safe to fly Buckbeak up to Gustavo's window. He won't be there for another couple of hours.... Oh, this is going to be difficult...."
　　She looked nervously over her shoulder into the depths of the forest. The sun was setting now.
　　"We're going to have to move," said Roberto, thinking hard. "We've got to be able to see the Whomping Willow, or we won't know what's going on."
　　"Okay," said Carolina, getting a firmer grip on Buckbeak's rope. "But we've got to keep out of sight, Roberto, remember...."
　　They moved around the edge of the forest, darkness falling thickly around them, until they were hidden behind a clump of trees through which they could make out the Willow.
　　"There's Diego!" said Roberto suddenly.
　　A dark figure was sprinting across the lawn and its shout echoed through the still night air.
　　"Get away from him -- get away -- Scabbers, come here --"
　　And then they saw two more figures materialize out of nowhere. Roberto watched himself and Carolina chasing after Diego. Then he saw Diego dive.
　　"Gotcha! Get off, you stinking cat --"
　　"There's Gustavo!" said Roberto. The great shape of the dog had bounded out from the roots of the Willow. They saw him bowl Roberto over, then seize Diego....
　　"Looks even worse from here, doesn't it?" said Roberto, watching the dog pulling Diego into the roots. "Ouch -- look, I just got walloped by the tree -- and so did you -- this is weird--"
　　The Whomping Willow was creaking and lashing out with its lower branches; they could see themselves darting here and there, trying to reach the trunk. And then the tree froze.
　　"That was Crookshanks pressing the knot," said Carolina.
　　"And there we go..." Roberto muttered. "We're in."
　　The moment they disappeared, the tree began to move again. Seconds later, they heard footsteps quite close by. Dominguez, Macnair, Fudge, and the old Committee member were making their way up to the castle.
　　"Right after we'd gone down into the passage!" said Carolina. "If only Dominguez had come with us..."
　　"Macnair and Fudge would've come too," said Roberto bitterly. "I bet you anything Fudge would've told Macnair to murder Gustavo on the spot...."
　　They watched the four men climb the castle steps and disappear from view. For a few minutes the scene was deserted. Then --
　　"Here comes Cardozo!" said Roberto as they saw another figure sprinting down the stone steps and hating toward the Willow. Roberto looked up at the sky. Clouds were obscuring the moon completely.
　　They watched Cardozo seize a broken branch from the ground and prod the knot on the trunk. The tree stopped fighting, and Cardozo, too, disappeared into the gap in its roots.
　　"If he'd only grabbed the cloak," said Roberto. "It's just lying there...."
　　He turned to Carolina.
　　"If I just dashed out now and grabbed it, Peralta'd never be able to get it and --"
　　"Roberto, we mustn't be seen!"
　　"How can you stand this?" he asked Carolina fiercely. "Just standing here and watching it happen?" He hesitated. "I'm going to grab the cloak!"
　　"Roberto, no!"
　　Carolina seized the back of Roberto's robes not a moment too soon. just then, they heard a burst of song. It was Villalba, making his way up to the castle, singing at the top of his voice, and weaving slightly as he walked. A large bottle was swinging from his hands.
　　"See?" Carolina whispered. "See what would have happened? We've got to keep out of sight! No, Buckbeak!"
　　The hippogriff was making frantic attempts to get to Villalba again; Roberto seized his rope too, straining to hold Buckbeak back. They watched Villalba meander tipsily up to the castle. He was gone. Buckbeak stopped fighting to get away. His head drooped sadly.
　　Barely two minutes later, the castle doors flew open yet again, and Peralta came charging out of them, running toward the Willow.
　　Roberto's fists clenched as they watched Peralta skid to a halt next to the tree, looking around. He grabbed the cloak and held it up.
　　"Get your filthy hands off it," Roberto snarled under his breath. "Shh!"
　　Peralta seized the branch Cardozo had used to freeze the tree, prodded the knot, and vanished from view as he put on the cloak.
　　"So that's it," said Carolina quietly. "We're all down there... and now we've just got to wait until we come back up again...."
　　She took the end of Buckbeak's rope and tied it securely around the nearest tree, then sat down on the dry ground, arms around her knees.
　　"Roberto, there's something I don't understand.... Why didn't the dementors get Gustavo? I remember them coming, and then I think I passed out... there were so many of them...."
　　Roberto sat down too. He explained what he'd seen; how, as the nearest dementor had lowered its mouth to Roberto's, a large silver something had come galloping across the lake and forced the dementors to retreat.
　　Carolina's mouth was slightly open by the time Roberto had finished.
　　"But what was it?"
　　"There's only one thing it could have been, to make the dementors go," said Roberto. "A real Patronus. A powerful one."
　　"But who conjured it?"
　　Roberto didn't say anything. He was thinking back to the person he'd seen on the other bank of the lake. He knew who he thought it had been... but how could it have been?
　　"Didn't you see what they looked like?" said Carolina eagerly. "Was it one of the teachers?"
　　"No," said Roberto. "He wasn't a teacher."
　　"But it must have been a really powerful wizard, to drive all those dementors away... If the Patronus was shining so brightly, didn't it light him up? Couldn't you see --?"
　　"Yeah, I saw him," said Roberto slowly. "But... maybe I imagined it.... I wasn't thinking straight.... I passed out right afterward...."
　　"Who did you think it was?"
　　I think --" Roberto swallowed, knowing how strange this was going to sound. I think it was my dad."
　　Roberto glanced up at Carolina and saw that her mouth was fully open now. She was gazing at him with a mixture of alarm and pity.
　　"Roberto, your dad's -- well -- dead," she said quietly.
　　"I know that," said Roberto quickly.
　　"You think you saw his ghost?"
　　"I don't know... no... he looked solid...."
　　"But then --"
　　"Maybe I was seeing things," said Roberto. "But... from what I could see... it looked like him.... I've got photos of him...."
　　Carolina was still looking at him as though worried about his sanity.
　　I know it sounds crazy," said Roberto flatly. He turned to took at Buckbeak, who was digging his beak into the ground, apparently searching for worms. But he wasn't really watching Buckbeak.
　　He was thinking about his father and about his father's three oldest friends... Moony, Wormtail, Padfoot, and Prongs.... Had all four of them been out on the grounds tonight? Wormtail had reappeared this evening when everyone had thought he was dead.... Was it so impossible his father had done the same? Had he been seeing things across the take? The figure had been too far away to see distinctly... yet he had felt sure, for a moment, before he'd lost consciousness....
　　The leaves overhead rustled faintly in the breeze. The moon drifted in and out of sight behind the shifting clouds. Carolina sat with her face turned toward the Willow, waiting.
　　And then, at last, after over an hour...
　　"Here we come!" Carolina whispered.
　　She and Roberto got to their feet. Buckbeak raised his head. They saw Cardozo, Diego, and Salazar clambering awkwardly out of the hole in the roots. Then came Carolina... then the unconscious Peralta, drifting weirdly upward. Next came Roberto and Martinez. They all began to walk toward the castle.
　　Roberto's heart was starting to beat very fast. He glanced up at the sky. Any moment now, that cloud was going to move aside and show the moon....
　　"Roberto," Carolina muttered as though she knew exactly what he was thinking, "we've got to stay put. We mustn't be seen. There's nothing we can do...."
　　"So we're just going to let Salazar escape all over again.. said Roberto quietly.
　　"How do you expect to find a rat in the dark?" snapped Carolina. "There's nothing we can do! We came back to help Gustavo; we're not supposed to be doing anything else!"
　　"All right!"
　　The moon slid out from behind its cloud. They saw the tiny figures across the grounds stop. Then they saw movement --
　　"There goes Cardozo," Carolina whispered. "He's transforming
　　"Carolina!" said Roberto suddenly. "We've got to move!"
　　"We mustn't, I keep telling you --"
　　"Not to interfere! Cardozo's going to run into the forest, right at us!"
　　Carolina gasped.
　　"Quick!" she moaned, dashing to untie Buckbeak. "Quick! Where are we going to go? Where are we going to hide? The dementors wilt be coming any moment --"
　　"Back to Villalba's!" Roberto said. "It's empty now -- come on!"
　　They ran as fast as they could, Buckbeak cantering along behind them. They could hear the werewolf howling behind them....
　　The cabin was in sight; Roberto skidded to the door, wrenched it open, and Carolina and Buckbeak flashed past him; Roberto threw himself in after them and bolted the door. Fang the boarhound barked loudly.
　　"Shh, Fang, it's us!" said Carolina, hurrying over and scratching his ears to quieten him. "That was really close!" she said to Roberto.
　　"Yeah..."
　　Roberto was looking out of the window. It was much harder to see what was going on from here. Buckbeak seemed very happy to find himself back inside Villalba's house. He lay down in front of the fire, folded his wings contentedly, and seemed ready for a good nap.
　　"I think I'd better go outside again, you know," said Roberto slowly. "I can't see what's going on -- we won't know when it's time --"
　　Carolina looked up. Her expression was suspicious.
　　"I'm not going to try and interfere," said Roberto quickly. "But if we don't see what's going on, how're we going to know when it's time to rescue Gustavo?"
　　"Well... okay, then... I'll wait here with Buckbeak... but Roberto, be careful -- there's a werewolf out there -- and the dementors
　　Roberto stepped outside again and edged around the cabin. He could hear yelping in the distance. That meant the dementors were closing in on Gustavo.... He and Carolina would be running to him any moment....
　　Roberto stared out toward the lake, his heart doing a kind of drumroll in his chest.... Whoever had sent that Patronus would be appearing at any moment....
　　For a fraction of a second he stood, irresolute, in front of Villalba's door. You must not be seen. But he didn't want to be seen. He wanted to do the seeing.... He had to know...
　　And there were the dementors. They were emerging out of the darkness from every direction, gliding around the edges of the lake.... They were moving away from where Roberto stood, to the opposite bank.... He wouldn't have to get near them....
　　Roberto began to run. He had no thought in his head except his father... If it was him... if it really was him... he had to know, had to find out....
　　The lake was coming nearer and nearer, but there was no sign of anybody. On the opposite bank, he could see tiny glimmers of silver -- his own attempts at a Patronus --
　　There was a bush at the very edge of the water. Roberto threw himself behind it, peering desperately through the leaves. On the opposite bank, the glimmers of silver were suddenly extinguished. A terrified excitement shot through him -- any moment now --
　　"Come on!" he muttered, staring about. "Where are you? Dad, come on --"
　　But no one came. Roberto raised his head to look at the circle of dementors across the lake. One of them was lowering its hood. It was time for the rescuer to appear -- but no one was coming to help this time --
　　And then it hit him -- he understood. He hadn't seen his father -- he had seen himself --
　　Roberto flung himself out from behind the bush and pulled out his wand.
　　"EXPECTO PATDIEGOUM! "he yelled.
　　And out of the end of his wand burst, not a shapeless cloud of mist, but a blinding, dazzling, silver animal. He screwed up his eyes, trying to see what it was. It looked like a horse. It was galloping silently away from him, across the black surface of the lake. He saw it lower its head and charge at the swarming dementors.... Now it was galloping around and around the black shapes on the ground, and the dementors were falling back, scattering, retreating into the darkness.... They were gone.
　　The Patronus turned. It was cantering back toward Roberto across the still surface of the water. It wasn't a horse. It wasn't a unicorn, either. It was a stag. It was shining brightly as the moon above ... it was coming back to him....
　　It stopped on the bank. Its hooves made no mark on the soft ground as it stared at Roberto with its large, silver eyes. Slowly, it bowed its antlered head. And Roberto realized... "Prongs, "he whispered.
　　But as his trembling fingertips stretched toward the creature, it vanished.
　　Roberto stood there, hand still outstretched. Then, with a great leap of his heart, he heard hooves behind him -he whirled around and saw Carolina dashing toward him, dragging Buckbeak behind her.
　　"What did you do?" she said fiercely. "You said you were only going to keep a lookout!"
　　"I just saved all our lives...," said Roberto. "Get behind here -- behind this bush -- I'll explain."
　　Carolina listened to what had just happened with her mouth open yet again.
　　"Did anyone see you?"
　　"Yes, haven't you been listening? I saw me but I thought I was my dad! It's okay!"
　　"Roberto, I can't believe it.... You conjured up a Patronus that drove away all those dementors! That's very, very advanced magic. I knew I could do it this time," said Roberto, "because I'd already done it.... Does that make sense?"
　　"I don't know -- Roberto, look at Peralta!"
　　Together they peered around the bush at the other bank. Peralta had regained consciousness. He was conjuring stretchers and lifting the limp forms of Roberto, Carolina, and Martinez onto them. A fourth stretcher, no doubt bearing Diego, was already floating at his side. Then, wand held out in front of him, he moved them away toward the castle.
　　"Right, it's nearly time," said Carolina tensely, looking at her watch. "We've got about forty-five minutes until Dominguez locks the door to the hospital wing. We've got to rescue Gustavo and get back into the ward before anybody realizes we're missing.... 11
　　They waited, watching the moving clouds reflected in the lake, while the bush next to them whispered in the breeze. Buckbeak, bored, was ferreting for worms again.
　　"D' you reckon he's up there yet?" said Roberto, checking his watch. He looked up at the castle and began counting the windows to the right of the West Tower.
　　"Look!" Carolina whispered. "\Who's that? Someone's coming back out of the castle!"
　　Roberto stared through the darkness. The man was hurrying across the grounds, toward one of the entrances. Something shiny glinted in his belt.
　　"Macnair!" said Roberto. "The executioner! He's gone to get the dementors! This is it, Carolina --"
　　Carolina put her hands on Buckbeak's back and Roberto gave her a leg up. Then he placed his foot on one of the lower branches of the bush and climbed up in front of her. He pulled Buckbeak's rope back over his neck and tied it to the other side of his collar like reins.
　　"Ready?" he whispered to Carolina. "YotM better hold on to me --
　　He nudged Buckbeak's sides with his heels.
　　Buckbeak soared straight into the dark air. Roberto gripped his flanks with his knees, feeling the great wings rising powerfully beneath them. Carolina was holding Roberto very tight around the waist; he could hear her muttering, "Oh, no -- I don't like this oh, I really don't like this --"
　　Roberto urged Buckbeak forward. They were gliding quietly toward the upper floors of the castle.... Roberto pulled hard on the left-hand side of the rope, and Buckbeak turned. Roberto was trying to count the windows flashing past --
　　"Whoa!" he said, pulling backward as hard as he could.
　　Buckbeak slowed down and they found themselves at a stop, unless you counted the fact that they kept rising up and down several feet as the hippogriff beat his wings to remain airborne.
　　"He's there!" Roberto said, spotting Gustavo as they rose up beside the window. He reached out, and as Buckbeak's wings fell, was able to tap sharply on the glass.
　　Martinez looked up. Roberto saw his jaw drop. He leapt from his chair, hurried to the window and tried to open it, but it was locked.
　　"Stand back!" Carolina called to him, and she took out her wand, still gripping the back of Roberto's robes with her left hand.
　　"Alohomora!"
　　The window sprang open.
　　"How -- how --?" said Martinez weakly, staring at the hippogriff
　　"Get on -- there's not much time," said Roberto, gripping Buckbeak firmly on either side of his sleek neck to hold him steady. "You've got to get out of here -the dementors are coming -- Macnair's gone to get them."
　　Martinez placed a hand on either side of the window frame and heaved his head and shoulders out of it. It was very lucky he was so thin. In seconds, he had managed to fling one leg over Buckbeak's back and pull himself onto the hippogriff behind Carolina.
　　"Okay, Buckbeak, up!" said Roberto, shaking the rope. "Up to the tower -- come on.
　　The hippogriff gave one sweep of its mighty wings and they were soaring upward again, high as the top of the West Tower. Buckbeak landed with a clatter on the battlements, and Roberto and Carolina slid off him at once.
　　"Gustavo, you'd better go, quick," Roberto panted. "They'll reach Flitwick's office any moment, they'll find out you're gone."
　　Buckbeak pawed the ground, tossing his sharp head.
　　"What happened to the other boy? Diego?" croaked Gustavo.
　　"He's going to be okay. He's still out of it, but Madam Pomfrey says she'll be able to make him better. Quick -- go --"
　　But Martinez was still staring down at Roberto.
　　"How can I ever thank --"
　　"GO!" Roberto and Carolina shouted together.
　　Martinez wheeled Buckbeak around, facing the open sky.
　　"We'll see each other again," he said. "You are -- truly your father's son, Roberto...."
　　He squeezed Buckbeak's sides with his heels. Roberto and Carolina jumped back as the enormous wings rose once more.... The hippogriff took off into the air.... He and his rider became smaller and smaller as Roberto gazed after them... then a cloud drifted across the moon.... They were gone.
　　CHAPTER TWENTY-TWO
　　OWL POST AGAIN
　　Roberto!"
　　Carolina was tugging at his sleeve, staring at her watch. "We've got exactly ten minutes to get back down to the hospital wing without anybody seeing us -- before Dominguez locks the door --"
　　"Okay," said Roberto, wrenching his gaze from the sky, "let's go...."
　　They slipped through the doorway behind them and down a tightly spiraling stone staircase. As they reached the bottom of it, they heard voices. They flattened themselves against the wall and listened. It sounded like Fudge and Peralta. They were walking quickly along the corridor at the foot of the staircase.
　　"... only hope Dominguez's not going to make difficulties," Peralta was saying. "The Kiss will be performed immediately?"
　　"As soon as Macnair returns with the dementors. This whole Martinez affair has been highly embarrassing. I can't tell you how much I'm looking forward to informing the Daily Prophet that we've got him at last.... I daresay they'll want to interview you, Peralta... and once young Roberto's back in his right mind, I expect he'll want to tell the Prophet exactly how you saved him...."
　　Roberto clenched his teeth. He caught a glimpse of Peralta's smirk as he and Fudge passed Roberto and Carolina's hiding place. Their footsteps died away. Roberto and Carolina waited a few moments to make sure they'd really gone, then started to run in the opposite direction. Down one staircase, then another, along a new ,corridor -- then they heard a cackling ahead.
　　"Peeves!" Roberto muttered, grabbing Carolina's wrist. "In here!"
　　They tore into a deserted classroom to their left just in time. Peeves seemed to be bouncing along the corridor in boisterous good spirits, laughing his head off.
　　"Oh, he's horrible," whispered Carolina, her ear to the door. "I bet he's all excited because the dementors are going to finish off Gustavo...." She checked her watch. "Three minutes, Roberto!"

　　"Carolina -- what'll happen -- if we don't get back inside before Dominguez locks the door?" Roberto panted.
　　I don't want to think about it!" Carolina moaned, checking her watch again. "One minute!"
　　They had reached the end of the corridor with the hospital wing entrance. "Okay -- I can hear Dominguez," said Carolina tensely. "Come on, Roberto!"
　　They crept along the corridor. The door opened. Dominguez's back appeared.
　　"I am going to lock you in," they heard him saying. "it is five minutes to midnight. Miss Fernandez, three turns should do It. Good luck."
　　Dominguez backed out of the room, closed the door, and took out his wand to magically lock it. Panicking, Roberto and Carolina ran forward. Dominguez looked up, and a wide smile appeared under the long silver mustache. "Well?" he said quietly.
　　"We did it!" said Roberto breathlessly. "Gustavo has gone, on Buckbeak...."

　　"Well done. I think --" He listened intently for any sound within the hospital wing. "Yes, I think you've gone too -- get inside -- I'll lock you in --"
　　Roberto and Carolina slipped back inside the dormitory. It was empty except for Diego, who was still lying motionless in the end bed. As the lock clicked behind them, Roberto and Carolina crept back to their own beds, Carolina tucking the Time-Turner back under her robes. A moment later, Madam Pomfrey came striding back out of her office.
　　"Did I hear the headmaster leaving? Am I allowed to look after my patients now?"
　　She was in a very bad mood. Roberto and Carolina thought it best to accept their chocolate quietly. Madam Pomfrey stood over them, making sure they ate it. But Roberto could hardly swallow. He and Carolina were waiting, listening, their nerves jangling.... And then, as they both took a fourth piece of chocolate from Madam Pomfrey, they heard a distant roar of fury echoing from somewhere above them....
　　"What was that?" said Madam Pomfrey in alarm.
　　Now they could hear angry voices, growing louder and louder. Madam Pomfrey was staring at the door.

　　"Carlos -- be reasonable -- Roberto has been locked up --"
　　BAM.
　　The door of the hospital wing burst open.

　　"That will do, Carlos," said Dominguez quietly. "Think about what you are saying. This door has been locked since I left the ward ten minutes ago. Madam Pomfrey, have these students left their beds?"
　　"Of course not!" said Madam Pomfrey, bristling. "I would have heard them!"
　　"Well, there you have it, Carlos," said Dominguez calmly. "Unless you are suggesting that Roberto and Carolina are able to be in two places at once, I'm afraid I don't see any point in troubling them further."
　　Peralta stood there, seething, staring from Fudge, who looked thoroughly shocked at his behavior, to Dominguez, whose eyes were twinkling behind his glasses. Peralta whirled about, robes swishing behind him, and stormed out of the ward.
　　"Fellow seems quite unbalanced," said Fudge, staring after him. "I'd watch out for him if I were you, Dominguez."
　　"Oh, he's not unbalanced," said Dominguez quietly. "He's just suffered a severe disappointment."
　　"He's not the only one!" puffed Fudge. "The Daily Prophet's going to have a field day! We had Martinez cornered and he slipped through our fingers yet again! All it needs now is for the story of that hippogriff's escape to get out, and I'll be a laughingstock! Well... I'd better go and notify the Ministry.....
　　"And the dementors?" said Dominguez. "They'll be removed from the school, I trust?"
　　"Oh yes, they'll have to go," said Fudge, running his fingers
　　distractedly through his hair. "Never dreamed they'd attempt to administer the Kiss on an innocent boy... Completely out of control... no, I'll have them packed off back to Azkaban tonight.... Perhaps we should think about dragons at the school entrance...."
　　"Villalba would like that," said Dominguez, smiling at Roberto and Carolina. As he and Fudge left the dormitory, Madam Pomfrey hurried to the door and locked it again. Muttering angrily to herself, she headed back to her office.
　　There was a low moan from the other end of the ward. Diego had woken up. They could see him sitting up, rubbing his head, looking around.
　　"What -- what happened?" he groaned. "Roberto? Why are we in here? Where's Gustavo? Where's Cardozo? What's going on?"
　　Roberto and Carolina looked at each other.
　　"You explain," said Roberto, helping himself to some more chocolate.
　　When Roberto, Diego, and Carolina left the hospital wing at noon the next day, it was to find an almost deserted castle. The sweltering, heat and the end of the exams meant that everyone was taking full advantage of another Hogsmeade visit. Neither Diego nor Carolina felt like going, however, so they and Roberto wandered onto the grounds, still talking about the extraordinary events of the previous night and wondering where Gustavo and Buckbeak were now. Sitting near the lake, watching the giant squid waving its tentacles lazily above the water, Roberto lost the thread of the conversation as he looked across to the opposite bank. The stag had galloped toward him from there just last night....
　　A shadow fell across them and they looked 'tip to see a very bleary-eyed Villalba, mopping his sweaty face with one of his tablecloth-sized handkerchiefs and beaming down at them.
　　"Know I shouldn' feel happy, after wha' happened las' night," he said. "I mean, Martinez escapin' again, an, everythin' -- but guess what?"
　　"What?" they said, pretending to look curious.
　　"Beaky! He escaped! He's free! Bin celebratin' all night!"
　　"That's wonderful!" said Carolina, giving Diego a reproving look because he looked as though he was close to laughing.
　　"Yeah... can't've tied him up properly," said Villalba, gazing happily out over the grounds. "I was worried this mornin', mind... thought he mighta met Professor Cardozo on the grounds, but Cardozo says he never ate anythin' las' night...."
　　"What?" said Roberto quickly.
　　"Blimey, haven' yeh heard?" said Villalba, his smile fading a little. He lowered his voice, even though there was nobody in sight. "Er -- Peralta told all the Slytherins this mornin'.... Thought everyone'd know by now... Professor Cardozo's a werewolf, see. An' he was loose on the grounds las' night.... He's packin' now, o' course.
　　"He's packing?" said Roberto, alarmed. "Why?"
　　"Leavin', isn' he?" said Villalba, looking surprised that Roberto had to ask. "Resigned firs' thing this mornin'. Says he can't risk it happenin again.
　　Roberto scrambled to his feet.
　　"I'm going to see him," he said to Diego and Carolina.
　　"But if he's resigned --"
　　"-- doesn't sound like there's anything we can do --"
　　"I don't care. I still want to see him. I'll meet you back here."
　　Cardozo's office door was open. He had already packed most of his things. The grindylow's empty tank stood next to his battered old suitcase, which was open and nearly full. Cardozo was bending over something on his desk and looked up only when Roberto knocked on the door.
　　"I saw you coming," said Cardozo, smiling. He pointed to the parchment he had been poring over. It was the Marauder's Map.
　　"I just saw Villalba," said Roberto. "And he said you'd resigned. It's not true, is it?"
　　"I'm afraid it is," said Cardozo. He started opening his desk drawers and taking out the contents.
　　"Why?" said Roberto. "The Ministry of Magic don't think you were helping Gustavo, do they?"
　　Cardozo crossed to the door and closed it behind Roberto.
　　"No. Professor Dominguez managed to convince Fudge that I was trying to save your lives." He sighed. "That was the final straw for Carlos. I think the loss of the Order of Merlin hit him hard. So he -- er -- accidentally let slip that I am a werewolf this morning at breakfast."
　　"You're not leaving just because of that!" said Roberto.
　　Cardozo smiled wryly.
　　"This time tomorrow, the owls will start arriving from parents.... They will not want a werewolf teaching their children, Roberto. And after last night, I see their point. I could have bitten any of you.... That must never happen again."
　　"You're the best Defense Against the Dark Arts- teacher we've ever had!" said Roberto. "Don't go!"
　　Cardozo shook his head and didn't speak. He carried on emptying his drawers. Then, while Roberto was trying to think of a good argument to make him stay, Cardozo said, "From what the headmaster told me this morning, you saved a lot of lives last night, Roberto. if I'm proud of anything I've done this year, it's how much you've learned.... Tell me about your Patronus."
　　"How d'you know about that?" said Roberto, distracted.
　　"What else could have driven the dementors back?"
　　Roberto told Cardozo what had happened. When he'd finished, Cardozo was smiling again.
　　"Yes, your father was always a stag when he transformed," he said. "You guessed right... that's why we called him Prongs."
　　Cardozo threw his last few books into his case, closed the desk drawers, and turned to look at Roberto.
　　"Here -- I brought this from the Shrieking Shack last night," he said, handing Roberto back the Invisibility Cloak. "And..." He hesitated, then held out the Marauder's Map too. "I am no longer your teacher, so I don't feel guilty about giving you back this as well. It's no use to me, and I daresay you, Diego, and Carolina will find uses for it."
　　Roberto took the map and grinned.
　　"You told me Moony, Wormtail, Padfoot, and Prongs would've wanted to lure me out of school... you said they'd have thought it was funny."
　　"And so we would have," said Cardozo, now reaching down to close his case. "I have no hesitation in saying that Ricardo would have been highly disappointed if his son had never found any of the secret passages out of the castle."
　　There was a knock on the door. Roberto hastily stuffed the Marauder's Map and the Invisibility Cloak into his pocket.
　　It was Professor Dominguez. He didn't look surprised to see Roberto there.
　　"Your carriage is at the gates, Pedro," he said.
　　"Thank You, Headmaster."
　　Cardozo picked up his old suitcase and the empty grindylow tank.
　　"Well -- good-bye, Roberto," he said, smiling. "It has been a real pleasure teaching you. I feel sure we'll meet again sometime. Headmaster, there is no need to see me to the gates, I can manage...."
　　Roberto had the impression that Cardozo wanted to leave as quickly as possible.
　　"Good-bye, then, Pedro," said Dominguez soberly. Cardozo shifted the grindylow tank slightly so that he and Dominguez could shake hands. Then, with a final nod to Roberto and a swift smile, Cardozo left the office.
　　Roberto sat down in his vacated chair, staring glumly at the floor. He heard the door close and looked up. Dominguez was still there.
　　"Why so miserable, Roberto?" he said quietly. "You should be very proud of yourself after last night."
　　"It didn't make any difference," said Roberto bitterly. "Salazar got away."
　　"Didn't make any difference?" said Dominguez quietly, "It made all the difference in the world, Roberto. You helped uncover the truth. You saved an innocent man from a terrible fate."
　　Terrible. Something stirred in Roberto's memory. Greater and more terrible than ever before... Professor Trelawney's prediction!
　　"Professor Dominguez -- yesterday, when I was having my Divination exam, Professor Trelawney went very -- very strange."
　　"Indeed?" said Dominguez. "Er -- stranger than usual, you mean?"
　　"Yes... her voice went all deep and her eyes rolled and she said ... she said Salvador's servant was going to set out to return to him before midnight.... She said the servant would help him come back to power." Roberto stared up at Dominguez. "And then she sort of became normal again, and she couldn't remember anything she'd said. Was it -- was she making a real prediction?"
　　Dominguez looked mildly impressed.
　　"Do you know, Roberto, I think she might have been." he said thoughtfully. "Who'd have thought it? That brings her total of real predictions up to two. I should offer her a pay raise...."
　　"But --" Roberto looked at him, aghast. How could Dominguez take this so calmly?
　　"But -- I stopped Gustavo and Professor Cardozo from killing Salazar! That makes it my fault if Salvador comes back!"
　　"It does not," said Dominguez quietly. "Hasn't your experience with the Time-Turner taught you anything, Roberto? The consequences of our actions are always so complicated, so diverse, that predicting the future is a very difficult business indeed.... Professor Trelawney, bless her, is living proof of that.... You did a very noble thing, in saving Salazar's life."
　　"But if he helps Salvador back to power
　　"Salazar owes his life to you. You have sent Salvador a deputy who is in your debt.... When one wizard saves another wizard's life, it creates a certain bond between them... and I'm much mistaken if Salvador wants his servant in the debt of Roberto Gonzales."
　　"I don't want a connection with Salazar!" said Roberto. "He betrayed my parents!"
　　"This is magic at its deepest, its most impenetrable, Roberto. But trust me... the time may come when you will be very glad you saved Salazar's life."
　　Roberto couldn't imagine when that would be. Dominguez looked as though he knew what Roberto was thinking.
　　"I knew your father very well, both at Hogwarts and later, Roberto," he said gently. "He would have saved Salazar too, I am sure of it."
　　Roberto looked up at him. Dominguez wouldn't laugh -- he could tell Dominguez...
　　"I thought it was my dad who'd conjured my Patronus. I mean, when I saw myself across the lake ... I thought I was seeing him." "An easy mistake to make," said Dominguez softly. "I expect you'll tire of hearing it, but you do look extraordinarily like Ricardo. Except for the eyes... you have your mother's eyes.
　　Roberto shook his head.
　　"It was stupid, thinking it was him," he muttered. "I mean, I knew he was dead."
　　"You think the dead we loved ever truly leave us? You think that we don't recall them more clearly than ever in times of great trouble? Your father is alive in you, Roberto, and shows himself most plainly when you have need of him. How else could you produce that particular Patronus? Prongs rode again last night."
　　It took a moment for Roberto to realize what Dumblefore had said.
　　Last night Gustavo told me all about how they became Animagi," said Dominguez, smiling. "An extraordinary achievement -- not least, keeping it quiet from me. And then I remembered the most unusual form your Patronus took, when it charged Mr. Sosa down at your Quidditch match against Ravenclaw. You know, Roberto, in a way, you did see your father last night.... You found him inside yourself."
　　And Dominguez left the office, leaving Roberto to his very confused thoughts.
　　Nobody at Hogwarts now knew the truth of what had happened the night that Gustavo, Buckbeak, and Salazar had vanished except Roberto, Diego, Carolina, and Professor Dominguez. As the end of term approached, Roberto heard many different theories about what had really happened, but none of them came close to the truth.
　　Sosa was furious about Buckbeak. He was convinced that Villalba had found a way of smuggling the hippogriff to safety, and seemed outraged that he and his father had been outwitted by a gamekeeper. Miguel Lopez, meanwhile, had much to say on the subject of Gustavo's escape.
　　"If I manage to get into the Ministry, I'll have a lot of proposals to make about Magical Law Enforcement!" he told the only person who would listen -- his girlfriend, Penelope.
　　Though the weather was perfect, though the atmosphere was so
　　cheerful, though he knew they had achieved the near impossible in helping Gustavo to freedom, Roberto had never approached the end of a school year in worse spirits.
　　He certainly wasn't the only one who was sorry to see Professor Cardozo go. The whole of Roberto's Defense Against the Dark Arts class was miserable about his resignation.
　　"Wonder what they'll give us next year?" said Seamus Finnigan gloomily.
　　"Maybe a vampire," suggested Dean Thomas hopefully.
　　It wasn't only Professor Cardozo's departure that was weighing on Roberto's mind. He couldn't help thinking a lot about Professor Trelawney's prediction. He kept wondering where Salazar was now, whether he had sought sanctuary with Salvador yet. But the thing that was lowering Roberto's spirits most of all was the prospect of returning to the Carrizos. For maybe half an hour, a glorious half hour, he had believed he would be living with Gustavo from now on... his parents' best friend.... It would have been the next best thing to having his own father back. And while no news of Gustavo was definitely good news, because it meant he had successfully gone into hiding, Roberto couldn't help feeling miserable when he thought of the home he might have had, and the fact that it was now impossible.
　　The exam results came out on the last day of term. Roberto, Diego, and Carolina had passed every subject. Roberto was amazed that he had got through Potions. He had a shrewd suspicion that Dominguez might have stepped in to stop Peralta failing him on purpose. Peralta's behavior toward Roberto over the past week had been quite alarming. Roberto wouldn't have thought it possible that Peralta's dislike for him could increase, but it certainly had. A muscle twitched unpleasantly at the corner of Peralta's thin mouth every time he looked at Roberto, and he was constantly flexing his fingers, as though itching to place them around Roberto's throat.
　　Miguel had got his top-grade N.E.W.T.s; Pablo and Luis had scraped a handful of O.W.L.s each. Gryffindor House, meanwhile, largely thanks to their spectacular performance in the Quidditch Cup, had won the House championship for the third year running. This meant that the end of term feast took place amid decorations of scarlet and gold, and that the Gryffindor table was the noisiest of the lot, as everybody celebrated. Even Roberto managed to forget about the journey back to the Carrizos the next day as he ate, drank, talked, and laughed with the rest.
　　As the Hogwarts Express pulled out of the station the next mornIng, Carolina gave Roberto and Diego some surprising news.
　　"I went to see Professor Romero this morning, just before breakfast. I've decided to drop Muggle Studies."
　　"But you passed your exam with three hundred and twenty percent!" said Diego.
　　"I know," sighed Carolina, "but I can't stand another year like this one. That Time-Turner, it was driving me mad. I've handed it in. Without Muggle Studies and Divination, I'll be able to have a normal schedule again."
　　I still can't believe you didn't tell us about it," said Diego grumpily. "We're supposed to be your friends."
　　"I promised I wouldn't tell anyone," said Carolina severely. She looked around at Roberto, who was watching Hogwarts disappear from view behind a mountain. Two whole months before he'd see it again....
　　"Oh, cheer up, Roberto!" said Carolina sadly.
　　"I'm okay," said Roberto quickly. "Just thinking about the holidays."
　　"Yeah, I've been thinking about them too," said Diego. "Roberto, you've got to come and stay with us. I'll fix it up with Mum and Dad, then I'll call you. I know how to use a fellytone now --"
　　"A telephone, Diego," said Carolina. "Honestly, you should take Muggle Studies next year...."
　　Diego *ignored her.
　　"It's the Quidditch World Cup this summer! How about it, Roberto? Come and stay, and we'll go and see it! Dad can usually get tickets from work."
　　This proposal had the effect of cheering Roberto up a great deal.
　　"Yeah... I bet the Carrizos'd be pleased to let me come... especially after what I did to Aunt Marge...."
　　Feeling considerably more cheerful, Roberto joined Diego and Carolina in several games of Exploding Snap, and when the witch with the tea cart arrived, he bought himself a very large lunch, though nothing with chocolate in it.
　　But it was late in the afternoon before the thing that made him truly happy turned up....
　　"Roberto," said Carolina suddenly, peering over his shoulder. "What's that thing outside your window?"
　　Roberto turned to look outside. Something very small and gray was bobbing in and out of sight beyond the glass. He stood up for a better look and saw that it was a tiny owl, carrying a letter that was much too big for it. The owl was so small, in fact, that it kept tumbling over in the air, buffeted this way and that in the train's slipstream. Roberto quickly pulled down the window, stretched out his arm, and caught it. It felt like a very fluffy Snitch. He brought it carefully inside. The owl dropped its letter onto Roberto's seat and began zooming around their compartment, apparently very pleased with itself for accomplishing its task. Hedwig clicked her beak with a sort of dignified disapproval. Crookshanks sat up in his seat, following the owl with his great yellow eyes. Diego, noticing this, snatched the owl safely out of harm's way.
　　Roberto picked up the letter. It was addressed to him. He ripped open the letter, and shouted, "It's from Gustavo!"
　　"What?" said Diego and Carolina excitedly. "Read it aloud!"
　　Dear Roberto,
　　I hope this finds you before you reach your aunt and uncle. I don't know whether they're used to owl post.
　　Buckbeak and I are in hiding. I won't tell you where, in case this owl falls into the wrong hands. I have some doubt about his reliability, but he is the best I could find, and he did seem eager for the job.
　　I believe the dementors are still searching for me, but they haven't a hope of finding me here. I am planning to allow some Muggles to glimpse me soon, a long way from Hogwarts, so that the security on the castle will be lifted.
　　There is something I never got around to telling you during our brief meeting. It was I who sent you the Firebolt --
　　"Ha!" said Carolina triumphantly. "See! I told you it was from him!"
　　"Yes, but he hadn't jinxed it, had he?" said Diego. "Ouch!" The tiny owl, now hooting happily in his hand, had nibbled one of his fingers in what it seemed to think was an affectionate way.
　　Crookshanks took the order to the Owl Office for me. I used your name but told them to take the gold from my own Gringotts vault. Please consider it as thirteen birthdays' worth of presents from your godfather.
　　I would also like to apologize for the fright I think I gave you that night last year when you left your uncle's house. I had only hoped to get a glimpse of you before starting my journey north, but I think the sight of me alarmed you.
　　I am enclosing something else for you, which I think will make your next year at Hogwarts more enjoyable.
　　If ever you need me, send word. Your owl will find me.
　　I'll write again soon.
　　Gustavo
　　Roberto looked eagerly inside the envelope. There was another piece of parchment in there. He read it through quickly and felt suddenly as warm and contented as though he'd swallowed a bottle of hot butterbeer in one gulp.
　　I, Gustavo Martinez, Roberto Gonzales's godfather, hereby give him permission to visit Hogsmeade on weekends.
　　"That'll be good enough for Dominguez!" said Roberto happily. He looked back at Gustavo's letter. "Hang on, there's a RS...."
　　I thought your ftiend Diego might like to keep this owl, as it's my fault he no longer has a rat.
　　Diego's eyes widened. The minute owl was still hooting excitedly. "Keep him?" he said uncertainly. He looked closely at the owl for a moment; then, to Roberto's and Carolina's great surprise, he held him out for Crookshanks to sniff.
　　"What do you reckon?" Diego asked the cat. "Definitely an owl?"
　　Crookshanks purred.
　　"That's good enough for me," said Diego happily. "He's mine."
　　Roberto read and reread the letter from Gustavo all the way back into King's Cross station. It was still clutched tightly in his hand as he, Diego, and Carolina stepped back through the barrier of platform nine an(' three-quarters. Roberto spotted Uncle Francisco at once. He was standing a good distance from Mr. and Mrs. Lopez, eyeing them suspiciously, and when Mrs. Lopez hugged Roberto in greeting, his worst suspicions about them seemed confirmed.
　　"I'll call about the World Cup!" Diego yelled after Roberto as Roberto bid him and Carolina good-bye, then wheeled the trolley bearing his trunk and Hedwig's cage toward Uncle Francisco, who greeted him in his usual fashion.
　　"What's that?" he snarled, staring at the envelope Roberto was still clutching in his hand. "If it's another form for me to sign, you've got another ---"
　　"It's not," said Roberto cheerfully. "It's a letter from my godfather."
　　"Godfather?" sputtered Uncle Francisco. "You haven't got a godfather!"
　　"Yes, I have," said Roberto brightly. "He was my mum and dad's best friend. He's a convicted murderer, but he's broken out of wizard prison and he's on the run. He likes to keep in touch with me, though... keep up with my news... check if I'm happy..."
　　And, grinning broadly at the look of horror on Uncle Francisco's face, Roberto set off toward the station exit, Hedwig rattling along in front of him, for what looked like a much better summer than the last.
　　THE END
